1401 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Tucker v. Kittitas County


No. 20841-5-II, No. 21113-1-II (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 450



March 27, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1069.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 93-2-05496-9. Date filed: 06/21/96. Judge signing: Hon. Vicki L. Hogan.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's dismissal of Tuckers' tort claim reversed and trial court's denial of Tuckers' motion for mandamus affirmed. Matter remanded to trial court for trial and for reconsideration, in trial court's discretion, of order imposing terms against County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed a tort action against the defendant county. The Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) granted the county's motion for summary judgment. The property owners challenged the grant of summary judgment decision and the denial of their motion for mandamus. The county cross-appealed an order imposing the terms.


OVERVIEW: The property owners applied for a building permit to erect a sawmill storage building and a storage shed on the corner of its land. The county awarded the building permit. However, the property owners expanded his commercial sawmill operation beyond the scope of the building permit. The county charged the property owners with a criminal zoning code violation. After the county dropped the criminal charges, the property owners filed their tort action, alleging negligent issuance of the building permit, negligent and intentional non-enforcement of the zoning code, and negligent prosecution. However, the property owners did not file a notice of claim with the county before filing their lawsuit. The county denied the property owners' claim that the notice ordinance was unconstitutional, but did not plead as an affirmative defense any statute or local ordinance creating a notice of claim requirement. The court found no support for the conclusion that the property owners failed to file a claim with the county because the county failed to comply with the pleading requirements and that the county failed to argue its ordinance when it filed its motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's ruling on the mandamus and remanded the order for terms. However, the court reversed the trial court's decision granting summary judgment in favor of the county.

 

1402 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Reid


No. 15801-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 440



March 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 95-1-02445-0. Judgment or order under review. Date filed: 05/15/96. Judge signing: Hon. Paul A. Bastine.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington) that convicted appellant on two counts of first-degree theft, six counts of second-degree theft, and one count of forgery.


OVERVIEW: The lower court convicted appellant on various counts of first and second-degree theft and one count of forgery. The court affirmed because it found no merit in appellant's claims that her speedy trial rights were violated. The court found that appellant failed to follow the provisions of Wash Rev. Code § 9.98.010(1) because she did not cause to be delivered to the prosecuting attorney and the superior court a proper written notice of her incarceration in another county. The court also found the preliminary proceedings and trial on another charge were excludable from time computations. The court also found that the evidence disclosed facts which, if believed by the jury, supported the elements of each charge claimed to be in error by appellant so the evidence was sufficient to support the verdict for each count. The court also found appellant was not being imprisoned for nonpayment of debt because her debt was accumulated by color of aid or deception. The court also found she could not claim the verdicts were inconsistent and that the exceptional sentence she received was not in error. The court also affirmed because there was no prosecutorial misconduct in the closing argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that convicted appellant on two counts of first-degree theft, six counts of second-degree theft, and one count of forgery.

 

1403 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dozier


NO. 35368-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 413



March 23, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 768.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1062.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-01558-0. Date filed: 10/07/94. Judge signing: Hon. Brian D. Gain.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which sentenced defendant to life in prison under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (Act), Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030(23), (27), as a result of repeated convictions for second-degree robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction and sentence alleging both trial error as well as constitutional and procedural defects with the Act. The court found that the trial court was correct in permitting the manager's identification of defendant and defendant's cross examination of the manager as to the detective's statements as well as the physical events surrounding the manager's identification of the person running through the parking lot. Defendant's argument that the sergeant illegally seized the identification card failed because the scope of defendant's voluntary consent was not exceeded and the sergeant had a reasonable suspicion to investigate the identification card. Even if the permanent retention of the card was found to be an unlawful seizure, there were no fruits of the poisonous tree to suppress. The trial court's denial of discovery was proper because defendant did not overcome the threshold necessary to obtain the desired discovery. The state gave early notice that if convicted; defendant could have been found a persistent offender. The Act, as applied to defendant, did not constitute ex post facto punishment. According, the court affirmed the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which sentenced defendant to life in prison under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act.

 

1404 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 21345-1-II, consolidated # 21346-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 410



March 20, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1061.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pacific County. Docket No: 96-1-00129-3. Judgment or order under review. Date filed: 11/08/96. Judge signing: Hon. Joel M. Penoyar.



DISPOSITION: Reversed Count I, affirmed Count II, and remanded for resentencing and recalculation of restitution on Count II.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Superior Court for Pacific County, Washington, which convicted defendants of first degree theft by welfare fraud and fraudulent verification.


OVERVIEW: Defendant were accused of wrongfully receiving Aid to Families with Dependent Children on behalf of their minor children during periods when the children stayed with their paternal grandparents. Defendants were convicted of theft by welfare fraud and fraudulent verification. On appeal, defendants argued, among other things, that the trial court committed reversible error by instructing the jury on the crime of theft by welfare fraud as defined by Wash. Rev. Code § 74.08.331, when defendants were charged with committing theft as defined by Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.020. The court agreed and reversed defendant's theft by welfare fraud convictions. Defendants were charged in the indictment with committing the crime of theft, but that the jury was instructed on a different uncharged crime, welfare fraud. The jury convicted the defendants of a crime that was never charged. The court affirmed defendants' convictions for fraudulent verification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' theft convictions but affirmed defendants' fraudulent verification convictions. The court remanded the case for resentencing and recalculation of restitution.

 

1405 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hamby


No. 38236-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 397



March 16, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1057.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 96-2-07645-7. Date filed: 08/30/96. Judge signing: Hon. Glenna S. Hall.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a weapon under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a). Defendant alleged that the officer lacked probable cause to make an arrest and that the seriousness level of his crime was erroneously increased by an unconstitutionally-enacted initiative.


OVERVIEW: The officer responded to a tip. When the suspect saw that the apartment manager had seen him carrying a shotgun, he hid the gun and ran away. The officer observed an individual running who matched the description. Another officer conducted a search and determined that defendant was a convicted felon. The first officer found the shotgun. The trial court convicted defendant under the unlawful possession statute. The court affirmed. The apartment manager had previously reported suspicious arrests. His previous reports were credible and he was not involved in criminal activity. The court held that the relaxed veracity standard that applied to identified citizen informants was satisfied. The tip provided the officer with probable cause to believe that two crimes had been committed. Defendant was around the area where the gun was stashed. The court held this provided a reasonable basis to detain defendant. Since defendant's actions suggested he might be violent, the officer's drawing of his gun was proper. The duration of the stop was reasonable. The court held that the defendant's motion to suppress was properly denied. The court held that defendant showed no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant by the trial court.

 

1406 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burke


No. 37724-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


90 Wn. App. 378; 952 P.2d 619; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 398



March 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 1, 1998, Reported at: 136 Wn.2d 1018, 966 P.2d 1277, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 736.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of first degree burglary pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.020 as amended by Initiative 159, the Hard Time for Armed Crime Act.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction. On review, the court affirmed and held that Initiative 159, § 9's armed with a deadly weapon provision did not violate the single subject rule of Wash. Const. art II, § 19 of the Washington Constitution. Initiative 159, § 9 expanded the first degree burglary statute to include armed burglaries of nonresidential buildings and this fell squarely within Initiative 159's legislative title's single subject of increasing penalties for armed crime. Therefore, defendant's first degree burglary conviction did not result from "logrolling." Also, the jury's special verdict finding that defendant was not actually armed during the burglary was not irreconcilable with its general verdict finding him guilty of first degree burglary.The jury found that his accomplice was armed. To convict defendant of first degree burglary, the jury had to find that in so entering or while in the building or in immediate flight from the building defendant or an accomplice was armed with a deadly weapon.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree burglary.

 

1407 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Department of Licensing


No. 16236-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


90 Wn. App. 370; 952 P.2d 197; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 378



March 10, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted September 2, 1998, Reported at: 136 Wn.2d 1001, 966 P.2d 901, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 699.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, Department of Licensing, challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Grant County (Washington) that enjoined it from suspending the driver's license of respondent juvenile in the juvenile's action seeking a declaratory judgment and an order enjoining the Department from suspending his license. The Department suspended the juvenile's license pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.265 after he pled guilty to possession of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: The Department contended that it was error to determine that Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.265 applied only to persons younger than 18. The court reversed the judgment and dissolved the injunction, explaining that § 46.20.265 unambiguously required the Department to revoke the driving privileges of "a juvenile" when it received notice from a court of certain criminal violations. The court acknowledged certain provisions of § 46.20.265 were not consistent with each other because their applicability depended upon different definitions for "a juvenile" but opined that the legislative intent to apply the license-revocation scheme for drug violators up to age 21 rather than up to age 18 was clear. The court found no violation of the equal protection guaranties of the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution or Wash. Const. art. 1, § 12, noting that the statutory classification was not wholly arbitrary because it was rationally related to the legitimate state objectives of promoting highway safety and deterring drug use. The court concluded that it was an error to find that the revocation provision of § 46.20.265 did not apply to drug offenders over the age of 18.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment declaring that the Department did not have the authority to suspend the juvenile's license and dissolved the injunction preventing the Department from suspending the juvenile's license.

 

1408 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


In re Detention of Clewley


No. 20253-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 354



March 6, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied June 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 409.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 93-2-02802-0. Date filed: 11/27/95. Judge signing: Hon. Vicki L. Hogan.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which granted the State's petition to have him committed as a sexually violent predator under the Sexually Violent Predator Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. Defendant argued that he did not have a speedy trial and that his commitment violated guarantees of equal protection and substantive due process and prohibitions against double jeopardy and ex post facto laws.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a long history of sexually violent felonies. The State sought to have him committed under the Act. Defendant was detained but was not brought to trial within the 45 days, as the Act formerly required. Defendant's attorney filed a motion to dismiss, which the trial court denied, concluding that defendant had waived his rights to a speedy trial. Defendant was ordered committed and on his appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant had been denied a speedy trial because it was the State's obligation to bring him before the trial court and defendant had not asked for a continuance or stated that he would waive his right to a speedy trial. However, the violation of the right to a speedy trial did not required vacation of defendant's commitment as a remedy because he provided no argument that the delay affected the outcome of his trial. Each of defendant's constitutional challenges to the Act, including substantive due process, equal protection, double jeopardy, and ex post facto violations, had been ruled meritless by the Washington Supreme Court in another case, as well as by the United States Supreme Court in a case challenging a similar Kansas statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's commitment under the Act.

 

1409 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 16318-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 328



March 3, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Ferry County. Docket No: 91-1-00027-1. Date filed: 12/11/96. Judge signing: Hon. Larry M. Kristianson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Superior Court of Ferry County (Washington), which denied defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea or to modify the sentence imposed by his plea to second degree murder.


OVERVIEW: When defendant entered a guilty plea to second degree murder, the trial court informed defendant that community placement was mandatory for his crime. Five years later, defendant filed a motion to withdraw his guilty plea or to modify his sentence, arguing that his guilty plea was not entered intelligently or voluntarily because he was not informed that community placement was a direct consequence of his plea. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that: (1) a defect in defendant's outdated plea form, which did not contain a provision required by Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 4.2(g), was remedied by the trial court's careful determination of the mandatory community placement term and discussion with defendant and counsel of the consequences; (2) the trial court and the State gave defendant extensive information on the two years of mandatory community placement and allowed him two recesses to discuss the consequence before the guilty plea was entered; and (3) defendant's appeal almost five years after sentencing was untimely pursuant to Wash. Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b)(1) and Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea or to modify his sentence.

 

1410 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


King County v. Cent. Puget Sound Bd.


No. 39333-2-I, No. 39914-4-I, No. 40310-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


91 Wn. App. 1; 951 P.2d 1151; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 344



March 2, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals August 6, 1998.]


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County (Washington) held that appellee Central Puget Sound Growth Management Board's (board) decision ordering appellee county to include certain acres within its urban growth area was consistent with the Growth Management Act, Wash Rev. Code § 36.70 et seq. Appellant environmental organization challenged the decision.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted a countywide planning policy under the Growth Management Act. The county submitted the plan to the board. The board ordered the county to include certain acres of land in its urban growth area. The county initiated an action against the board challenging the inclusion order. The trial court found that the inclusion order was proper and consistent with the Act. The environmental organization challenged the decision contending that the inclusion order was merely suggestive, rather than directive, and the environmental impact statement was inadequate. On appeal, the court upheld the trial court's decision. The inclusion order expressly directed the county to include the areas in the urban growth area. The inclusion order was only subject to one interpretation and expressly required the county to include the acres. The court found that the environmental impact statement was adequate because it informed the county of the environmental consequences of the plan and allowed the county to make reasonable decisions regarding its implementation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

1411 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davido


Nos. 35377-2-I, 36924-5-I, 37670-5-I (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 305



March 2, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 771.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1036.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 93-1-05332-7. Date filed: 09/12/94. Judge signing: Hon. Patricia H. Aitken.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of King County (Washington) convicting defendant of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver and imposing an exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: After a lengthy passport fraud investigation, federal agents found that defendant had rented an apartment under a false identity. Local police served an arrest warrant and saw numerous suspicious documents in plain view after a protective sweep of defendant's apartment. The federal agents used these observations to seek and obtain a search warrant for documents and driver's licenses under one of defendant's aliases. While executing the search warrant, the agents opened an ice chest and found cocaine. They also read the numerous documents in the apartment and seized evidence of a large mail order cocaine distribution scheme. The court held that: (1) the agents had legitimately performed the protective sweep and read the documents; (2) because the area inspected immediately adjoined the place of arrest, the agents need not have justified their actions by establishing a concern for safety as an incident to the arrest; (3) the plain view doctrine was an exception to the Fourth Amendment requirement that search warrants particularly describe the items to have been seized; and (4) the agents were entitled to have searched anything inside the apartment that could have contained the items.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and the exceptional sentence from the trial court.

 

1412 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nero


No. 35786-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 310



March 2, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1036.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-04637-0. Date filed: 12/09/94. Judge signing: Hon. James A. Noe Jr.



DISPOSITION: Nero's conviction and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which, following a jury trial, convicted him of delivering cocaine within a school zone.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold cocaine to an undercover police officer inside a tavern that was located within 1,000 feet of a school. Defendant argued that the sentencing enhancement statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(a), violated due process and equal protection when the drug sale occurred in a tavern because children could not be there. On appeal, the court rejected his arguments, holding that the "school zone" statute sufficiently defined the prohibited conduct to include drug deliveries that occurred in taverns. Due process did not require offenders to know they were dealing drugs inside a drug-free zone, and the school zone enhancement was a strict liability statute. Moreover, the legislative interest underlying the statute, to keep drug dealers away from schoolchildren, was a legitimate one. The court held that the objective was rationally related to punishing drug dealers more harshly when they did business in taverns in drug-free zones. In order to enter a tavern that was located within 1,000 feet of a school, a drug seller had to pass through areas in which school children were likely to be present. This increased the likelihood that children would be exposed to the drug culture.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for delivering cocaine within a school zone.

 

1413 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ronquillo


NO. 35840-5-I, NO. 35875-8-I (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 334



March 2, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitions for Review Denied October 1, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 747.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1037.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-02988-2. Date filed: 12/20/94. Judge signing: Hon. Larry Jordan.
State v. Ronquillo, 89 Wn. App. 1037, 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 2480 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, principal and accomplice, appealed the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington). The trial court convicted the principal of first degree murder, two counts of attempted first degree murder, and assault in the second degree. The trial court convicted the accomplice of murder in the second degree, two counts of attempted murder in the second degree, and assault in the second degree on the basis of accomplice liability.


OVERVIEW: The principal and the accomplice were convicted on murder charges arising out of a drive-by shooting which killed the victim. The principal and the accomplice appealed, and the court affirmed the convictions. The court concluded that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by declining juvenile court jurisdiction, rejecting a motion for mistrial due to alleged improper comments on the principal's right to remain silent, and refusing repeated motions to sever. The court rejected the principal's argument that the jury instructions impermissibly broadened the charge against him. The court affirmed the trial court's decision to admit expert testimony on gangs and its decision to strike a portion of the gang expert testimony elicited by the principal on cross-examination. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion either by admitting the impeaching evidence or allowing it to be proved by extrinsic evidence. The court determined that sufficient evidence was presented to support the accomplice's conviction and that the trial court's response to jury inquiries regarding the intent element of accomplice liability did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the principal's convictions for first degree murder, two counts of attempted first degree murder, and assault in the second degree. The court affirmed the accomplice's convictions for murder in the second degree, two counts of attempted murder in the second degree, and assault in the second degree on the basis of accomplice liability.

 

1414 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Manufactured Housing v. State


No. 21705-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


90 Wn. App. 257; 951 P.2d 1142; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 300



February 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted December 4, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 935.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff park owners' group appealed from the orders of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which denied its motion for summary judgment on the question of whether the Mobile Home Parks--Resident Ownership Act (the Act), Wash. Rev. Code § 59.23, allowed a taking of property without just compensation in violation of Wash. Const. art. I, § 16 and the Fifth Amendment. The trial court dismissed the facial challenge.


OVERVIEW: The Act allowed tenants of mobile home parks to form associations and to receive a statutory right of first refusal in the event that a mobile home park owner wished to sell his mobile home park. On appeal, the court first considered whether Wash. Const. art. I, § 16 provided greater protection than the Fifth Amendment and looked at six nonexclusive factors: (1) the textual language of the state constitutional provision; (2) differences in the parallel texts of the federal and state constitutions;(3) state constitutional and common law history; (4) preexisting state law; (5) structural differences between the federal and state constitutions; and (6) whether the clause dealt with matters of particular state or local concern. The court held that the state and federal provisions were coextensive. The court examined the Act and found that no real property estate or interest was taken because a right of first refusal was a personal contract right under state law. The court found that the Act was a de minimis intrusion on the owners' rights, advanced a legitimate state interest in preserving housing, and did not deny the owners all economically viable use of their lands.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court that the law that gave mobile home tenants a right of first refusal was not a taking that violated either the state or federal constitutions.

 

1415 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Hendrix v. Waters


No. 38526-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


89 Wn. App. 921; 951 P.2d 317; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 249



February 17, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the order of the Superior Court of King County (Illinois), which conditioned his visitation rights to his son upon the father's ceasing his use of marijuana, in the action of appellee, State of Washington (state), on behalf of the son, to determine the parentage, visitation, and child support of the son.


OVERVIEW: The state initiated the underlying action to determine the parentage, visitation, and child support of the son of the father and mother. At trial, the father testified that he regularly used marijuana as a part of his Rastafarian religious practices. The trial court granted visitation to the mother and conditioned the father's visitation upon his ceasing his use of marijuana. On the father's appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order and held that it did not violate the father's First Amendment Right to free exercise of his religion because neutral, generally applicable laws could be applied to religious practices even when they were not supported by a compelling governmental interest. The trial court's order conditioning the father's visitation rights on ceasing illegal activity was not unreasonable or untenable. The court summarily dismissed the father's other challenges to the trial court's order for his failure to support the challenges with a cogent argument. The court declined to award costs to the state because the father's appeal was not frivolous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court, which conditioned the father's visitation of the son on the father's ceasing his use of marijuana.

 

1416 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Staples


No. 37855-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 205



February 9, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-1-06323-0. Date filed: 12/18/95. Judge signing: Hon. Richard M. Ishikawa.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a firearm. Defendant argued that police unlawfully seized him when they shined a spotlight on him. Defendant also challenged the constitutionality of underlying sentencing provisions.


OVERVIEW: The officer received a call about a man carrying a gun. The officer saw defendant, who matched the description of the suspect, and was carrying a revolver. The officer stepped out of his patrol car and shined a spotlight directly on defendant. Defendant got rid of the gun and ran from the police. The police found defendant and the gun. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence of the gun. On appeal, the court upheld the denial of defendant's motion to suppress evidence of the gun and affirmed his conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm. The court held that defendant failed to preserve his argument that the act of shining the spotlight on him was an unconstitutional seizure in the trial court. Regardless, the court held that defendant failed to prove that a seizure occurred because by running from the officer, defendant did not submit to the show of authority as required to establish a seizure. The court held that the penalty enhancement provisions, which increased the seriousness level of defendant's crime and resulted in a longer sentence, was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence of the gun and affirmed his conviction for unlawful possession of a firearm.

 

1417 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Vallan v. Miyahara


No. 21228-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


90 Wn. App. 324; 950 P.2d 532; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 188



February 6, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, citizens and Board of Denture Technology (board), sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which awarded judgment in favor of respondents, Secretary and Washington State Department of Health, and dismissed appellants' challenges to Substitute Senate Bills 5308, Laws of 1995, ch. 198 (SSB 5308), and 5365, Laws of 1995, ch. 336 (SSB 5365) as violative of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19.


OVERVIEW: Appellants asserted that SSB 5308 and SSB 5365 violated the single subject and title specificity provisions of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19. They noted that when the voters passed Initiative 607, which allowed persons other than dentists to make and sell dentures, they created the board to regulate that activity. Appellants argued that SSB 5308 and SSB 5365 improperly included provisions transferring regulatory authority over denturists to the secretary without giving adequate notice to the public in the bills' titles. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that §§ 18-25 of SSB 5308 were unconstitutional since the bill's title was restrictive and mentioned only the use of examinations in credentialing health professionals. The court stated that since §§ 18-25 dealt with other subjects outside of the scope of the title but could be severed from the rest of the bill, it would only strike down §§ 18-25. The court found that the title of SSB 5365 was general in that it related to "the uniform disciplinary act" and that all its sections fit within the scope of the title. Thus, the court held that SSB 5365 did not violate Wash. Const. art II, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's decision that awarded judgment to respondents and dismissed appellants' constitutional challenge to SSB 5365, but reversed the portion of the decision that dismissed appellants' constitutional challenge to §§ 18-25 of SSB 5308; the court ruled that §§ 18-25 of SSB 5308 were unconstitutional as outside the scope of the title of SSB 5308.

 

1418 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Association to Protect Anderson Creek v. City of Bremerton


No. 20878-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 166



February 6, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 89 Wn. App. 1009.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 95-2-02790-5. Date filed: 06/03/96. Judge signing: Hon. Frederick B. Hayes.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant environmental group challenged a grant of summary judgment to respondents, city and buyers, by the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), in an action by the environmental group seeking to have the city's sale of land to the buyers declared invalid.


OVERVIEW: The city sold undeveloped property to the buyers under a negotiated sale agreement, in which the city administration agreed to apply for and support a rezone of the property by the city council. The environmental group sued to have the sale declared invalid and the trial court granted summary judgment to respondents. The court affirmed. The court held that the environmental group did not have standing to challenge the sale because its members were not taxpayers or residents of the city and they could not show any specific harm caused by the sale. The court considered the merits of the environmental group's claims to determine whether the appeal was frivolous. Because the city determined that the land was surplus to the city's needs and that the negotiated sale created benefits to the city outweighing an open bid process, there were no violations of law. The sale was not a loan of public money. The negotiated sale was not ultra vires because the city did not promise to rezone the land. Accordingly, the court found that the appeal was frivolous and awarded a nominal sum for reasonable attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to respondents in the environmental group's action seeking to have the city's sale of land to the buyers declared invalid.

State v. Johnson


No. 19714-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


90 Wn. App. 54; 950 P.2d 981; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 169



February 6, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Johnson, 122 Wn. App. 1050, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2476 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) of being a felon in possession of a firearm, first degree assault, and second degree murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant signed an omnibus order indicating that his defense was general. He later revealed that he would rely on an alibi defense. The trial court ruled that the State could use the self-defense claim to impeach defendant and his witnesses. The court reversed and remanded. It held that the jury could have reached a different outcome absent the trial court's errors. It was error to admit defendant's prior rape conviction. Defendant's proffered stipulation would have proved that he was a felon, and the unfair prejudice was significant. Defendant's statement on the omnibus order was not admissible to impeach his witnesses. It was error to deny defendant permission to impeach the State's witness because defendant's questions went to both the witness's prior inconsistency and his bias. The State should not have been able to cross-examine a witness about her prior conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for being a felon in possession of a firearm, first degree assault, and second degree murder was reversed and remanded for a new trial because erroneous rulings denied him a fair trial.

State v. Fuller

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 138



February 2, 1998, Filed

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for robbery in the Superior Court of King County (Washington). Defendant argued that the trial court erred by not dismissing his case for violation of his speedy trial rights and prosecutorial mismanagement, that there were errors in the admission of exhibits and in his sentencing, and that the prosecutor committed misconduct in closing argument.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and two friends robbed a victim by enticing the victim to a hotel room, after which defendant and one of the friends beat the victim until he was unconscious. The victim positively identified defendant and his friends, and all three were tried together. Defendant was convicted of robbery, and the jury found him to be a persistent offender. The trial court was within its discretion to grant the continuance that did not violate defendant's speedy trial rights. Any reference to defendant's decision to remain silent at trial was tangential at most, so the trial court correctly denied defendant's motion for mistrial. Defendant's sentence was not disproportionate or cruel under Wash. Const. art. I, § 14 and did not violate the Sentencing Reform Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for robbery and his sentence as a persistent offender to life without the possibility of parole.

State v. Stephenson


No. 20059-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


89 Wn. App. 794; 950 P.2d 38; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 126

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of intimidating a public servant, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.180. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of § 9A.76.180, contending that the statute was overbroad because it criminalized a substantial amount of constitutionally protected speech or conduct. The court rejected defendant's argument, and affirmed his conviction. While the court found that defendant's speech was entitled to some First Amendment protection, it determined that the state had a compelling interest in maintaining the integrity of government action and that the statute was narrowly tailored to achieve that purpose. The court further concluded that the statute was reasonable in light of its purpose. The court rejected defendant's contention that the judges, who were the subject of defendant's speech, were not "public servants" under § 9A.76.180. The court found sufficient evidence that the targeted judges were public servants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for two counts of intimidating a public servant.

State v. Lintz


No. 34485-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 54



January 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions in the Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington) of two counts of vehicular homicide committed by driving while under the influence after a jury trial. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the "two hour" rule under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502 was unconstitutionally vague, and that omission of the "implied" element in the "to convict" jury instructions was reversible error.

OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court entered on a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of two counts of vehicular homicide. Based upon an error in a jury instruction, the court remanded the case for a new trial.

 

1423 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Gilliam v. DSHS


NO. 35689-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


89 Wn. App. 569; 950 P.2d 20; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 62



January 26, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1998, Reported at: 135 Wn.2d 1015, 960 P.2d 937, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 536.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which directed a verdict in favor of respondent State of Washington Department of Social and Health Services, Child Protective Services (CPS) on the grounds that a CPS social worker had absolute immunity from liability for negligence in conducting an investigation into allegations made by the father's children that he had sexually abused them.


OVERVIEW: The children's parents were divorced and custody granted to the mother. Thereafter the mother reported to CPS that the children claimed their father had sexually abused them. CPS's case worker initiated an investigation that was never resolved, although eventually it appeared that respondents, mother and her new husband, had influenced the children to make the allegations and that the new husband may have been the one abusing the children. In the father's tort action, the trial court directed a verdict for CPS on the grounds of absolute immunity. On appeal the court reversed, finding that absolute immunity was available only to functions that were intimately associated with the judicial phase of a proceeding, and finding further that the case worker's function was primarily investigatory. The court held that the state was not immune to a claim alleging negligence in an investigation. The court affirmed the dismissal of the cause of action for negligent supervision, finding that such claim was redundant inasmuch as the state had acknowledged that the case worker was acting within the scope of her employment and that the state would be vicariously liable for her conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the directed verdict in favor of CPS, finding that its case worker did not have absolute immunity because her function was primarily investigatory rather than intimately associated with a judicial proceeding. The court held that the state was not immune to the father's claim alleging negligent investigation into allegations that the father sexually abused his children.

Longview Fibre Co. v. Ecology


No. 20926-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


89 Wn. App. 627; 949 P.2d 851; 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 36



January 23, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington) reversed, on the ground that Wash. Admin. Code § 173-405-040(10) was unconstitutionally vague, a board ruling that had upheld appellant state agency's imposition of a fine on respondent corporation for failing to maintain pollution control equipment at a pulp mill. The state agency appealed.


OVERVIEW: The state agency's inspection had discovered large holes in the mill's scrubber system that emitted steam and spray into the air and created large quantities of mud. The corporation claimed that the requirement that it operate and maintain its scrubber system consistently with "good air pollution control practices" was unconstitutionally vague. The state agency contended that § 173-405-040(10) was necessarily general because it had to apply to a variety of facilities, each with its own unique processes and equipment. The court determined that § 173-405-040(10) was not unconstitutionally vague. The court stated that the corporation had fair notice that its failure to follow operation and maintenance procedures, in conjunction with its continued operation of damaged air pollution control equipment, could subject it to civil sanctions. The court noted that compliance with emissions limits was relevant but not dispositive. The court concluded that the trial court erred in finding § 173-405-040(10) unconstitutionally vague, and further concluded that the board did not err in fining the corporation for violating the regulation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court and remanded.

State v. Binford


No. 20637-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 38



January 23, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 599.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 95-1-04812-1. Date filed: 04/11/96. Judge signing: Hon. Arthur W. Verharen III.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which was entered on a verdict convicting him of first degree armed robbery, attempting to elude a pursuing police vehicle, three counts of first degree assault with a deadly weapon, and taking a motor vehicle without permission and which sentenced him to a life sentence under the three strikes law.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for his involvement in a bank robbery. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding no error in the prosecutor's comments on defendant's failure to testify because they were in response to defense counsel's assertion that defendant told the truth during a polygraph test. The court ruled that defendant was properly sentenced as a persistent offender because his discharged conviction could be used for sentencing in later offenses, and his convictions were proven by a preponderance of the evidence. The court found no prosecutorial misconduct in an alleged accomplice declining to testify and invoking his Fifth Amendment right to remain silent after the State informed him that federal authorities were also considering filing charges. The court ruled that the information was properly amended because defendant failed to show that the amendment added new facts to the case of which defendant had no notice such as prejudiced his substantial rights. The court concluded that the three strikes law was constitutional and was not ex post facto because it enhanced the penalty for the last crime committed and did not impose additional punishment for a prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of first degree armed robbery, attempting to elude a pursuing police vehicle, three counts of first degree assault with a deadly weapon, and taking a motor vehicle without permission and sentenced him to life in prison under the three strikes law.

City of Richland v. Michel

January 22, 1998, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:

OVERVIEW:  Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055 provided that a person who was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI) and who had a prior offense, which included deferred prosecutions, within the last five years had to be given a higher minimum punishment than a person who had no prior offenses. The driver was arrested for DUI on September 13, 1995 and he had been granted a deferred prosecution for a similar charge in April 1992. The individual contended that § 46.61.5055 was unconstitutional. The court stated that the driver's contention that his deferred prosecution agreement did not give him fair notice that an enhanced sentence was a consequence of his agreement was without merit because the deferred prosecution statute did not require written notice of all consequences of the agreement. The court held that the state had a legitimate, substantial interest in preventing people from threatening life and property by habitually drinking and driving and the statute was a valid exercise of police power and it was reasonably related to accomplishing its purpose. The court upheld the constitutionality of the statute and the driver's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment of conviction and sentence were affirmed. The constitutionality of the statute was also upheld.

State v. Sapp


No. 16155-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2120



December 23, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1064.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Douglas County. Docket No: 96-1-00054-3. Date filed: 10/01/96. Judge signing: Hon. Ted W. Small Jr.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Douglas County (Washington), convicting him of escape from community custody, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 72.09.310, and sentencing him to 90 days based on an offender score of one point imposed under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.360(18) (now Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.360(17)).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of a felony drug offense, obtained early release to community custody, and subsequently violated the conditions of community placement. Defendant argued that the community custody escape statute was unconstitutionally vague, his incriminating statements in the administrative hearing, which revoked his community placement, were inadmissible at the criminal trial, and the revocation of early release was punishment that precluded his escape prosecution on double jeopardy grounds. The appellate court ruled that defendant's vagueness claim was without merit and his statements from the administrative proceeding were admissible. Arguably the testimony of defendant's caseworker regarding his incriminating statements were more prejudicial than probative, however, the trial court had wide discretion in making such determinations, and an erroneous evidence ruling did not require reversal, unless it was of constitutional magnitude and materially affected the outcome. Furthermore, the criminal prosecution did not constitute double jeopardy, as returning defendant to jail for violating the terms of his conditional release was punishment for the original crime.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

1432 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hartke


No. 15931-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


89 Wn. App. 143; 948 P.2d 402; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2064



December 18, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, pleaded guilty in the Chelan County Superior Court (Washington) to five counts of second degree burglary, one count of first degree theft, and one count of third degree malicious mischief. The court ordered defendant to pay restitution and subsequently extended the time period it retained jurisdiction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, pursuant to an amendment to Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.190, extended the date to collect restitution for 10 years beyond the date of the disposition. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by extending jurisdiction to collect restitution beyond the date he turned 21, as that imposed an ex post facto punishment. The court of appeals disagreed. The purpose of juvenile restitution was to compensate the victim and impose accountability on the juvenile. Restitution primarily served the goal of rehabilitation. Because restitution was not punitive, the ex post facto doctrine was not implicated. The fact that a sanction, including imprisonment, might later have been imposed for willfully violating a restitution order did not change the remedial nature of the restitution. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1433 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Detention of R.P.


No. 39532-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


89 Wn. App. 212; 948 P.2d 856; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2089



December 18, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which dismissed the State's petition to commit appellee patient for 180 days.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the trial court erred by dismissing its petition, because Wash. Rev. Code § 71.05 did not require supporting affidavits for 180-day petitions. The court of appeals disagreed. While the statute did not set out the procedural requirements for a 180-day petition, it did state that the hearing was the same as that for a 90-day petition. The legislature assured patients' due process rights for each duration of commitment. As the length of detention increased, the statute provided additional procedural rights. Therefore, it was unlikely that the legislature intended to exclude the notice provision for patients who faced the longest period of commitment. The legislature intended all of the procedural requirements for the 90-day petition to apply in a 180-day petition. There was no support in law or logic for lessening the rights of a patient who faced a longer commitment. Therefore, the trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Norris v. Department of Retirement Sys.


No. 20849-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2049



December 12, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitions for Review Denied September 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 682.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1052.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 93-2-02639-8. Date filed: 06/04/96. Judge signing: Hon. Christine A. Pomeroy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, teachers, appealed the judgment of the Thurston County Superior Court (Washington), which upheld the ruling of appellee Washington Department of Retirement Systems that the teachers' excess pay could not be included in pension benefit calculations, as it was neither earnable compensation, nor excess compensation.


OVERVIEW: The teachers argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by upholding the Department's finding that earnable compensation did not include retirement incentive payments. The court of appeals disagreed. Substantial evidence supported the Department's finding. The director testified that, upon learning that excess payments for retirement incentives were included by the colleges in earnable compensation, the Department did not categorize such pay as compensation for rendering services. That interpretation and practice, he further testified, was also based upon advice from the Washington Attorney General's Office that those types of retirement incentive payments could not be included for purposes of calculating pension benefits. The department's finding was also supported by the testimony of an auditor, who stated that she understood that the department consistently excluded payment above and beyond normal rates from earnable compensation. Accordingly, the trial court did not commit error by affirming the department's finding.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1435 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stackhouse


No. 14957-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FIVE


88 Wn. App. 963; 947 P.2d 777; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1991



December 4, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pend Oreille County. Docket No: 95-1-00003-0. Date filed: 05/24/95. Judge signing: Hon. Larry M. Kristianson.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a 17-year-old with no criminal history when the offense was committed, was convicted of first degree murder by the Superior Court, Pend Oreille County (Washington). He appealed, contending the court erred by denying his request for a declination hearing in juvenile court and that Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.030 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a friend, burglarizing a residence, heard a vehicle pull into the driveway, and exited. The homeowner confronted them and they both shot at him. Defendant's shot missed, but the other's shot hit and killed the homeowner. They were arrested and defendant was charged as an adult with first degree murder. The trial court denied his motion for a declination hearing, and rejected the argument that Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.030 as amended was unconstitutional. It denied his motion to dismiss for violation of his right to a speedy trial and he was found guilty of first degree murder and sentenced to 280 months' imprisonment. On appeal, he contended the trial court erred by denying his motion for a decline hearing and maintained Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.110 mandated a declination hearing for juvenile defendants, unless waived. He pointed to a conflict with the automatic decline provisions of Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.030. The conflict between Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.110 and Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.030 was resolved by applying rules of statutory construction supporting the validity of the automatic decline provisions of Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Spokane Arcade v. City of Spokane


No. 15679-6-III, No. 15680-0-III, (Consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1989



December 4, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1034.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 95-2-02795-9. Date filed: 03/26/96. Judge signing: Hon. Neal Q. Rielly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult entertainment establishments sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which upheld the constitutionality of Spokane, Wash., Mun. Code § 10.08 in a suit against appellees, city and hearing officer. The ordinance prohibited licensing of adult arcades owned by those previously convicted of certain crimes and regulated peep show operations.


OVERVIEW: The adult entertainment establishments were denied licenses to operate adult arcades because they failed to comply with open booth and other requirements contained in § 10.08 and one of them had been convicted of interstate transport of obscenity, which disqualified it from licensing under Spokane, Wash. Mun. Code § 10.08.118(8)(b). On appeal, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part, finding first that the restrictive provisions of the ordinance were constitutional. The court reasoned that the ordinance was content neutral, aimed at protecting the public health, safety, and welfare, was narrowly tailored to promote a substantial governmental interest, did not affect the content of the peep shows, or restrict the number of booths in an establishment. Thus, the court held that the restrictions passed muster under the First Amendment and Wash. Const. art. I, § 5. However, the court determined that the provision disqualifying applicants from licensing based on previous criminal convictions was an unconstitutional prior restraint since an applicant's past convictions did not necessarily reflect on his qualifications to operate an adult entertainment business.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that part of the trial court's order that held that the ordinance provisions regulating the adult entertainment establishments' peep show operations were constitutional. The court reversed that part of the order which held constitutional the ordinance provision disqualifying those with convictions for certain criminal convictions from obtaining licenses to operate adult arcades within the city.

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which entered summary judgment in favor of respondent city in the property owner's action challenging the city's ordinance that established a downtown parking and business improvement area and imposed assessments against commercial property owners.

State v. Davis


No. 21002-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1927



November 21, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied June 3, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 461. Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1025.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 96-1-00310-1. Date filed: 07/26/96. Judge signing: Hon. Richard A. Strophy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), convicting him of one count of unlawful possession of a firearm in the first degree, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a), and four counts of possession of a stolen firearm, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.310.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a) was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence underlying the unlawful possession of a firearm was insufficient to support his conviction on that count. The appellate court ruled that the statute was not void for vagueness and that the evidence was sufficient to support the count. Based on the evidence, a rational trier could have found that defendant possessed and controlled the backpack, including the gun found therein, and that he had previously been convicted of second degree burglary. Also, defendant failed to establish he received ineffective assistance of counsel, as some of defendant's witnesses were accomplices, and defense counsel may have reasonably believed that the jury instruction, which would have told the jury to view the testimony of accomplices with caution, would disadvantage the defense. Furthermore, the bailiff did not think that the jury actually observed defendant handcuffed, and the trial court so found. Even if a juror caught a glimpse, there was nothing to suggest that the sight inflamed or prejudiced the jury to such an extent that a fair trial was not possible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Smith v. Spokane County


No. 16486-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


89 Wn. App. 340; 948 P.2d 1301; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1913



November 18, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Publication Status of this Document has been Changed by the Court from Unpublished to Published December 30, 1997. As Amended December 30, 1997. Petition for Review Denied June 3, 1998, Reported at: 135 Wn.2d 1007, 959 P.2d 125, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 455. Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1024.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant water and sewer services customer challenged the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, city and county, in the class action case arising from fees imposed on water and sewer services customers to fund an aquifer protection area, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 36.26.040.


OVERVIEW: Appellant water and sewer services customer brought the class action proceeding to challenge fees imposed for the aquifer protection area, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 36.26.040. The water and sewer services customer challenged the superior court's grant of summary judgment in favor of respondents, city and county. The court held that the charges were fees, not taxes, based on the regulatory purposes for the program, the allocation of amounts generated for those regulatory purposes, and the direct relationship between the fees and the services received by the payors and the burden on the payors. The sewer construction contemplated under the program served the regulatory purpose of preventing pollution and continued degradation of the aquifer. The court then rejected the water and sewer services customer's claims based on the assumption that the charges were taxes, and held that the fees did not violate the Due Process Clause or the Equal Protection Clause. Further, the fees for the aquifer protection area did not constitute unlawful special assessments or the deprivation of property under the Takings Clause. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of respondents, city and county, in the class action case brought by appellant water and sewer services customer contesting fees imposed for support of the aquifer protection area.

State v. Fonville


No. 38627-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1861



November 10, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied June 3, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 443. Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1018.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 81-1-00680-3. Date filed: 04/16/96. Judge signing: Hon. Thomas J. Wynne.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court for Snohomish County, Washington, that convicted him of one count of first-degree statutory rape and one count of indecent liberties.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's statutory rape conviction arose from allegations of multiple acts. He generally denied all but one of the acts. The indecent liberties conviction arose from the one act that defendant specifically denied. On appeal, the court reversed the statutory rape conviction and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the trial court committed a manifest constitutional error affecting defendant's right to a unanimous jury error by not electing one of the multiple acts to support the single statutory rape count and by not giving a Petrich instruction. The error was not harmless because there was evidence as to the one act that could have justified a reasonable doubt in a juror's mind. Regarding the indecent liberties' conviction, the court held that none of the alleged instances of prosecutorial misconduct, individually or cumulatively, warranted a reversal. The trial court's admitting into evidence one of two relevant photos was not unduly prejudicial. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in issuing a warrant to search defendant's property bin at a jail for items containing his alias name because the alias information was contained on a booking sheet property form.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the trial court's judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant of first-degree statutory rape. The court remanded for a new trial on that charge. Otherwise, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Semakula


NO. 39730-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


88 Wn. App. 719; 946 P.2d 795; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1866



November 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1998, Reported at: 134 Wn.2d 1022, 958 P.2d 317, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 375.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a firearm, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a) (1996) and sentenced him to 21 months of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: In 1990, defendant, then a juvenile, was adjudicated guilty of burglary in the second degree. At the time, the unlawful possession of a firearm statute made no reference to juvenile offenders. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1) (1989) (amended 1992). In 1992, this statute was amended to include juvenile adjudications as predicate offenses. In 1994, the legislature amended the statute again and enacted Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.047, which required notification at the time of conviction of ineligibility to possess a firearm. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.047(1)(a). In 1996, defendant was charged with one count of unlawful possession of a firearm in the first degree, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a) (amended 1996). Defendant was convicted of the charge and sentenced to 21 months. Defendant appealed the judgment and argued that plaintiff state was required to prove his guilty knowledge. The court affirmed the judgment and held that defendant's conviction was proper because knowledge of the illegality of possession of a firearm was not an element to the crime of unlawful possession of a firearm, according to legal precedent and legislative history.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a firearm and sentenced him to 21 months of imprisonment.

 

1443 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chambers


No. 20464-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


88 Wn. App. 640; 945 P.2d 1172; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1859



November 7, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Washington (state) sought review of decision from the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which granted defendant's motion to suppress marijuana that police obtained pursuant to a search warrant, declaring the search warrant was insufficiently particular because it did not identify marijuana as the item to be seized. Rather, it allowed police to search for "any and all controlled substances."


OVERVIEW: The state challenged the trial court's order granting defendant's motion to suppress marijuana that police had obtained pursuant to a search warrant. The trial court declared the search warrant was insufficiently particular because it did not identify marijuana as the item to be seized but instead allowed police to search for "any and all controlled substances." Upon appeal, the court reversed, holding that all that was required was reasonable particularity under these circumstances. The court stated that the officers were authorized to inspect virtually every aspect of the premises, and if during their search they discovered another illegal substance, the nonspecified substance would be subject to seizure under the plain view doctrine. The court stated that the officers executing the warrant at hand had no broader discretion to search than they would have had if the warrant had specified "marijuana." The court held that the fact the warrant could have been more precise in terms of identifying marijuana as the focus of the search did not affect its validity, since reasonable particularity was all that was required.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded, concluding that the warrant satisfied fourth amendment particularity requirements. The court reversed the trial court's ruling granting defendant's motion to suppress the marijuana and dismissing the charge against him and remanded for trial.

In re L.L.


No. 20483-5-II, consolidated with, No. 20484-3-II, No. 20485-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1815



October 31, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 347.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1009.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No: 94-7-00100-1. Date filed: 02/02/96. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth D. Williams.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the judgment of the Clallam County Superior Court (Washington) that terminated her parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by terminating her parental rights because the State had not proved that termination was in the children's best interests. The court of appeals disagreed. Each of the children suffered from post-traumatic stress disorder. An expert testified that they were highly scarred, and needed to be part of long term, stable, and nurturing families. A doctor testified that the children's development and integration would be severely hampered if they were allowed to stay with their mother, and that continued contact with the mother would have exacerbated the children's feelings of trauma due to the long term, repeated abuse they had suffered. A social worker testified that the mother was not responding to services and had shown an inability to change. She testified that termination was in the best interests of the children. Therefore, the State proved that termination of the mother's parental rights was in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
