State v. Robbins


No. 14579-4-III, No. 14580-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1799



October 28, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Granted May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 306.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Docket No: 94-2-00170-3. Date filed: 12/05/94. Judge signing: Hon. John G. Burchard Jr.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the judgments of a Superior Court (Washington), which convicted them in separate jury trials of driving under the influence in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502.


OVERVIEW: Defendant A was arrested for driving under the influence as he parked his car. Defendant A claimed that he was not feeling the effects of the alcohol he had consumed when he drove the car, but that he was feeling the effects when he took a breathalyzer test an hour later. Defendant B was arrested for driving under the influence after being stopped for speeding. Both defendants challenged their convictions based on § 46.61.502. The court affirmed defendant A's conviction but reversed and remanded as to defendant B's conviction. The court held that while the statute as a whole was constitutional, the affirmative defense set forth in § 46.61.501(3) required defendants to disprove a necessary element of the crime in violation of due process protections. As the jury was not given the § 46.61.501(3) instruction in defendant A's case and the state met is burden, his conviction should stand. However, in defendant B's case, the process was defective because the jury was given the incorrect instruction relating to the affirmative defense, and thus a new trial was warranted. Double jeopardy did not bar defendant B's retrial, and the other errors asserted by defendants were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant A, but reversed defendant B's conviction and remanded for a new trial.

State v. Anderson


No. 36412-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1795



October 27, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 377.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 88 Wn. App. 1004.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-05565-4. Date filed: 03/28/95.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the King County Superior Court (Washington) of two counts of first-degree robbery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by admitting his confession because it was not voluntary. The court of appeals disagreed. The critical question was whether a promise was made. Defendant's credibility was central to that issue and was resolved against him, as was a detective's credibility. The court of appeals deferred to those determinations, noting that they were circumstantially supported by the fact that defendant had the opportunity to record the alleged promise but did not do so, and by defendant's statement that he knew that he had just admitted to the crime. There was thus substantial evidence supporting the finding that no promise was made by police. The lack of a promise was fatal to defendant's claim that his confession was involuntary. Therefore, the trial court did not err by admitting the confession.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Initiative 172 v. Fair Ass'n


No. 20254-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


88 Wn. App. 579; 945 P.2d 761; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1785



October 24, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant activists challenged an order of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which held in the activists' action for an injunction against respondent fair operator that the fair operator could restrict the activists' activity to a "free speech area" and that they were entitled to be present throughout the entire duration of the fair.


OVERVIEW: The trial court determined, in the activists' action against the fair operator for injunctive relief, that the fair operator could restrict the activists' efforts to collect signatures to the fair's "free speech area" and that the activists could collect signatures each day that the fair was open. The court affirmed that judgment on appeal. The court held that because the fair took place on the fair operator's private property, the activists had no right to violate or to unreasonably restrict the fair operator's right to provide a safe and uncongested atmosphere where fairgoers could freely walk the fairgrounds and independently choose to visit a specific booth, exhibit, or display. The court also concluded that the activists did not show that restricting their solicitation to the "free speech area" caused the substantial injury that was required for issuing an injunction against that restriction. The court further opined that the fair was not a public forum because the fair operators did not have any direct ties to any governmental organization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment, in the activists' action for injunctive relief against the fair association, that held that the fair association could restrict the activists' efforts to collect signatures to the fairs' "free speech area" and that the activists had the right to solicit signatures for the fair's entire duration.

City of Seattle v. Norby


No. 37074-0-I, No. 40467-9-I, Consolidated Cases


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


88 Wn. App. 545; 945 P.2d 269; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1805



October 20, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted them by a jury trial of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed their convictions. The court reversed defendants' conviction and affirmed one defendant's conviction to the extent that his complaint was constitutional. The court found that a logically and legally required, albeit implied, element of the offense described in Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502 was that an amount of alcohol sufficient to cause a measurement of breath or blood of one defendant to register 0.10 percent or greater within two hours of driving was present in the defendant's system while he was driving. The court found that the implied element mitigated the appellate court's concern that the statute criminalized behavior not generally deemed criminal. Because the appellate court's construction of the DWI statute operated as if it were originally written into it, the "implied element" was deemed to have been a required element for both convictions. The court held that failure to instruct on an element of an offense was automatic reversible error. The court also found that the complaints gave defendants notice of the elements of the charge against them and it was constitutionally sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' conviction of driving while intoxicated and found that the trial court committed reversible error when it omitted the implied element in the jury instructions. The court affirmed the one defendant's conviction to the extent that it found the criminal complaint constitutionally sufficient.

Mauser v. City of Edmonds


NO. 38072-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1772

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant factory filed an action against appellee city and pollution control authority for intentional and negligent interference with business expectations and business relations. OVERVIEW: Certain citizens filed complaints against the factory for fumes that it emitted. The pollution control authority (PCA) issued notice of fines and penalties against the factory. The factory applied for a permit to construct pollution control equipment and the city denied the permit. The factory filed an action against the city and the PCA for intentional and negligent interference with business expectations and business relations. The court also rejected the factory's claim that there was a civil conspiracy because the factory failed point out the facts that would establish that claim.

In re Det. of Begay


No. 13899-2-III, No. 14243-4-III, (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1712



October 14, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 307.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Franklin County. Docket No: 93-2-50075-3. Date filed: 02/08/94. Judge signing: Hon. Duane E. Taber.
In re Det. of Begay, 87 Wn. App. 1101, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3612 (1997).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant detainee sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court for Franklin County, Washington, which committed detainee for treatment as a sexually violent predator pursuant to the Community Protection Act of 1990, Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09 in an action brought by respondent State of Washington.


OVERVIEW: Detainee was convicted of second-degree rape and sentenced to prison. Shortly before he was scheduled to be released, the State filed a petition for commitment and a motion for determination of probable cause to find detainee a sexually violent predator. Detainee moved to dismiss the petition, contending that the Community Protection Act ("Act") was unconstitutional. The court denied his motion. The jury found detainee was a sexually violent predator and the court ordered him committed. Detainee contended that the Act violated his right to due process by denying an adversarial hearing on the probable cause determination, and by failing to require treatment in the least restrictive environment. On appeal, the court held that due process required that detainee be allowed to appear in person to contest probable cause. However, detainee failed to show any prejudice resulting from denial of an adversarial hearing. The commitment proceeding, which was civil in nature, as with commitment of the criminally insane, was dealing with a most imprecise area of human behavior and attempting to predict future conduct for a particular individual. The trial court committed no error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1451 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lightle


No. 15871-3-III, No. 15872-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL EIGHT


88 Wn. App. 470; 944 P.2d 1114; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1739



October 14, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged an order from the Superior Court of Benton County, Washington, which dismissed the Wash. Rev. Code § 27.53.060(1) charges against defendants because the statute was unconstitutional. The statute prohibited removing archeological objects from any archeological resource or site.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were engaged in digging for and gathering arrowheads, items specifically mentioned in the definition of archeological resources per Wash. Rev. Code § 27.53.040. Defendants argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 27.53.060(1) was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The trial court agreed, found the statute unconstitutional, and dismissed the criminal charges of removing archeological objects from any archeological resource or site. The court reversed and remanded, holding that § 27.53.060(1) was not unconstitutional. The court reasoned that while the term "of archeological interest" in Wash. Rev. Code § 27.53.060(1) might involve a subjective judgment, the judgment would be that of an archeologist, not a law enforcement officer. Wash. Rev. Code § 27.53.040, which defined "archeological resource," adequately notified defendants of what objects and sites were prohibited from excavation. The court concluded that in determining whether a statute defined the prohibited conduct with sufficient specificity, the court considered whether the terms used were so vague that persons of common intelligence must necessarily guess at its meaning.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for new trial.

 

1452 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mulholland


NO. 36926-1


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1733



October 13, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 95-1-00525-4. Date filed: 06/30/95. Judge signing: Hon. Joseph Thibodeau.
State v. Mulholland, 87 Wn. App. 1095, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3593 (1997).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, which convicted him of second degree assault for stabbing another person in the left buttock.


OVERVIEW: The trial court denied defendant's request to impeach the victim with a telephone tape recording made in violation of the Washington Privacy Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.73. On appeal, defendant alleged that the trial court's suppression of the recorded telephone conversation violated his constitutional rights to confront witnesses and put on a defense. Upon review, the court found that the trial court properly suppressed the recording because defendant failed to make a sufficient offer of proof. Without a record of the tape's contents, the court was unable to review the trial court's ruling for error. While provisions of the Washington Privacy Act could have been overcome given sufficient constitutional justification, the instant matter was not such a case. The excluded tape was not the sole evidence impeaching the victim, and there was additional evidence implicating defendant as the stabber. Defendant's interest in impeaching the victim with cumulative evidence did not outweigh the State's compelling interest in protecting personal privacy by suppressing surreptitious recordings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1453 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Torres


No. 15151-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1674



October 7, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 337.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Benton County. Docket No: 95-1-00104-5. Date filed: 09/01/95. Judge signing: Hon. Carolyn A. Brown.
State v. Torres, 87 Wn. App. 1089, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3573 (1997).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Benton County, Washington, convicting her of possession with intent to deliver one kilogram of cocaine and imposing an exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: When the officer arrested defendant, the officer read her Miranda rights in Spanish, and defendant confirmed she understood her rights. Defendant argued her waiver of Miranda was not knowing and intelligent, as the officer spoke Texas-accented Spanish and misused the complex Spanish word "ocupar." The appellate court ruled that the record supported the determination that the translation adequately conveyed the information that indigence was not a barrier to legal representation, and the record contained substantial evidence that defendant was given the opportunity to clear up any confusion she might have had and that she claimed she understood her rights. The appellate court ruled that there was no support for defendant's claim her representation was deficient, as the record showed her counsel negotiated a generous plea offer, which counsel effectively communicated with an unequivocal recommendation she accept the offer. Furthermore, the appellate court did not address defendant's contention that the sentencing reform act's designation of quantity of drugs as an aggravating circumstance was unconstitutionally vague for lack of clear guidelines for uniform sentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed.

 

1454 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Parsons


No. 36617-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1641



September 29, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Skagit County. Docket No: 94-1-00317-7. Date filed: 05/05/95. Judge signing: Hon. George E. McIntosh.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Superior Court of Skagit County, Washington, which ordered him to pay restitution after he was convicted of theft.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of theft and sentenced him on May 5, 1995. The State sought restitution. On July 23, 1995, Wash. Rev. Code Ann. § 9.94A.142 was amended to change the restitution hearing time period from 60 days to 180 days after sentencing. Defendant sought a restitution hearing, but the State did not seek a hearing until November 1, 1995. Defendant asked for a continuance, which the trial court granted until November 9, 1995. The trial court stayed the restitution hearing until the court could determine defendant's restitution appeal. The court remanded the case to the trial court for further restitution proceedings, holding that because defendant committed an offense after July 1, 1985, Wash. Rev. Code Ann. § 9.94A.142 applied to his case. The amendment provided that the 180-day limit had retroactive effect if three conditions were met: (1) The court failed to set restitution within 60 days of sentencing as previously required; (2) the defendant was sentenced after July 23, 1994; and (3) the defendant was not unfairly prejudiced by the delay. The court concluded that the trial court complied with amended § 9.94A.142.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case to the trial court to hold the restitution proceeding and determine restitution.

State v. Sang Anh Chuong


No. 20239-5-II, No. 20234-4-II, No. 20315-4-II, No. 20283-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1623



September 26, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Sang Anh Chuong, 966 P.2d 903, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 281 (Wash., 1998)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 95-1-01658-8. Date filed: 12/18/95. Judge signing: Hon. Thomas L. Lodge.
State v. Chuong, 87 Wn. App. 1075, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2204 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Four co-defendants were convicted and sentenced for first degree kidnapping and robbery, burglary, first and third degree possession of stolen property in the first degree, by the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington). They appealed.


OVERVIEW: Four males broke into a couple's home. The couple was sleeping. They were held at gunpoint and restrained. Defendants took many items of property. The Hard Time for Armed Crime Act (the Act), 1995 Wash. Laws 129, did not violate Wash. Const. art. II, § 19. The imposition of firearm enhancements, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.310(3), on defendants' first-degree robbery and burglary convictions did not violate double jeopardy principles. Defendants' convictions for first-degree robbery did not merge with first degree kidnapping. The trial court did not err in refusing to give defendants' kidnapping instruction, which would have required the State to prove the victims were moved. The statute did not require movement of the victims. The trial court's instructions properly stated the law. The trial court did not err by failing to suppress testimony about the victims' identification of the defendants in a showup; it was not overly coercive and met the threshold test for reliability and was admissible. The trial court did not err by rejecting defendants' motion to sever or by ordering the firearm enhancements to run consecutively.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed, except that it reversed and remanded for resentencing solely as to the defendant who was merely a passenger in a stolen vehicle driven by his co-defendant.

 

1456 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wright


No. 37876-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


88 Wn. App. 683; 946 P.2d 792; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1564



September 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
 Reported at State v. Wright, 87 Wn. App. 1068, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3529 (1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of unlawfully possessing a firearm while having previously been convicted of a serious offense, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.010(1)(1) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Responding to reports of gun shots, police officers found defendant, a 19-year old, walking down the street with a friend. Defendant was holding a box of ammunition, and his friend had a .44-caliber handgun. Defendant admitted that he had fired about four shots. Plaintiff state charged him with unlawfully possessing a firearm while having previously been convicted of a serious offense. At the age of 16, defendant had been adjudicated guilty in juvenile court of second degree robbery and second degree assault. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the charge for failure to state a claim, arguing that he was not "convicted" of a "serious offense" within the meaning of § 9.41.010(1)(1) (1994), because his offenses were adjudicated in juvenile court. The trial court denied his motion and found him guilty of the offense. The court affirmed the judgment, by holding that although the statute deleted the reference to juvenile adjudications, if such adjudications did not constitute predicate offenses, the statute would be superfluous because juveniles could never violate it even though it contained language that either an adult or juvenile could be guilty.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted defendant of unlawfully possessing a firearm while having previously been convicted of a serious offense.

 

1457 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


In re Detention of Haga


No. 21373-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


87 Wn. App. 937; 943 P.2d 395; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1522



September 12, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review denied at 134 Wn.2d 1015 (1998).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, which committed him under Washington's Sexually Violent Predator Statute pursuant to the State's motion before defendant was released from prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant suffered previous convictions for several violent rapes against adolescent girls and young women. Before he was released from prison, the State moved to have him committed under the Washington's Sexually Violent Predator Statute (SVPS). At the SVPS trial, the State called defendant's victims, several experts, and defendant. Defendant stated that he wanted to testify; however, the trial court, after consulting with defense counsel, refused to let defendant testify on his own behalf although he had testified when the State called him. The trial court committed. On appeal, the court held that when defendant insisted that he wanted to testify, the trial court erred when it deprived him of that opportunity. The court reasoned that it had held that the right to testify was absolute and could not be abrogated by defense counsel. Although a SVPS commitment proceeding was civil in nature, Wash. Rev. Code Ann. § 71.09.060(2) expressly provided that all constitutional rights available to defendants at criminal trials, other than the right not to be tried while incompetent, applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded with instructions to allow defendant to testify on his own behalf.

 

1458 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Spokane v. Ismail


No. 15534-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1507



September 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 95-1-01113-7. Date filed: 01/19/96. Judge signing: Hon. Kenneth H. Kato.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court for Spokane County, Washington, which convicted defendant pursuant to Spokane, Wash., Municipal Code § 10.06.020 (1996) of lewd conduct after he urinated in the dark entryway of a closed bus depot.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the trial court erred by denying his motion for a directed verdict in which he claimed that the City failed to establish that the act was intentional and that it occurred in a public place. On appeal, the court held that the trial court properly denied the motion. The court found that § 10.06.020(A) defined urination in a place other than a toilet or public restroom as a lewd act. The court found that it was irrelevant that the act was not witnessed by anyone. Moreover, the court found that the City proved that defendant's act was intentional. Defendant also argued that § 10.06.020 was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to define "public place." The court held that § 10.06.020 could be reasonably understood to forbid urinating in an entryway on a public street. Defendant also argued that § 10.06.020 was unconstitutional because it embraced five types of conduct that were considered lewd acts. The court held that § 10.06.020 was constitutional because there was a rational unity between the subject matter and the title. The proscribed acts were rationally related because they all involved lewd conduct, even though four of them were sexual in nature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for lewd conduct.

 

1459 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


McLean v. King County


No. 37400-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1519



September 8, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 86-2-17924-1. Date filed: 09/22/95. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald L. Castleberry.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners appealed from the order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) granting summary judgment to defendant county in the homeowners' action alleging violation of their rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The homeowners' other claims alleging numerous torts and civil rights violations was previously dismissed pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 12(b)(6).


OVERVIEW: As part of a serial murder investigation, a search warrant was issued for the homeowners' home. The homeowners filed an action against the county alleging numerous torts and violation of their constitutional rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. The trial court granted the county's motion to dismiss all claims except the § 1983 claim pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 12(b)(6), from which the homeowners took no appeal. The trial court later granted the county's motion for summary judgment on the homeowners' § 1983 claim. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order granting summary judgment to the county. The court ruled that municipalities could not be held liable for constitutional torts under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 on the basis of respondeat superior. However, municipalities could be held liable under § 1983 for the single act of a municipal policymaker. The court ruled that the police officer who obtained the search warrant was not a policymaker for purposes of § 1983 because he merely implemented municipal policy by seeking the warrant based on probable cause. Thus, there were no genuine issues of material fact, and the county was entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court granting summary judgment to the county in the homeowners' § 1983 action.

 

1460 of 2268 DOCUMENTS



State v. Wooten


NO. 36232-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


87 Wn. App. 821; 945 P.2d 1144; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1508



September 8, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1998, Reported at: 134 Wn.2d 1021, 958 P.2d 317, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 365.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which, after a jury found defendant guilty of second degree murder and second degree felony murder, convicted her of the crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed the passenger of a car whose driver had threatened her life. She was convicted of second degree murder and second degree felony murder and appealed her convictions. The court reversed the convictions and remanded the matter. The court held that the trial court erred by ruling that the evidence did not support her requested "no duty to retreat" instruction. A reasonable jury could have believed defendant's testimony that the driver's threat meant that she would have been shot in the near future, she thought that it was necessary to return outside and armed herself out of fear of the driver, and that defendant reasonably believed that the driver was about to shoot her. Without a "no duty to retreat" instruction, the jury could have concluded that self-defense was not applicable because flight was a reasonably effective alternative to defendant's use of force.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of second degree murder and second degree felony murder and remanded the matter for a new trial.

City of Des Moines


NO. 38367-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


87 Wn. App. 689; 943 P.2d 669; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1459



September 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
As Corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city filed a forfeiture action against appellant individual. The Superior Court of King County (Washington) granted motions by the city to vacate a prior default judgment and for summary judgment. The individual appealed.


OVERVIEW: Cocaine and cash were discovered during a police health and safety check at the individual's home. The city filed a forfeiture action in the municipal court. The individual brought a motion to remove the matter to the trial court. The city failed to appear in the removal action but filed the forfeiture action in the trial court. The individual, without giving notice to the city, obtained a default judgment in the removal action. Ultimately, the trial court granted the city's motion to vacate the default judgment and its motion for summary judgment. The trial court also denied the individual's claim that the seizure violated her constitutional rights. The individual sought review. The court determined that: (1) the trial court did not err when it vacated the default judgment because the city was entitled to notice of the hearing where it did constructively appear when it filed the forfeiture action in the trial court; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in continuing the forfeiture hearing until the motion to vacate the default judgment was held; and (3) the constitutionality of the seizure had already been determined in the individual's criminal trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the granting of the city's motions to vacate and for summary judgment in the city's civil forfeiture action against the individual.

 

1462 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. McKiearnan


No. 18956-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1439



August 28, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. McKiearnan, 87 Wn. App. 1043, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3461 (1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 94-1-01964-5. Date filed: 12/07/94. Judge signing: Hon. Grant L. Anderson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which had convicted him of assault in the second degree, unlawful imprisonment, theft in the third degree, and attempted escape in the second degree in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.36.021(1), 9A.40.040, 9A.56.050, 9A.76.120 and sentenced him under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentencing statute was unconstitutional and that his life sentence under the statute was improper. He claimed that the statute violated his constitutional rights and the separation of powers, was an unlawful bill of attainder and a violation of due process, was cruel and unusual punishment, and violated equal protection rights and the constitutional guarantee of a republican form of government. The court found that: (1) the statute was a complete act rather than revisory and did not violate separation of powers because fixing penalties was always a legislative rather than judicial function; (2) the statute was not an unconstitutional bill of attainder and provided sufficient due process safeguards; (3) the statute did not permit cruel and unusual punishment through disproportionate sentencing; and (4) the statute was not in any way a violation of equal protection rights where persistent offenders were not part of a suspect class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting and sentencing defendant.

 

1463 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mutch


No. 35810-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


87 Wn. App. 433; 942 P.2d 1018; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1385



August 25, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied at 134 Wn.2d 1016, 958 P.2d 314 (1998).
Review denied by State v. Mutch, 134 Wn.2d 1016, 958 P.2d 314, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 262 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Mutch, 141 Wn. App. 1020, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 2995 (2007)
Subsequent appeal at State v. Mutch, 2011 Wash. LEXIS 391 (Wash., June 9, 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington), which had convicted him of second degree rape and second degree kidnapping. He was sentenced to life without the possibility of parole under the state's persistent offender statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of second degree rape and second degree kidnapping. The trial court sentenced him to life without the possibility of parole under the state's persistent offender statute, § 9.94A.120, finding that he had previous convictions for robbery in California and a federal bank robbery conviction. Defendant contended that the trial court erred when it concluded that he was subject to § 9.94A.120 based on his two out-of-state convictions. The court affirmed and held that the trial court applied the correct test and properly determined that defendant's foreign convictions were equivalent to the most serious offenses in Washington. Under § 9.94A.120, a persistent offender, one who has been convicted of two "most serious offenses," must be sentenced to life without parole upon conviction for a third such offense. "Most serious offenses" included any class A felony or other offense designated by the legislature and listed in Wash. Rev. Code. § 9.94A.030(23). Convictions from other jurisdictions, which were comparable to Washington's most serious offenses, were counted as prior convictions, Wash. Rev. Code. § 9.94A.030(23)(u).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of second degree rape and second degree kidnapping, and affirmed his sentence under the state's persistent offender statute.

 

1464 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Bellevue v. Factoria Ctr. Invs.


NO. 36096-5-I, NO. 37120-7-I, NO. 36796-0-I, NO. 38132-6-I, (Consolidated and Linked)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1405



August 25, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 329.
Reported at City of Bellevue v. Factoria Ctr. Invs., Inc., 87 Wn. App. 1033, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3424 (1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-2-32814-0. Date filed: 02/08/95. Judge signing: Hon. Charles V. Johnson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision from the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which granted summary judgment dismissing its constitutional challenges to the 600-foot setback provided in Bellevue, Wash., Land Use Code § 20.20.127 and to respondent City of Bellevue's adult entertainment licensing ordinance. The corporation also appealed contempt citations issued against it for failure to comply with an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The corporation had opened an establishment offering entertainment by male dancers wearing swimwear and lingerie. Before opening, the corporation obtained a cabaret license, but not an adult cabaret license, and failed to comply with the setback. It was the failure to comply with the ordinances that formed the basis of the parties' dispute. In affirming, the court held that the licensing ordinance's definitions were not unconstitutionally overbroad, as determined by a recently decided state supreme court case. The zoning setback did not rise to the level of a prior restraint because no evidence existed that it created a blanket prohibition on adult entertainment or limited the sites available for such clubs. The setback was also a valid time, place, and manner restriction, as it was carefully tailored to meet the important and legitimate government goals of consistency in zoning and minimizing the adverse secondary effects of adult entertainment, including those from entertainment by male performers. Moreover, by knowingly stipulating to the injunction, the corporation waived its right to raise its constitutional challenge as a defense to its violation of the injunction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

 

1465 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Price


No. 34477-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


87 Wn. App. 424; 942 P.2d 377; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1417



August 25, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Reconsideration Denied September 19, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 92-1-00810-9. Date filed: 03/17/94. Judge signing: Hon. Michael F. Moynihan.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington) convicted defendant of three counts of unlawful participation in fishing by a non-Indian in a treaty Indian fishery. The trial court sentenced defendant to six months in jail on each count, to be served concurrently, and ordered him to pay $ 10,000 in fines on each count. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: The State Fish and Wildlife officials alleged that defendant illegally sold sockeye salmon on three separate days from catch area 7 at a time when the fishery was open only to treaty Indian fishermen. Defendant admitted that he was not a treaty Indian, but that he was married to a treaty Indian and that he was assisting his wife in exercising her treaty fishing rights. Defendant's wife was not with him on any of the three occasions in questions. Defendant's wife owned the boat from which defendant fished. Defendant used a state-issued commercial fishing license containing a tribal code to sell his catches. Defendant alleged that the unlawful participation statute was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority and was void for vagueness. The court affirmed the trial court and held that Wash. Rev. Code § 75.12.320 was consistent with the signal cases interpreting Indian treaty fishing rights, the pertinent provisions of the Yakama tribal code, and other applicable federal law. The grant of Indian treaty fishing rights did not extend to non-treaty Indians unless the treaty Indian was present and was being assisted by individuals who were not treaty Indians.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentence of defendant for fishing by a non-Indian in a treaty Indian fishery.

Brutsche v. City of Kent


NO. 38842-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1305



August 11, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Brutsche v. City of Kent, 87 Wn. App. 1015, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 3383 (1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-2-17465-5. Date filed: 05/30/96. Judge signing: Hon. Michael J. Fox.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which dismissed the owners' declaratory judgment action and civil rights claims, arising out of amendments to Kent, Wash., Zoning Code, against appellee city.


OVERVIEW: The city amended the zoning code to create a downtown limited manufacturing district that allowed for light manufacturing, commercial, and multifamily residential uses and a downtown commercial enterprise district that allowed for commercial and multifamily residential uses. The owners claimed that the amendments were unconstitutional for various reasons. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed and held that (1) the amendments did not violate the owners' substantive due process because they were related to the stated purpose of the Kent, Wash. Zoning Code where they were part of a plan to revitalize the downtown area by promoting certain compatible uses; (2) the amendments were not unduly oppressive where the use of the owners' plants, though nonconforming, would be allowed to continue as long as they were run by the owners; and (3) the amendments did not create spot zoning where the amendments were consistent with the city's comprehensive plan, were specifically enacted to implement the plan, and the use of the manufacturing districts was not so different from the use for the surrounding areas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1467 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


In re M.I.S.


NO. 36743-9-I (Consolidated with: NO. 36744-7-I, NO. 36745-5-I, NO. 36746-3-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1251



August 4, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-7-01073-3. Date filed: 05/04/95. Judge signing: Hon. Deborah D. Fleck.
A.S. v. Department of Soc. & Health Servs. (In re M.I.S.), 87 Wn. App. 1005, 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2297 (1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In proceedings initiated by respondent, the Department of Social and Health Services, under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.030(4)(b), (c), appellant parents sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which entered an order of dependency and dispositional orders as to the parents' four surviving children after another son died from an abdominal injury alleged to be inflicted by the father.


OVERVIEW: After emergency personnel were unable to revive the parents' two-year-old son, an autopsy revealed that he died of a blunt trauma to his abdomen. The other children were taken into protective custody; the van driver testified at the dependency hearing that the oldest child said that the father disciplined the two-year-old by stepping on him. Under the dependency and dispositional orders, the mother was permitted to be reunited with the children, but the father was ordered not to reside in the home or have unsupervised contact with them. The court affirmed. The oldest child's statements did not qualify for the excited utterance exception from the hearsay rule as they were made too long after the stressful event, but admission of the statements was harmless error. The orders were based on medical evidence showing the injury was not accidental. The parents received a meaningful hearing. No advisory jury consisting of members of the Muslim community was required. Substantial evidence supported the orders. Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.030(4)(c) was narrowly drawn to serve the compelling state interest in protecting children and was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dependency and dispositional orders.

 

1468 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Guy


No. 20507-6-II, linked with No. 20753-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


87 Wn. App. 238; 941 P.2d 674; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1233



August 1, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review granted at 134 Wn.2d 1001 (1998).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed judgments from the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which convicted them of first degree escape when they failed to report to partial confinement with a work crew. Defendants argued that they never reported to work crew and, thus, were not in the state's custody at the time of their failure to report.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were sentenced to partial confinement with a work crew. Neither reported to the work crew and they never contacted corrections officials. They were convicted of first degree escape. Defendants argued that their failure to report to work crew was not an "escape from custody" and that their convictions violated their right to equal protection. One defendant also challenged the conversion of his work crew sentence to incarceration as a violation of double jeopardy. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held defendant's status hinged on their obligation to be in custody by being physically present at a particular time and place. It did not turn on their custody status proceeding the ordered custody date. Thus, their custody status immediately before their work release sentences was not relevant. The court also found no equal protection violation. Finally, the court determined that defendant was not double punishment for the same criminal act, i.e., failing to report to the work crew. The sentencing court's conversion of his work crew sentence to total confinement was not a new sentence, but a continuing consequence of his earlier prosecution for forgery.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants convictions for first degree escape after they failed to report to a work crew.

 

1469 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Elford v. City of Battle Ground


No. 19680-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


87 Wn. App. 229; 941 P.2d 678; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1230



August 1, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied June 2, 1998, Reported at: 135 Wn.2d 1001, 959 P.2d 126, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 427.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officer challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington), which granted respondent city's motion for judgment on the pleadings in the officer's personal injury action against the city. The officer argued that his action was permitted under the Law Enforcement Officers' and Fire Fighters' Retirement System Act (LEOFF). The trial court held the officer's remedy was under the Industrial Insurance Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The officer was injured when a police dog bit him on the arm while he was on duty. He received worker's compensation benefits but argued that the award was inadequate. The officer brought a negligence action against the city, and the trial court granted the city's motion for judgment on the pleadings, but denied the city's request for attorney fees. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings. The court held that: 1) the officer's appeal was sufficiently clear to merit review; 2) although the Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 51.04.010, was more recent than the LEOFF, the provisions of the LEOFF, Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26, were more explicit and unambiguous and therefore prevailed over the Act; 3) the "right to sue" provision of the LEOFF applied to the officer prior to the legislature's 1992 amendment of the LEOFF; and 4) because the amendment was unconstitutional, it was inapplicable to the officer. Finally, on the city's challenge of the trial court's denial of fees and costs, the court held that the city was no longer the prevailing party, and therefore not entitled to such fees and costs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court dismissing the officer's action against the city seeking to recover personal injury damages, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1470 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Expert Drywall v. Ellis-Don Constr.


No. 37774-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


86 Wn. App. 884; 939 P.2d 1258; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1172



July 21, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant subcontractor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which affirmed the arbitration award in a dispute that arose between the subcontractor and respondent general contractor. The trial court affirmed the award without modification.


OVERVIEW: The general contractor hired a drywall subcontractor for a project to construct a school. A dispute arose between the parties which was handled by an arbitrator, who advised that he intended to find in favor of the subcontractor. Prior to the arbitrator's decision, the subcontractor filed a claim against the retainage held by the district. The trial court granted the general contractor's motion for summary dismissal of the claim because the parties had submitted all their disputes to the arbitrator. The general contractor subsequently filed a motion to confirm the arbitration award. The subcontractor filed a motion to modify the arbitration award to include attorney fees or, in the alternative, for vacation and remand for the arbitrator to award it attorney fees. The trial court confirmed the arbitration award without modification and the court affirmed on appeal. The court found that the claim that was submitted to the arbitrator did not constitute a lien foreclosure under Wash. Rev. Code § 60.28.030, therefore, there was no basis to give rise to a fee award. The court found that as required by § 60.28.030 the arbitrator did not have before him a proceeding to enforce a lien.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that affirmed the arbitration award to subcontractor in its dispute with the general contractor and which the lower court did not modify to include an award of attorney fees to the subcontractor.

 

1471 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Snohomish County v. Long


NO. 38587-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1116



July 21, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 5, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 361.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 95-2-08425-5. Date filed: 04/10/96. Judge signing: Hon. Richard J. Thorpe.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which granted summary judgment to respondent county in its action against the property owners for zoning violations and restrained the property owners' occupation and use of the property.


OVERVIEW: The county cited the property owners for zoning violations because they were using a travel trailer as their full time residence and because they had multiple travel trailers on their property. The trial court granted summary judgment to the county and restrained the owners from placing more than one travel trailer on the property and from occupying the property for more than six months. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that there were no genuine issues of material fact because it was undisputed that the property owners were living permanently in a travel trailer, that they had multiple travel trailers on their lot, and that the property was designated as a special flood hazard area. The court found that the statute was not void for vagueness and the definition of "travel trailer" was not overly broad. The court rejected the property owners' assertion that their property was taken without compensation finding that a zoning regulation was not a taking when it was imposed to protect the public health and safety. The court found that the county was justified in limiting the property owners' use of their property in order to protect the public from flooding hazards.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1472 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hayes


No. 20462-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1153



July 18, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 95-1-00668-8. Date filed: 03/08/96. Judge signing: Hon. James D. Roper.



DISPOSITION: Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which denied his motion for reconsideration regarding the ruling on his motion for suppression and his conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of a school bus stop.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped near a school bus stop for a cracked windshield. The officer discovered that defendant had a suspended license, arrested him, and found drugs in the car. Defendant confessed to intending to deliver the drugs. Defendant's motion to suppress was denied in part on a finding that defendant had crossed a double yellow centerline. The officer later told the prosecutor that there was no double yellow line. The trial court granted a motion to remove this finding, but denied defendant's motion for reconsideration. On appeal, the court remanded for a hearing on the validity of the stop. Because the change to the findings was substantive and the validity of the stop for a cracked windshield required further consideration, the court held that defendant was entitled to a hearing under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(c)(2). If the stop was valid, the court ruled that the officer could arrest defendant for a suspended license and could search the car and that the evidence in the car was the corpus delicti for defendant's confession. The court found sufficient evidence of the school bus stop and that the enhancement was constitutional as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court remanded defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver within 1,000 feet of a school bus stop for a reconsideration of the denial of defendant's motion to suppress and a reconsideration of the validity of defendant's stop. If the denial of defendant's motion to suppress was affirmed, the trial court was to affirm the conviction, and if reversed, the trial court was to reverse the conviction.

 

1473 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Richards


No. 20375-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1113



July 18, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 7, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 69.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 95-1-00837-2. Date filed: 02/15/96. Judge signing: Hon. James D. Ladley.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) entered a judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder. Defendant, who was 16 years old at the time of the murder, appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police asked to search the crawl space below defendant's house. Defendant was present when his father consented to the search and did not object. After the victim's body was found, defendant, who was 16 years old at the time, led one of the officers back to his bedroom and confessed to the murder. Forensic evidence showed that the victim had been beaten on the head, rendered unconscious, and then strangled. Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to 47 years. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that because defendant's father consented to the search and because he had a superior interest in the house and in the area searched, the police had not needed defendant's consent before searching the crawl space. The court further held that defendant's confession was not coerced, that the defendant properly was tried as an adult, that there was sufficient evidence that the murder was premeditated, that the trial court's use of victim vulnerability as an aggravating factor was not clearly erroneous, and that, given the brutality of the crime and the vulnerability of the victim, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing defendant to 47 years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1474 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Grasser


No. 19703-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1080



July 11, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 94-1-00748-1. Date filed: 06/16/95. Judge signing: Hon. James Edgar F. Warme.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court for Cowlitz County, Washington, which convicted him of possession of firearms in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040.


OVERVIEW: An officer approached defendant while he was working on his pickup. Defendant consented to a search of the pickup, and the officer found two firearms. Defendant later admitted to owning the guns. As defendant was previously convicted of harassment, he was arrested, charged, and ultimately convicted of possessing firearms in violation of § 9.41.040. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. The court rejected defendant's contention that certain amendments to § 9.41.040 were unconstitutional because they were part of a bill embracing more than one subject and they were vague. The court held that the particular section that amended § 9.41.040 was clearly related to the act's title and to its primary purpose of violence prevention. The court held that Wash. Const. art. II, sec. 19 was not violated by the amendments to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040. The court also held that § 9.41.040, in clear and simple terms, barred the possession of firearms by individuals previously convicted of certain specified crimes. The court stated that the statute did not fail to give fair warning, nor did it permit arbitrary law enforcement. The court held that the statute was not void for vagueness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1475 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Lester v. Town of Winthrop


No. 15469-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL NINE


87 Wn. App. 17; 939 P.2d 1237; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 1072



July 10, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the judgment of the Superior Court of Okanogan County (Washington), which granted respondent town's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the property owners' action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for improperly conditioning their permit on their grant of an easement.


OVERVIEW: Two property owners, a husband and wife, applied for a shoreline substantial development permit. The town's permit administrator issued the permit with an easement condition. The property owners appealed, and before the appeal hearing, the town deleted the easement requirement. The revised permit was filed with the Department of Ecology (department). Because of the department's 30-day review period, the property owners could not begin construction until late November when weather conditions made it impractical to do so. The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of the town. The property owners could not recover under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, because they were not deprived of a federally protected right. The delay in obtaining the permit was not sufficient to establish a substantive due process claim. The property owners could not maintain a negligent hiring claim against the town because they failed to show that the imposition of the easement was due to the permit administrator's lack of training. Because the condition was consistent with the town's shoreline program, the permit administrator's poor job performance was not the proximate cause of the property owners' damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting the town's motion for summary judgment.

 

1476 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Zedler


No. 37680-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 958



June 16, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 94-1-00899-7. Date filed: 10/19/95. Judge signing: Hon. Steven J. Mura.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court for Whatcom County, Washington, which convicted defendant of two counts of first degree theft and two counts of unlawful issuance of bank checks.


OVERVIEW: Defendant purchased heating equipment on two separate occasions and paid for the equipment by checks. Defendant subsequently cancelled payment on both checks and refused to issue the heating equipment company new checks or to return the equipment. Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree theft and two counts of unlawful issuance of bank checks. Defendant claimed on appeal that his convictions for both offenses were prohibited by the double jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. amend. V and the merger doctrine. The court rejected defendant's claims. The court ruled that double jeopardy did not apply because the offenses of first degree theft under Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.56.020(b), 9A.56.020(1)(a) and unlawful issuance of bank checks under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.060 were separate crimes that required proof of separate elements that were punishable separately. The court also ruled that the merger doctrine did not apply because first degree theft did not require proof of the unlawful issuance of bank checks and because the unlawful issuance of bank checks did not depend upon the presence or absence of theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two counts of first degree thefts and two counts of unlawful issuance of bank checks.

 

1477 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vanoli


NO. 37218-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


86 Wn. App. 643; 937 P.2d 1166; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 923



June 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Island County (Washington), which convicted him of three counts of delivering LSD to minors within 1000 feet of a designated school bus stop.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sold drops of LSD to three minors. The court affirmed his convictions for three counts of delivery. The court held that the jury instruction defining knowledge did not allow the jury to find knowledge based on a high probability of the existence of a fact, but required the jury to find that defendant acted with actual, subjective knowledge in order to convict him. The first offender waiver was not available to defendant because Wash. Rev. Code § 9094A.030(22)(a) specifically excluded anyone convicted of selling LSD from the definition of first-time offender. The trial court did not err in calculating defendant's offender score because his convictions did not involve the same criminal conduct. Although the convictions involved the same time and place, they involved three different victims. Each transaction had as its objective the sale of LSD to a different purchaser. The purpose of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.406 was to punish deliveries to minors. His sentence, which imposed a 120-month prison sentence and 12-month community supervision did not exceed the statutory maximum because if he served the entire prison sentence he would not be subject to community supervision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision convicting defendant of three counts of delivering LSD to minors within 1000 feet of a designated school bus stop.

State v. Burton


NO. 35747-6-I Consolidated with NO. 38077-0-I, NO. 38217-9-I, NO. 39119-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 933



June 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 86 Wn. App. 1046.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 93-1-06948-7. Date filed: 12/19/94. Judge signing: Hon. Patricia H. Aitken.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and amended sentence from the Superior Court of King County (Washington) for rape, robbery, and burglary in the first degree. Two personal restraint petitions based on ineffective assistance of counsel were also presented for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered the home of a 15 year old boy, raped him, and stole money. He was in jail on another rape charge when he told the story of the rape to another inmate who then reported him by writing a letter to the prosecutor. The court held that the letter was admissible and was not hearsay, because it was consistent with the declarant's testimony at trial. The court held that a doctor's testimony as to time, as reported by the victim was admissible under the hearsay exception for statement made for medical diagnosis. The court held defendant was not entitled to a mistrial because of the admission of evidence of other crimes committed by him. The court held that it was highly unlikely that the admission of an unconstitutionally obtained prior conviction influenced the outcome of the present case, and the trial court did not err in refusing to grant a new trial on that basis. The court remanded defendant's sentence. The sentence was potentially subject to the presumption of judicial vindictiveness because it was a sentence imposed following a partially successful appeal. The court held that defendant had to be given a sentence not more severe than the original sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and remanded the case for sentencing consistent with its opinion.

 

1479 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tortorelli


No. 36560-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 936



June 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied February 2, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Wash. LEXIS 120. Reported in Table Case Format at: 86 Wn. App. 1046.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-05132-2. Date filed: 04/17/95. Judge signing: Hon. Leroy McCullough.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Kings County (Washington) convicting him of theft, trafficking in stolen property, criminal profiteering, and offering a false document.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of removing logs from a lake without authority. He contended that his case should have been dismissed after the State obtained a privileged document, that he should have been charged under log patrol statutes because they superseded the general statutes under which he was charged, and that his crimes should have been merged into one crime. The court held that (1) the privileged document was intercepted by the State during its investigation of defendant and it was defendant's burden to show application of the attorney-client privilege because the Sixth Amendment was not implicated; (2) defendant failed to show that the trial court's suppression of the privileged document was an inadequate remedy; (3) defendant was properly charged under general statutes because the special log patrol statute did not punish conduct that was also punishable under general statutes and thus, the special statute was not concurrent with the general statutes; and (4) the merger doctrine did not apply to defendant's theft and stolen property convictions because those crimes could not be elevated to a higher degree by proof of another crime proscribed elsewhere in the criminal code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.

1481 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. J.D.


No. 36797-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


86 Wn. App. 501; 937 P.2d 630; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 886



June 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted February 9, 1998, Reported at: 134 Wn.2d 1006, 954 P.2d 277, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 87.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minor sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington), which convicted him for resisting arrest when an officer tried to cite him for violating curfew. Respondent state sought to dismiss the conviction pursuant to Wash. R. App. P. 7.2(e).


OVERVIEW: The minor was arrested after police officers warned him that he would be cited if he refused to leave an area that had a curfew. The court granted the state's request to dismiss the conviction but review was still appropriate under the mootness doctrine. The court found the curfew ordinance unconstitutional, as it infringed upon minors' fundamental freedom of movement and expression and was not narrowly tailored to address the problem of juvenile crime. Although the curfew ordinance satisfied the first prong of the strict scrutiny test because crime prevention and protecting minors from becoming victims were sufficiently compelling interests, the ordinance was not narrowly tailored to meet the government's purpose. There was not a sufficient nexus between the curfew and juvenile victimization or crime rates to withstand strict scrutiny, as the only evidence before the court showed that the curfew had no impact at all on juvenile crime. The ordinance was also unconstitutionally vague, as it was unclear about what was and what was not an exempted activity.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's request to dismiss the minor's conviction for resisting arrest, which stemmed from the minor's curfew violation. Pursuant to the mootness doctrine, the court reviewed the curfew ordinance and found it unconstitutional.

 

1482 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Seattle v. McConahy


No. 36995-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


86 Wn. App. 557; 937 P.2d 1133; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 889



June 2, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County (Washington) held that Seattle, Wash., Ordinance 15.48.040 was constitutional in an action commenced by appellants, a homeless youth and an advocate for the city's homeless, against respondent city. The youth and advocate challenged the anti-sitting ordinance on several state constitutional grounds after being cited for violation of the ordinance. The youth and advocate appealed.


OVERVIEW: When cited for violating the anti-sitting ordinance, the youth was panhandling and the advocate was leafleting. The court affirmed their convictions. The court stated that although the state's constitution expressly acknowledged that governments were established to protect individual rights, the state constitution also permitted municipalities to make and enforce police and public health regulations. Consequently, the court held that the ordinance furthered a legitimate police power interest in a manner that infringed only minimally on the youth's and advocate's freedom of movement. The court found that (1) because neither the youth nor advocate was engaged in expressive conduct when arrested, the court need not decide whether the ordinance was a reasonable time, place, and manner restriction on speech; (2) because sitting did not have an inherent expressive value the ordinance was not overbroad; (3) although the ordinance exempted patrons of commercial establishments and hence created classes, the ordinance applied to all members of each class in the same way and the distinction it drew was a rational one; and (4) the ordinance did not implicate the right to travel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's holding that the municipal ordinance was constitutional.

 

1483 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Long


No. 37615-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 821



May 27, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-1-04704-8. Date filed: 11/06/95. Judge signing: Hon. Donald Haley.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court for King County (Washington) convicting him of one count of possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver after a bench trial and entering an exceptional sentence of 36 months' imprisonment, which was in excess of the top of the standard range of 21 to 27 months, based on the existence of an aggravating factor under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.390(2)(d)(ii) (repealed).


OVERVIEW: Defendant became subject to police audio and video surveillance and was apprehended attempting to sell what he acknowledged to be 2.5 kilograms of methamphetamine. He appealed his exceptional sentence, contending that the trial court erred by imposing an exceptional sentence based on the amount of methamphetamine involved in the transaction. Affirming the sentence, the court held that defendant's sentence was properly based on the statutory aggravating factor in § 9.94A.390(2)(d)(ii) which targeted sale or attempted sales of a controlled substance in an amount substantially larger than for personal use. The court found that the record supported the trial court's finding that defendant in fact attempted to sell an amount substantially larger than for personal use and that the exceptional sentence was justified as a matter of law. The court rejected defendant's arguments that he had been subjected to a violation of his constitutional right to equal protection because he did not have a right to a particular result with respect to the sentence imposed under the circumstances presented.


OUTCOME: The exceptional sentence was affirmed.

State v. Gholston


NO. 36360-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 833



May 27, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-04856-9. Date filed: 03/23/95. Judge signing: Hon. Richard M. Ishikawa.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which convicted defendant of two counts of rape in the first degree, one count of robbery, and one count of kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court erred by failing to suppress his statement where the police continued to question him after he requested counsel. Defendant challenged certain conditions of community placement imposed by the trial court, contending that those conditions exceed the trial court's authority under the Washington Sentencing Reform Act. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because defendant's statement was not introduced during the State's case-in-chief but was used to impeach defendant. The court affirmed the conditions of community placement, holding that (1) the trial court could require defendant to enter into mental health or sexual deviancy treatment under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(9)(c)(iii); (2) the prohibition against contact with minor children was a valid a prohibition against contact with a specified class under § 9.94A.120(9)(c)(ii); (3) the requirement of polygraph and plethysmograph testing was valid for the limited purpose of monitoring defendant's compliance with the community placement conditions; and (4) the restrictions upon possession or perusal of pornographic materials were reasonably related to the monitoring of defendant's progress.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court also affirmed the conditions of community placement, subject to the limitations on polygraph and plethysmograph testing for the purpose of monitoring defendant's compliance with the conditions of community placement.
