State v. Shadeed


No. 35647-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 858



May 27, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-01095-2. Date filed: 11/10/94. Judge signing: Hon. Richard M. Ishikawa.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of taking a motor vehicle without permission, attempted second degree robbery, and attempting to elude a police vehicle and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted robbery, eluding police officers, and taking a motor vehicle without permission and a separate jury sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole pursuant to the Sentencing Reform Act's persistent offender provisions (SRA-POP), Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9.94A.120(4), 9.94A.030(23), and 9.94A.030(27). The court affirmed the convictions and sentence and found that the lower court properly refused to sever the offenses because the evidence was particularly strong for the most serious charge, the defenses were simple denials, and defendant demonstrated no prejudice. The court determined that it was not erroneous to admit two exhibits establishing defendant's prior California convictions because the relevant documents were self-authenticating. The court concluded that defendant's sentence under SRA-POP was not cruel and unusual under the state constitution because the crimes he was convicted of were violent and involved risk of injury to persons. The court found that defendant did not have a state due process right to challenge the constitutionality of his earlier strikes during the sentencing proceeding for his third strike.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for taking a motor vehicle without permission, attempted second degree robbery, and attempting to elude a police vehicle and his sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.

State v. Conklin


No. 36409-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 780



May 19, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 8, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. LEXIS 721.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-00379-4. Date filed: 03/10/95. Judge signing: Hon. Carmen Otero.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and affirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of child molestation and indecent liberties.


OVERVIEW: Defendant held numerous positions in law enforcement and was an attorney. Defendant gave physical examinations to boys that he befriended. The defense trial strategy was to admit the examinations took place, but to deny their purpose was for sexual gratification. On review, the court found that defendant was able to and did participate to an unusual degree in his own defense and that each instance of counsel's performance that he alleged was ineffective, was consistent with their trial strategy. The court determined that defendant's counsel did not violate the exclusionary rule when his cross-examination questions referred to the suppressed fruits of an illegal search. The court found that the admission of evidence of examinations of boys that were not the subject of criminal charges was not error as the trial court understood that the defense would not and did not object to these witnesses as part of its trial strategy. The court concluded that the prosecutor did not commit misconduct by eliciting testimony that when female witnesses were at defendant's home, he was not interested in them. The court affirmed defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for child molestation and indecent liberties.

 

1487 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Westberg v. All-Purpose Structures


No. 19869-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


86 Wn. App. 405; 936 P.2d 1175; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 723



May 9, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Amending Published Opinion June 19, 1997.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An architect, the third party defendant, appealed the denial of his demand of a jury trial de novo by the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), after he did not attend a mandatory arbitration hearing that was held in an action filed by plaintiff customer against defendant builder.


OVERVIEW: The architect was named as a third party defendant by the builder that had been sued by the customer. The architect filed an answer and answered interrogatories. Then, the matter was submitted to binding arbitration. The architect did not appear at the arbitration hearing, and the builder was awarded damages on his third party complaint. The architect then demanded a jury trial de novo, which the trial court denied because of his failure to appear at the arbitration hearing. The architect appealed, asserting violations of due process and the right to a jury trial. The court affirmed the trial court's denial of a jury trial de novo. The court held that there was no denial of due process as alleged. The right to a trial de novo could be conditioned on participation in an evidentiary hearing at the arbitration stage without such a constitutional violation occurring. Further, there was no denial of the right to a jury trial. Rather, the architect waived that right by his failure, without good cause, to participate in the arbitration process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the architect's request for a jury trial de novo.

State v. Randon


No. 20106-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 728



May 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1101.
Petition for Review Denied October 7, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. LEXIS 681.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 95-1-01065-4. Date filed: 10/11/95. Judge signing: Hon. Nile E. Aubrey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County Washington, which convicted defendant of delivery of rock cocaine within 1,000 feet of school grounds.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted, defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence, that the State made improper remarks during closing arguments, and that the evidence did not support the conviction. On review, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. In reaching its conclusion, the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting testimony concerning polygraphs. The court then held that, because defendant did not contemporaneously object to the State's remarks they were reviewed to determine whether it was so flagrant and ill intentioned that it causes an enduring and resulting prejudice that it could not be neutralized by an admonition to the jury. Applying such a standard, the court held that the State's comments did not warrant reversal. The court then held that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction under the enhancement statute. The court found that an officer's pacing of the distance between the location of the offense and the school was sufficient to establish the distance element under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Zenker v. City of Puyallup


No. 19499-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 731



May 9, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1099.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 94-2-00209-6. Date filed: 04/21/95. Judge signing: Hon. Donald H. Thompson.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which ruled that the landowner's petition for review of respondent city's conditional approval of a preliminary plat application was untimely.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought preliminary plat approval to subdivide a parcel of real property into single-family residential lots. The city council voted to approve the plat on condition that the landowner would be required to construct a temporary storm drainage system. The landowner sought judicial review by filing a petition for writ of certiorari within the 30-day time limit of Wash. Rev. Code § 58.17.180. The trial court found that the petition was untimely under Puyallup, Wash., Municipal Code § 2.54.140, which provided only a 10-day period to appeal the city council's action. The court reversed, observing that when more than one appeal period applied, the longer period generally controlled. Moreover, a city could exercise only such power as was delegated to it by the legislature, and the legislature had not explicitly delegated to municipalities the task of setting time limits for judicial review of land use decisions. Consequently, the ordinance was void to the extent that it conflicted with state law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for trial.

State v. Doppie


No. 20481-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 672



May 2, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1092.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 95-1-01627-1. Date filed: 02/23/96. Judge signing: Hon. Richard D. Hicks.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court for Thurston County, Washington, which convicted him of first-degree manslaughter based on his guilty plea. Defendant argued lack of jurisdiction at the trial court level and contended that Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to first-degree manslaughter. The trial court convicted him. Section 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv) made an exception to juvenile court jurisdiction for 16 or 17-year-old juveniles accused of specific violent offenses. Here on appeal, defendant argued that § 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv) was unconstitutional. He also argued that the trial court had lacked jurisdiction because he was under the age of 18 and because the trial court never held a juvenile court declination hearing prior to trying him. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The constitutionality of § 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv) had previously been upheld by the supreme court. The supreme court had held that decline hearings were not constitutionally required and that § 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv) did not confer unlimited discretion on prosecutors to decide jurisdiction based upon charges. The supreme court had also held that § 13.04.030(1)(e)(iv) satisfied the rational unity test under Wash. Const. art. II, § 19.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Riles


NO. 32516-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


86 Wn. App. 10; 936 P.2d 11; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 614



April 28, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Petition for Review Granted October 7, 1997, Reported at: 133 Wn.2d 1009, 946 P.2d 402.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which convicted defendant of first degree rape of a child and sentenced defendant to a term of community placement to follow his confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a jury of first degree rape of a child. The trial court imposed a term of community placement to follow his confinement. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by attaching conditions to his community placement term, including the condition that he submit to polygraph and plethysmograph tests and the condition prohibiting unapproved contact with minors. Defendant also contended that the search warrant's supporting affidavit was insufficient. In affirming the conviction and sentence, the court held that the trial court was authorized, under the Sentencing Reform Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A, to order the polygraph and plethysmograph tests to monitor defendant's compliance with other community placement conditions. Moreover, each of the conditions, including the condition prohibiting unapproved contact with minors, gave sufficient notice of what conduct was prohibited and were not overbroad or vague. Finally, defendant failed to show that the search warrant's supporting affidavit was insufficient because the affiant's failure to expressly state that the affiant learned his information from the victim's mother did not constitute a material omission.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Andree


No. 39567-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


90 Wn. App. 917; 954 P.2d 346; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 2163



April 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Denying Appellant's Motion for Reconsideration July 29, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. App. LEXIS 1196.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon a jury verdict, the Superior Court of King County (Washington) entered a judgment of conviction against defendant for animal cruelty in the first degree, which was a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.205. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: At trial, the state's evidence showed that defendant stabbed a kitten nine times with a hunting knife. On appeal, defendant initially claimed that the animal cruelty statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.205 was vague. The court pointed out that the statute established three separate and distinct acts that amounted to first degree animal cruelty. The court found that defendant's actions were clearly prohibited under the first two alternatives. Section 16.52.205 provided in part that a person was guilty of animal cruelty in the first degree when he or she intentionally inflicts substantial pain on an animal or causes physical injury to an animal. Defendant also challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to support his conviction. The court thought that defendant's own testimony was enough evidence to support a conviction based on causing physical injury to the kitten.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for animal cruelty in the first degree.

Mount Spokane Skiing Corp. v. Spokane County


No. 16149-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


86 Wn. App. 165; 936 P.2d 1148; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 560



April 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Order Granting Motion to Publish May 7, 1997. Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1072.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ski corporation challenged the order of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington) that granted summary judgment to respondent county in the ski corporation's action, which sought a declaration that the county unlawfully created a public development authority to operate a ski concession at the state park in which the ski corporation held an exclusive agreement to operate a sports, recreation, and ski area.


OVERVIEW: The ski corporation previously entered into an exclusive 20-year agreement with the state to operate a sports, recreation, and ski area in a state park. The ski corporation held a possessory interest in the ski lifts and other improvements in the concession area. After the county subsequently created the public development authority (authority) to operate the ski concession at the state park, the ski corporation filed an action in superior court, seeking a declaration that the authority was an illegal entity, and that the statute that gave the county permission to create the authority, Wash. Rev. Code § 35.21.730, was unconstitutional. The superior court granted summary judgment against the ski corporation. The court affirmed, holding that because the authority, as a public corporation, met two of the purposes set out in § 35.21.730, the authority was validly created by the county. The court noted that the authority's operation of the ski area constituted a public purpose and function. The court further concluded that the county did not abuse its discretion in creating the authority and delegating its powers to it to remedy the problems with the concessions at the ski area.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's order that granted summary judgment to the county in the ski corporation's action, which sought a declaration that the county unlawfully created the public development authority to operate a ski concession at the state park in which the ski corporation held an exclusive agreement to operate a sports, recreation, and ski area.

State v. Hampton


No. 37271-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 534



April 14, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1065.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-07847-6. Date filed: 08/21/95. Judge signing: Hon. George T. Mattson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court for King County, Washington, based on a jury verdict that convicted defendant of rape of a child and two lesser included offenses of communication with a minor for immoral purposes, and the exceptional sentence imposed thereon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for engaging in sexual intercourse with his 14-year old niece. The evidence included a provocative photograph of the girl, found during a warrantless search of defendant's wallet. The wallet was taken from defendant's person at the time of arrest, but was not search until three hours later. The court stated that the delay was reasonable because it resulted from special arrangements the officers made to accommodate defendant's status as a police officer, and that the search was lawful as incident to a valid arrest. Because the inventoried wallet was inventoried for the legitimate purpose of protecting against a fraudulent claim of theft, the court held that the wallet search of the wallet was valid as an inventory search. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by imposing an exceptional sentence. The niece was sent to live with defendant because she was having serious problems including drug and alcohol abuse, failure to attend school, and engaging in sexual relations with numerous young men. The exceptional sentence was justified under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(2), in view of the niece's status as an "at risk" child and defendant's abuse of trust.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1495 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. Wayman


No. 19331-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


85 Wn. App. 710; 934 P.2d 707; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 522



April 11, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county appealed the orders of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which denied its motions for summary judgment and judgment notwithstanding the verdict in an action by plaintiff homeowners, as assignee of defendant builders, for damages caused by negligent building inspections. The trial court submitted the issue of the public duty doctrine to the jury, which gave judgment against the county.


OVERVIEW: In an action over the grossly deficient construction of a new home, only a cross-claim of the builders against the county, assigned by the homeowners, remained at trial. On appeal, the court reversed the denial of the motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict because it also was dispositive of the summary judgment issue. The court held that the public duty doctrine provided that a government was not liable to individuals except in certain circumstances and relieved the government from liability for negligence. The court held that the doctrine did not apply to proprietary functions, but that building inspection was a governmental function. The doctrine was not a grant of immunity, but rather defined the persons to whom a government owed an actionable duty for negligence. The court held that under the "special relationship" exception, a government could be liable to an individual when the individual made specific inquiries of an official, the official answered, and the individual relied on the answers. The court held that building inspections were not warranties of code compliance and created no special duty absent specific representations.


OUTCOME: The court held that there was no evidence of a special relationship between the homeowners or builder and the county, and the trial court erred when it did not grant the county's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict based on the public duty doctrine. The court also held that the failure-to-enforce doctrine and legislative intent exceptions did not apply. The court reversed the judgment against the county.

 

1496 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Johns v. Erhart


No. 15238-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


85 Wn. App. 607; 934 P.2d 701; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 503



April 8, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment creditors took a default judgment against respondent judgment debtors in 1985. In 1995, they filed the judgment in Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington). Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 6.17.020, they moved for an order extending the time for execution of their judgment. The trial court refused to grant the extension. The creditors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The question was whether execution of the bankruptcy court judgment qualified for an extension under Wash. Rev. Code § 6.17.020. The court held that it did not and affirmed the trial court. The creditors argued that pursuant to § 6.36.025(1) foreign judgments filed in superior court were to be enforced in the same manner as a judgment of the superior court. The creditors' bankruptcy judgment was not rendered by a court of record in Washington. They were not, therefore, entitled to an extension. Section 6.17.020 unambiguously required that a judgment be rendered by a court of record of Washington and that application for the extension be made to the court rendering the judgment. The trial court correctly refused to extend the time for execution. Section 6.36.025 implemented the constitutional requirement of full faith and credit. It provided that any properly authenticated foreign judgment filed in superior court could be enforced like any state superior court judgment. The creditors' bankruptcy judgment could be "enforced" like any other state superior court judgment. It was only the time within which that judgment had to be enforced that could not be extended.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court denying the creditors' motion for an extension of time for execution.

Walden v. City of Seattle


NO. 37059-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 499



April 7, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1055.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 92-2-16337-3. Date filed: 07/07/95.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, minor and his mother, appealed from the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which entered judgment in favor of defendant police department in a case concerning alleged misconduct by the police department.


OVERVIEW: The officer attempted to stop a car occupied by four young men. The car did not stop immediately, but soon pulled up in front of the home of one of the passengers. The officer began to ticket the driver for having a defective license plate lamp. Meanwhile, the minor came out of the house and joined the three passengers on the stairs above the sidewalk. The group directed toward the officers a torrent of criticism and insult. The minor was booked for harassment, obstruction, and hindering. On appeal, the minor and his mother contended that one of the jury instructions allowed the jury to find obstruction of a police officer based on mere speech. The superior court's refusal to consider giving a limiting instruction may have been reversible error had the minor proposed one that did not go to the opposite extreme. However, the minor failed to preserve any error there may have been in the instruction. Therefore, the court affirmed the ruling of the superior court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the superior court, which entered judgment in favor of the police department in a case concerning the alleged misconduct by one of its officers.

 

1498 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Harlow


No. 15219-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


85 Wn. App. 557; 933 P.2d 1076; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 463



April 3, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Yakima County (Washington), which denied her motion to dismiss a citation for driving with a suspended license. Defendant claimed that the maintenance of a suspended licenses list was an unconstitutional search, and an unreasonable invasion of her private affairs.


OVERVIEW: A police officer kept a list of city residents who were believed to have suspended licenses and pulled over defendant after he saw her driving and remembered her name was on the list. Defendant was arrested and booked into jail for driving while her license was suspended and moved to dismiss the citation. The trial court denied the motion, and defendant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that: (1) the officer was not running a random check; (2) defendant's driving record was obtained through Wash. Rev. Code § 46.52.150, which provided an articulable reason to stop and investigate her; (3) driving records kept by the department of licensing, like warrants records, were neither subjectively nor reasonably expected to be unavailable to police officers; and (4) defendant's limited privacy interest in her driving record was outweighed by the state's vital interest in promoting highway safety by ensuring that only those qualified to drive do so.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court that denied defendant's motion to dismiss a citation for driving with a suspended license.

 

1499 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Bauknecht v. State


No. 14986-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 467



April 3, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 85 Wn. App. 1050.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 94-2-01977-0. Date filed: 05/30/95. Judge signing: Hon. Harold D. Clarke Jr.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, employee and his wife (employee), sought recovery from appellees employer and its individual officers (employer) for wrongful termination. The employer alleged that this claim was barred by collateral estoppel because it had been ruled upon in a prior action in federal court. The Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington) granted the employer's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the complaint. The employee sought review.


OVERVIEW: The employer claimed that the federal court's finding that the employee had no property interest in his position because he was an at-will employee collaterally estopped him from litigating this wrongful termination claim in state court. The employee claimed that collateral estoppel did not apply because the issue in state court was not identical with that in federal court, where there was no final judgment, and because application of the doctrine would be unjust. The court rejected the employee's claim and affirmed the lower court's judgment. The court found that, in granting the employer summary judgment, the federal court specifically concluded that the employee was an at-will employee with no property interest in his position, and that the issue in the state court was the same. The court also found that the federal court's dismissal on summary judgment was a final judgment on the merits and that issues decided on summary judgment were accorded preclusive effect. The court also held that there was no injustice because the evidence established that the employee had no property interest in his position because the employer could terminate him at will, instead of for cause.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment that granted the employer's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the employee's complaint.

 

1500 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hrycenko


No. 37687-0-I, No. 37770-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE, DIVISION ONE


85 Wn. App. 543; 933 P.2d 435; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 462



March 31, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 95-1-00524-4. Date filed: 10/11/95. Judge signing: Hon. Michael F. Moynihan.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged judgments of the Superior Court for Whatcom County, Washington, which imposed exceptional sentences after finding that the quantities of drugs in their possession were substantially larger than for personal use.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted of possession with intent to deliver controlled substances. They were each given exceptional sentences after the trial court determined that the quantities of drugs involved were substantially larger than for personal use. The court affirmed the judgments, finding that defendants did not meet their burden of proving that the statute was unconstitutionally void as applied to them. The court held that The Sentencing Reform Act of 1981 structured discretionary decisions affecting sentences and required the sentencing court to articulate reasons for any exceptional sentence as a limit to the judge's discretion. Thus, while a justification for an exceptional sentence was necessarily subjective, a sentencing court's discretion was not arbitrary. Further, because standard range and exceptional sentences were determined on an individualized basis with reference to the conduct of the defendant, equal protection was not violated by differing sentences for different offenders committing the same crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which imposed exceptional sentences on defendants for their convictions of possession with intent to deliver controlled substances.

 

1501 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Seattle v. Abercrombie


No. 37079-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


85 Wn. App. 393; 945 P.2d 1132; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 359



March 17, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Denying Motion for Reconsideration April 8, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wn. App. LEXIS 564. Petition for Review Denied September 3, 1997, Reported at: 133 Wn.2d 1005, 943 P.2d 663, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 654.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of obstructing a public officer in violation of Seattle, Wash., Municipal Code § 12A.16.010(A)(5), arguing that the obstruction ordinance under which he was charged was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Police were investigating a narcotics incident and were interviewing people at the crime scene. They interviewed defendant and told him he was free to go. He chose to remain at the scene and screamed obscenities at the officers and threatened to kill them. The officers told him that if he did not leave he would be arrested. When he still did not leave, they arrested him. He was convicted of obstructing a public officer in violation of § 12A.16.010(A)(5). On appeal, the court affirmed, finding that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it did not limit what a person could say to police officers, nor did it limit a person's ability to observe what police were doing at a public crime scene. Rather, a violation of the ordinance was triggered only by refusing to comply with an order to leave the scene of an investigation, not by an exercise of free speech rights. The court also found that the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague because it did not allow police unfettered discretion to tell a person observing public police action to move on; rather, it required that before a person could be told to leave, he must have acted in a way that obstructed an officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order convicting defendant of obstructing a public officer.

 

1502 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Sigler v. Sigler


No. 14541-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TEN


85 Wn. App. 329; 932 P.2d 710; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 340



March 13, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, State of Washington (state), challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Kittitas County (Washington), which held that Wash. Rev. Code § 26.19.075(1)(d), a statute disallowing a residential credit to noncustodial parents when the custodial parent received Aid for Families with Dependent Children (AFDC), was unconstitutional and granted defendant father a reduction in child support without having made specific findings of fact.


OVERVIEW: The state brought an action for child support against the father, and he requested a deviation from the child support schedule for a residential credit. Section 26.19.075(1)(d) disallowed a residential credit to noncustodial parents when the custodial parent received AFDC. The trial court held that § 26.19.075(1)(d) was unconstitutional under a rational basis test. The court reversed. The statute was presumed to be constitutional, and the court rejected a strict scrutiny and intermediate scrutiny test. Although maintaining a relationship with one's child was a fundamental right that would require a strict scrutiny analysis, § 26.19.075(1)(d) did not directly and substantially interfere with that right. Intermediate scrutiny was usually used when physical liberty was at stake. The statute passed the rational basis test in that the law affected an entire class of noncustodial parents whose children received AFDC, there were reasonable grounds to distinguish that class based on laws that required reimbursement by AFDC recipients, and there was a rational relationship to a state interest in requiring parents, rather than the state, to support their children.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision that determined the statute to have been unconstitutional. The court also reversed the order that reduced the father's child support because the required specific findings were not made.

 

1503 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bevins


NO. 36637-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


85 Wn. App. 280; 932 P.2d 190; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 322



March 10, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of second-degree arson.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the State did not establish the lower court's jurisdiction and produced insufficient evidence to prove he acted maliciously. He also argued that the late entered findings and conclusions were tailored, and warrant reversal. Finally, he argued that the statute providing for manifest injustice dispositions was unconstitutional, and the lower court's manifest injustice finding was error. The court affirmed defendant's conviction because it accepted the late entered findings and conclusions. The court also held that sufficient evidence was presented and the lower court's jurisdiction was established. Furthermore, the court found that the manifest injustice statute was constitutional and that the lower court's manifest injustice ruling was not erroneous. It was very likely that defendant would commit the offense again, needed treatment, was a danger to the community, and would not receive the necessary treatment with a standard range disposition. These factors justified a manifest injustice disposition.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for second-degree arson was affirmed.

 

1504 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 19545-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


85 Wn. App. 271; 932 P.2d 665; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 315



March 7, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 93-2-12726-5. Judgment or order under review. Date filed: 05/12/95. Judge signing: Hon. Rosanne N. Buckner.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which revoked his Washington driver's license issued by respondent state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the federal security officer who stopped him at the gate to the military base was not a "law enforcement officer" or "arresting officer" within the contemplation of the implied consent statute. Thus, the state department of licensing (DOL) did not establish jurisdiction for its revocation of his driver's license. On review, the court disagreed. The DOL had authority under prior Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.308(6) (1986) to revoke a licensee's driving privilege upon receipt of a sworn report of a law enforcement officer stating that, after valid warnings, the licensee refused to take a breathalyzer test. The terms "law enforcement officer" and "arresting officer" included any officer empowered to enforce the law. The court also found that the state lost jurisdiction to regulate within federal property only where state and federal law conflicted. The suspension or revocation of a driver's license was not penal in nature and was not intended as punishment, but was designed solely for the protection of the public in the use of the highways. There was no double jeopardy violation because defendant was already punished in federal court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of defendant's driver's license by the state.

 

1505 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barnes


No. 17717-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


85 Wn. App. 638; 932 P.2d 669; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 316



March 7, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended on Denial of Motion for Reconsideration April 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 578.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision from the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which convicted him of leading organized crime. He contended that the trial court should have applied principles of double jeopardy and collateral estoppel to bar the prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Evidence of a sophisticated system for growing marijuana was found at property owned by defendant. The county brought a civil forfeiture action against defendant, but it was dismissed for lack of evidence. The state filed criminal charges, including crimes listed as predicate acts from the prior action. Defendant sought a motion to dismiss. The court denied his motion, finding the decision in the civil case was not a final judgment on the merits and the doctrine of collateral estoppel created an injustice. After a mistrial, a second trial resulted in defendant's conviction. He appealed. The court held the double jeopardy argument lacked merit and that all the elements for a collateral estoppel had not been proven. The court agreed that there were compelling public policy considerations supporting the trial court's refusal to apply the doctrine. The issue of vindictiveness failed where Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.100 contemplated both civil and criminal prosecutions. Evidence was sufficient to prove a pattern of criminal profiteering activity and trial testimony was sufficient to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that defendant acquired $ 500,000 by engaging in predicate acts.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. George


NO. 38401-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 263



February 24, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1113.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-8-04470-2. Date filed: 03/07/96. Judge signing: Hon. Norma S. Huggins.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, filed a motion to modify a commissioner's ruling that affirmed the manifest injustice disposition entered by the Superior Court for King County, Washington, on all issues other than her challenge to the continuing constitutional validity of the manifest injustice disposition authorized by the Juvenile Justice Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.010(2).


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered a manifest injustice disposition, which was affirmed by a commissioner. Defendant sought to modify the commissioner's ruling affirming the manifest injustice disposition on all issues other than her challenge to the continuing constitutional validity of the manifest injustice disposition authorized by the Juvenile Justice Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.010(2). The commissioner referred that issue to the court. The court affirmed the manifest injustice disposition, and the motion to modify was denied. Even though defendant argued that the statutory authorization of manifest injustice dispositions had been rendered unconstitutional, the court found the due process protections necessary to the validity of the manifest injustice exception remained. The necessary protections were still in place to prevent the arbitrary or discriminatory application of the manifest injustice exception and to ensure meaningful appellate review.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to modify and affirmed the manifest injustice disposition.

 

1507 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Thurston County Rental Owners Ass'n v. Thurston County


No. 19160-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


85 Wn. App. 171; 931 P.2d 208; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 254



February 21, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1997, Reported at: 132 Wn.2d 1010, 940 P.2d 655, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 490.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant rental owners association challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Lewis County (Washington), which upheld the Thurston County, Wash., Thurston County Ordinance § 10.4 and granted summary judgment to dismiss the association's complaint against respondent county's permit system for on-site septic tank systems.


OVERVIEW: The association claimed that the county lacked the authority to impose the disputed fees and that the ordinance violated various provisions of the state and federal constitutions. The trial court found that the ordinance was constitutional, and on appeal, the court affirmed. The fees were not taxes because the ordinance's purpose was to protect public health, and fees were part of the county's overall plan to regulate the septic systems. The county's use the fee revenues covered the costs to issue the permits and monitor water quality, which did not violate due process. The fees were not excessive and did not violate Rev. Wash. Code § 70.05.060(7), and the county imposed the fees under its general police powers. The ordinance was reasonably related to protecting health and safety of the county's residents and did not authorize warrantless searches for septic tank inspections. Thus, the ordinance was constitutional. All members of each class were treated equally, and the county reasonably distinguished amongst the classes, which were rationally related to the county's goal to gradually implement the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that upheld the ordinance, which imposed a permit system for on-site septic tank systems.

 

1508 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Fray v. Spokane County


No. 15076-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


85 Wn. App. 150; 931 P.2d 918; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 249



February 20, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant deputy challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which entered summary judgment for respondents, a county and a sheriff's department, in the deputy's personal injury action. The deputy had filed the action pursuant to the right to sue provisions of the Law Enforcement Officers' and Fire Fighters' Retirement System Act (LEOFF), codified at Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.281.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Industrial Insurance Act (IIA), Wash. Rev. Code tit. 51, the deputy collected workmen's compensation benefits after he was injured on the job. Thereafter he sued his employer under LEOFF, seeking additional compensation for his injuries. The employer successfully argued that the deputy's receipt of worker's compensation benefits barred the suit and that the deputy's right to sue under LEOFF had been revoked by a statutory amendment, 1992 Wash. Laws. 72. In reversing, the court held that the amendment was unconstitutional and therefore the deputy's right to sue had not been revoked. Wash. Const. art. II, §§ 19, 37 required bills to express their subjects in their titles and prohibited the amendment of laws by mere reference to their titles. The amendment did not meet these requirements because its title indicated that it contained only technical corrections and did not provide sufficient notice as to its true impact, and outside research was necessary to see what laws the amendment related to. 1977 Wash. Laws 294, § 9 returned IIA benefits to LEOFF Plan II members, such as the deputy, but did not make IIA benefits the exclusive remedy for on the job injuries.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment entered for respondents and reinstated the deputy's action.

State v. Johnson


NO. 37472-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 245



February 18, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. LEXIS 439.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1109.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-07630-9. Date filed: 08/09/95. Judge signing: Hon. Richard A. Jones.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence for vehicular assault, imposed by the Superior Court of King County (Washington), claiming that the exceptional sentence he received was not warranted.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to three counts of vehicular assault. All three victims occupied the same vehicle. The trial court imposed an exceptional sentence, and defendant appealed. The court affirmed defendant's sentence, holding that the trial court had properly extended defendant's sentence because the operation of the multiple offense policy of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.400 resulted in a clearly too lenient sentence. The trial court also properly considered the fact that defendant bore extraordinary culpability as an aggravating factor. The court further determined that, although the trial court improperly based defendant's sentence on the permanent, multiple, and life devastating injuries sustained by the victims, resentencing was unnecessary, because the trial court made it clear that it would have imposed the same sentence even without reliance upon the improper factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentence imposed by the trial court.

State v. Paul


No. 35225-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 188



February 10, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied September 2, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Wash. LEXIS 636.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1107.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-01773-6. Date filed: 08/15/94. Judge signing: Hon. John M. Darrah.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed his conviction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment from the Superior Court of King County, Washington, that convicted him stalking a female victim at a shopping center in violation of former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.110.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.110 was unconstitutionally vague due to its use of the term "repeatedly" and the phrase of "knows or reasonably should know." Defendant also claimed that Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.110(1)(c)(ii) was void for vagueness, overbroad, prohibited protected activity, and violated due process and equal protection. Defendant finally claimed there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction. The court determined that the evidence showed that defendant was seen by the victim on two separate occasions, during which time he followed her in his van and watched her as she was shopping, which was sufficient to convict him. The court held that § 9A.46.110(1)(c)(ii) was sufficiently specific to let defendant know what conduct was prohibited and the activities prohibited were not protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The court also held that § 9A.46.110(1)(c)(ii) did not violate due process or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court that convicted defendant of stalking.

State v. Moore


No. 14749-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 163



February 4, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1092.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 93-1-02029-6. Date filed: 02/21/95. Judge signing: Hon. Kathleen O'Connor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which convicted him for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: Before trial, defendant brought a motion to dismiss on the basis that Spokane, Wash., Municipal Code § 10.15.020(C), a drug loitering ordinance, was unconstitutional and his arrest was illegal. Defendant also sought to suppress the rock cocaine that was obtained during a strip search. Both motions were denied. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) § 10.15.020(c) was constitutional because it passed the common intelligence test of the void-for-vagueness doctrine and officer arbitrariness in enforcement was diminished by the fact that that the arresting officers were required to observe overt conduct consistent with the intent to engage in drug-related activity additional to loitering; (2) the arrest was valid because any reasonable officer could have made the arrest based on the observations of defendant's suspicious behavior; (3) the second strip search was legal because it was conducted in a reasonable manner and was based on objectively reasonable suspicion and Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.130(2)(c); and (4) the prosecutor did not commit misconduct because his comment that the officers' testimony was not misleading was an inference from the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver.

State v. Walker


No. 38144-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 155



February 3, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1091.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-8-05492-9. Date filed: 01/31/96. Judge signing: Hon. Michael S. Spearman.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed the disposition order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the disposition order of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which found defendant guilty of obstructing a law enforcement officer in that defendant walked away from police officers, refused to stop, swore at the officers numerous times, and attempted to leave the area.


OVERVIEW: When the police officers attempted to restrain defendant, he struggled, attempted to break away, and continued to swear at the officers. Defendant argued that two police officers unjustifiably tried to effect a Terry stop. The court found that a witness told the officers that defendant had been involved in a fight. The officers observed defendant's bloodied face and muddy clothing. The court found that the officers had a well-founded suspicion that defendant was connected to criminal activity. Consequently, the officers were justified in asking defendant to stop so that they could investigate. Also, although the information cited a revised version of obstructing not yet effective at the time police apprehended defendant, the information notified him of all necessary elements of the correct version of the crime. As a result, the information's defect did not deny him due process of law. The court affirmed the trial court's disposition order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's disposition order.

 

1513 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brokman


No. 17254-2-II, No. 17647-5-II, (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


84 Wn. App. 848; 930 P.2d 354; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 142



January 31, 1997, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought a consolidated review of decisions from the superior court (Washington), which reversed the trial courts' convictions of defendants for driving under the influence because the blood alcohol testing machines were malfunctioning, and they did not give their implied consent to provide additional breath samples for valid tests.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants had received the appropriate implied consent warnings before they provided their initial breath samples. However, when it was discovered that the blood alcohol testing machines were malfunctioning, the police officers took additional breath samples for analysis without renewing the implied consent warnings. The lower court found that the state had exceeded its lawful authority by administering the second tests. Upon review, the court reversed. It found that the purpose of the test was to achieve accurate results. The court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.308 and the administrative protocol permitted multiple breath samples to be taken until a valid test occurred. Further, the court held that under § 46.20.308, a person was deemed to have given consent to a valid, accurate, reliable test or tests and renewed implied consent warnings were not necessary when a disruption of a test was caused by a malfunctioning equipment. The court stated that each defendant's conviction should have been affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's reversal of defendants' convictions for driving under the influence because the blood alcohol testing machines were malfunctioning, and they had not given their implied consent to provide additional breath samples for a valid test. The court remanded the actions for proceedings consistent with its opinion.

 

1514 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Perkins Coie v. Williams


No. 36964-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


84 Wn. App. 733; 929 P.2d 1215; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 135



January 27, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1997, Reported at: 132 Wn.2d 1013, 940 P.2d 654.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, parents of client, appealed the order of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which denied their motion to strike the request of plaintiff law firm that sought trial de novo under Wash. Super. Ct. Mandatory Arbitration R. 7.1(a) and their motion for reconsideration in the law firm's claim against the parents and defendant client for fees earned in the representation of the client in a personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: The law firm represented the client in a personal injury action. When the fees were not paid, the law firm filed suit, and the case was sent for mandatory arbitration. The arbitrator awarded judgment to the law firm against the clients but not against the parents. The law firm sought to request a limited trial de novo under Rule 7.1(a) of only the claim against the parents. The parents filed a motion to strike for failure to include the claim against the daughter. The superior court denied the motion and a motion for reconsideration. The parents appealed. The court reversed and agreed with the parents that Wash. Rev. Code § 7.06.050 barred a request for a trial de novo of less than all the issues and parties to the arbitration proceeding. The language "all issues of law and fact" in § 7.06.050 was plain on its face and prohibited the law firm's attempts to limit the parties and issues. The court declined to base its holding on the policy considerations advanced by the parties because the language of § 7.06.050 clearly permitted no other construction. The court rejected the law firm's construction of § 7.06.050 because it would have rendered part of the statute superfluous.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the superior court that denied the parents' motion to strike the request of the law firm to limit the parties and issues on a trial de novo following an arbitration award of fees against the client but not against her parents. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

1515 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burger


No. 36758-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 122



January 27, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1082.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-8-00108-6. Date filed: 05/10/95. Judge signing: Hon. Mary W. Brucker.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of unlawful possession of a firearm. Defendant contended that former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(e) was unconstitutional as applied to his conduct and on its face because it proscribed mere momentary handling of an unloaded firearm.


OVERVIEW: Police officers removed five occupants from a car after the car turned onto a highway without signaling and a passenger was seen looking back and bending down as if trying to hide something. The officers obtained consent to search. They found a pistol wrapped in defendant's jacket under the right front passenger seat, which he claimed was not his. The State charged defendant with unlawful possession of a firearm. The juvenile court rejected the defense's contention that the evidence showed only momentary handling of the gun. Defendant was convicted and he appealed. The court held that the right to bear arms under Wash. Const. art. I, § 24 was subject to reasonable regulation under the State's police power. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(e) restricted the right to bear arms by making it unlawful for a person under 18 to have a firearm in his or her possession or control. The facts supported the juvenile court's finding that defendant exerted dominion and control beyond that associated with momentary handling. The court found defendant had shown no infirmity in § 9.41.040(1)(e) as applied to his conduct and his facial challenge was not accompanied by a demonstration of standing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the juvenile court that convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a firearm.

Pacific Trucking v. Department of Revenue


No. 20030-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 68



January 17, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. LEXIS 267.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1073.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 91-2-01969-7. Date filed: 02/23/95. Judge signing: Hon. Richard A. Strophy.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which granted respondent revenue department's motion for summary judgment, denied the taxpayer's cross-motion for summary judgment, and dismissed the taxpayer's action challenging the revenue department's assessment of a use tax.


OVERVIEW: The revenue department assessed a use tax on the taxpayer's acquisition of its fleet of trucks. The taxpayer appealed the assessment contending that various use tax exemptions were applicable. An administrative law judge (ALJ) upheld the assessment. The taxpayer appealed the ALJ's determination to the trial court. The trial court granted the revenue department's motion for summary judgment and dismissed the case. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the use tax statute, former Wash. Rev. Code § 82.12.0254, was not unconstitutionally vague and that the revenue department did not exceed its authority in applying the statute or in determining that the trucks did not qualify for an exemption from the use tax. The court ruled that § 82.12.0254 was not the proper subject of a constitutional vagueness challenge because it neither forbade nor required the taxpayer to act. The court declined to sanction the revenue department by treating its responses as admissions because the taxpayer never asked the trial court to determine if the revenue department's responses to the request for admissions were sufficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which had granted summary judgment in favor of the revenue department and dismissed the taxpayer's action challenging the revenue department's assessment of a use tax.

Washington State Council of Fire Fighters v. City of Seattle


NO. 37387-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 47



January 13, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 94 Wn. App. 1069.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-2-08557-3. Date filed: 02/13/95. Judge signing: Hon. Robert S. Lasnik.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, union and fire fighters, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, which dismissed appellants' action to obtain a declaration that they had the right to sue respondent employer for negligently causing work-related injuries.


OVERVIEW: The Law Enforcement Officers' and Fire Fighters' Retirement System (LEOFF) provided benefits to injured workers and gave LEOFF members or their survivors the right to sue governmental employers for any excess of damages over the amount received for injuries resulting from the employers' intentional or negligent acts. Thereafter, the system was reorganized and the right to sue was listed as applicable to both LEOFF I and LEOFF II. The legislature again recodified the provision to limit the right to sue to LEOFF I members only. Appellants then brought suit to obtain a judgment declaring that they had the right to sue their employer for negligently causing work-related injuries. The trial court dismissed the action because no fire fighters were alleged to have been injured and denied the ability to sue. The court affirmed the judgment. It found that the dispute was possible or potential, rather than actual, as neither of the two individual fire fighters suffered any workplace injuries for which they wished to sue their employer and the union did not claim to be representing any such person.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, which dismissed appellants' suit to obtain a judgment declaring that they had the right to sue their employer for negligently causing work-related injuries.

 

1518 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shelley


No. 37830-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


85 Wn. App. 24; 929 P.2d 489; 1997 Wash. App. LEXIS 51



January 13, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration Denied February 14, 1997. Petition for Review Denied October 7, 1997, Reported at: 133 Wn.2d 1010, 946 P.2d 402, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 702.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for assault in the second degree from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), contending that he was entitled to argue that the victim consented to the possibility of injury when he decided to play pickup basketball.


OVERVIEW: During a basketball game, defendant struck another player and broke his jaw in three places. He was convicted after the state successfully argued to the jury that he intentionally punched the other player. While the court agreed that consent may be a defense to assault in athletic competitions, defendant failed to establish a factual basis for that defense in his particular set of circumstances. Further, the court held that the consent defense was not limited to conduct within the rules of the games; rather it was applicable to the conduct and harm that were the reasonably foreseeable hazards of joint participation in an athletic contest. The court found that defendant's conduct was not a reasonably foreseeable hazard. The magnitude and dangerousness of defendant's actions were beyond the limit. He lashed out at the victim with sufficient force to land a substantial blow to the jaw. There was no question that defendant intended to hit the victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1519 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tarnavsky


No. 13506-3-III, No. 14330-9-III (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 805



December 31, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied July 8, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. LEXIS 469. Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1056.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of. Docket No: 92-1-00521-6. Date filed: 08/27/93. Judge signing: Hon. Duane E. Taber.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in two separate cases of cruelty to animals in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.070. As a part of her sentence, the trial court (Washington) ordered a forfeiture of her horses pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.085. Defendant appealed the convictions and the forfeiture. She contended that § 16.52.070 was unconstitutional and that the forfeiture constituted an excessive fine under U.S. Const. amend. VIII.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the forfeiture of her horses violated due process requirements because it contained no provisions for notice and an opportunity to be heard. She also contended that the imposition of criminal penalties in addition to the forfeiture violated double jeopardy protections against multiple punishments, and that the forfeiture statute, § 16.52.085, violated the excessive fines clause of U.S. Const. amend. VIII. In affirming the convictions and the forfeiture, the court held that the statute that authorized the forfeiture of animals seized from a person convicted of cruelty to animals did not violate constitutional guaranties of due process, protections against double jeopardy, and it did not constitute an unjust fine. The court also held that § 16.52.070 was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant because a rational trier of fact, viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, could conclude that defendant cruelly deprived her animals of necessary sustenance or knowingly failed to provide them with proper food.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions for cruelty to animals were affirmed. The court also held that the forfeiture of defendant's horses did not constitute an excessive fine.

 

1520 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


L.H. v. Department of Labor & Indus.


No. 37593-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


86 Wn. App. 512; 928 P.2d 436; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 829



December 23, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Denying Appellant's Motion for Reconsideration June 3, 1997, Reported at: 86 Wn. App. 512, 940 P.2d 657, 1997 Wn. App. LEXIS 926.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants sought review of the judgments of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which affirmed the decisions of the Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals (Washington) denying them benefits under Wash. Rev. Code § 7.68, the crime victims' compensation act (CVCA), after respondent Washington's Department of Labor and Industries denied their claims. The Washington Supreme Court transferred the consolidated appeals.


OVERVIEW: The applicants had been abused as children while residents of states other than Washington. They had repressed their memories of the abuse until after they had become residents of the state. They contended they were eligible for benefits under the CVCA because their injury occurred when they recovered their memories, at a time when they were Washington State residents. The court held that the residency requirement in the CVCA had to be satisfied at the time a criminal perpetrated an act. It also held that the CVCA's meaning was clear when the word "resident" was read in context with the words "act committed." The applicants did not qualify for benefits because they were not residents of Washington State at the time the criminals perpetuated the criminal conduct. The court rejected the applicant's argument that the CVCA's accrual provision, relating to childhood victims who repressed conscious memory, expanded the pool of beneficiaries to include them. It found that the residency requirement in § 7.68.020(2)'s second clause was bona fide and did not unconstitutionally burden interstate travel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the superior court in all three cases.

 

1521 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wallace


NO. 37068-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 836



December 23, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Wash. LEXIS 252.
Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1049.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 95-1-02293-2. Date filed: 07/24/95. Judge signing: Hon. George T. Mattson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree rape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree rape. He challenged the conviction upon the ground that the first-degree rape statute, as provided in Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.040(1)(c), was unconstitutionally vague because it did not defined the "serious physical injury" element. He argued that the undefined term of "serious physical injury" contained no ascertainable standards for adjudication, which left the trial judge and the jury to decide arbitrarily whether defendant was guilty of first-degree rape. The court held that although some discretion was inherent in the task of defining an injury as "serious," the subjective nature of the term did not violate constitutional principles because the need for a subjective evaluation of that term did not invite an inordinate amount of discretion. Finally, the court held that the trial court did not err in refusing to give defendant's proposed jury instruction on the issue of serious physical injury because it did not accurately state the law. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree rape.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of first-degree rape.

 

1522 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


City of Kennewick v. Henricks


No. 15120-4-III, No. 15121-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL ONE


84 Wn. App. 323; 927 P.2d 1143; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 778



December 17, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 6, 1997, Reported at: 131 Wn.2d 1022, 937 P.2d 1102, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 257.


PRIOR HISTORY: District Court County: Benton. Appeal from Superior Court of Benton County. Docket No: 95-2-00271-1. Date filed: 08/03/95. Judge signing: Hon. Philip M. Raekes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of orders of the Benton County Superior Court (Washington), which reinstated defendants' traffic citations given for failing to wear a motorcycle helmet pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 46.37.5301(c).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were cited for failing to wear motorcycle helmets pursuant to a statute that had previously been found as unconstitutionally vague. Defendants argued that the superior court erred in finding that an administrative regulation had cured the constitutional infirmity. Defendants disagreed. However, on review, without determining whether the administrative regulation had cured the constitutional violation, the court affirmed the superior court's order. In reaching its conclusion, the court held defendants' lacked standing to challenge the helmet statute. The court held that, because the challenge did not involve First Amendment issues, the statute was examined under the circumstances to which it was applied. Thus, the court held that, although the statute may have been unconstitutionally vague, it clearly mandated the wearing of helmets of some type. Because defendants wore no helmets they had violated what the court termed the "hard core" of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order reinstating defendants' citations.
