State v. Anthony


No. 35335-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 747



December 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1032.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 94-1-00101-3. Date filed: 09/29/94. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald L. Castleberry.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the trial court is affirmed, but the case is remanded so that the order requiring Anthony to submit to polygraph and plethysmograph tests may be limited to crime-related requirements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, which convicted and sentenced defendant for first-degree child molestation and first-degree rape of a child.


OVERVIEW: Subsequent to being convicted, defendant argued that the trial court did not properly consider all factors prior to admitting the child victim's hearsay statements concerning the sexual abuse. Defendant also argued that conditions imposed upon defendant in sentencing were improper. On review, the court affirmed defendant's convictions. The court held that sufficient indicia of reliability were present to warrant the admission of the child's hearsay statements. The court held that evidence supported a finding that the child was competent at the time she made the statements at issue. The court then held that sufficient evidence corroborated the allegation of sexual abuse such that the hearsay statements could be admitted, without the child's in-court testimony in support of the statements. The court then held that defendant was not deprived of his right to effective assistance of counsel. The court then held that defendant could be required to submit to polygraph and similar tests as part of community placement order. However, the court remanded the case to ensure that the tests were tied to defendant's treatment or monitoring in compliance with the crime-related prohibitions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions but remanded the case for instructions limiting a requirement that defendant take polygraph and related tests to crime-related requirements.

 

1524 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Rogers v. State


No. 13742-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 700



December 3, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format at: 84 Wn. App. 1020.
Later proceeding at Rogers v. State, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 188 (Wash., Apr. 2, 1997)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Walla Walla County. Docket No: 93-2-00616-1. Date filed: 12/21/93. Judge signing: Hon. Yancey Reser.
Rogers v. State (In re Detention of Rogers), 84 Wn. App. 1020, 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 1138 (1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant detainee challenged the decision from the Superior Court of Walla Walla County (Washington), which committed him under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09, Washington's sexually violent predators statute. The detainee claimed that the trial court erred by ruling the state was not required to prove a recent overt act and failing to hold a probable cause hearing within the required 72 hour period.


OVERVIEW: The detainee, a 53-year-old pedophile, was released from prison and rearrested after the state filed a petition for commitment and certification for determination of probable cause. The probable cause hearing was scheduled within 72 hours but was continued because the detainee had been arrested in another county. A jury committed the detainee. On appeal, the detainee claimed that the trial court erred by ruling that the state was not required to prove a recent overt act, the probable cause hearing was not held within 72 hours, the certificate of determination for probable cause had no basis in fact, and the state was allowed to amend its petition during trial. The court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that: (1) the issue of the state's obligation to prove a recent overt act was moot where the trial court ultimately required proof; (2) where the probable cause hearing was delayed because the detainee was not available, procedures were not disregarded; (3) the certificate of determination for probable cause contained detailed facts about the detainee's past convictions for sexual offenses; and (4) the petition could be amended to conform to the evidence at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on a jury verdict committing the detainee under the state's sexually violent predators statute.

 

1525 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dana


No. 34410-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


84 Wn. App. 166; 926 P.2d 344; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 680



November 25, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 93-1-01511-3. Date filed: 03/09/94. Judge signing: Hon. Paul D. Hansen.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) that convicted him of luring a child in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.40.090. Defendant challenged the luring statute as void for vagueness and unconstitutionally overbroad.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of luring a child under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.40.090 after two girls, ages 11 and 12, testified that defendant had invited them into his car and had partially exposed his genitals to them. On appeal, defendant argued that the luring statute was unconstitutional because it was facially void for vagueness and overbroad, that the luring statute constituted an unreasonable exercise of the state's police power, and that there was insufficient evidence to support his conviction. In affirming the trial court's judgment and sentence, the court held that: (1) the statute was not vague where its plain language and the ordinary meaning of the word "lure" gave defendant clear notice of the proscribed prohibited conduct; (2) the luring statute was not unconstitutionally overbroad because it required more than a mere invitation to satisfy the elements of luring; (3) the statute was a legitimate exercise of the legislature's discretion and valid exercise of police power because the state had a legitimate interest in protecting children; and (4) defendant's invitation and exposure of his genitals was sufficient evidence to satisfy the elements beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant for luring a child.

 

1526 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. DeMar


No. 14037-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 624



November 4, 1996, FILED


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kittitas County. Docket No: 94-1-00011-9. Date filed: 03/28/94. Judge signing: Hon. Michael E. Cooper.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Superior Court for Kittitas County (Washington), which convicted defendant of negligent driving, driving with a suspended license, and possession of a controlled substance. Defendant admitted taking controlled medication prescribed to his girlfriend. He appealed only his possession conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a collision with a motorcycle. While he was being booked on suspicion of vehicular assault, defendant said he was taking hydrocodone (a controlled substance) for shoulder pain. A trooper obtained a search warrant and found two bottles, one prescribing an anti-inflammatory (naprosyn) to defendant, and another prescribing hydrocodone to defendant's girlfriend. Defendant contended that the criminal possession statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401, unconstitutionally shifted the burden of disproving an element of the crime to defendant. The court stated that the burden on defendant to prove he had a valid prescription for the hydrocodone was not unconstitutional. Defendant also contended that he should only have had to establish a reasonable doubt as to his guilt. Defendant's constructive possession of his girlfriend's medication was well established. The fact of constructive possession thus established, the burden shifted to defendant to prove lawful possession. The fact that defendant had a prescription for vicodin dated a year earlier did not constitute a preponderance of the evidence. Defendant failed to carry his burden of proving lawful possession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1527 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williamson


No. 19192-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


84 Wn. App. 37; 924 P.2d 960; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 580



October 25, 1996, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for being a minor in possession of a firearm and for obstructing a public servant rendered in the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) on grounds of insufficient evidence and an improper information.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for possession of a handgun, gave a false name to the arresting officer, and repeated it when asked again at the police station. Defendant was charged with being a minor in possession of a firearm and with obstructing a public servant. The information describing the obstruction charge cited to a repealed statute. Defendant was convicted on both counts, and he appealed. On appeal, the court affirmed the possession charge, but reversed the obstruction conviction. The court found that the information charging defendant with obstruction failed to notify him of the accusation with reasonable certainty. The information charged defendant with obstruction by conduct under a repealed statute, but the state proved the offense by showing obstruction by false statements. The court held that defendant's false statements did not constitute "conduct" under the current obstruction statute, and he could not be convicted of an uncharged alternative means of obstruction. Because the information did not provide defendant with notice of the legal elements necessary for a conviction, prejudice was presumed. The court found sufficient evidence to sustain the possession conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction for minor in possession of a handgun, but reversed the conviction for obstructing a public servant without prejudice to the state's right to file new charges and retry defendant for the offense.

 

1528 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Edwards


No. 18325-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


84 Wn. App. 5; 924 P.2d 397; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 551



October 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied April 2, 1997, Reported at: 131 Wn.2d 1016, 936 P.2d 416, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 217.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Skamania County (Washington) for threatening to injure property, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.160, challenging the sufficiency of the evidence, trial court instructions, and the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of threatening to injure property, in violation of § 9.61.160, after evidence was presented to the jury that he was arrested by deputies sent by a dispatcher after defendant called the dispatcher and threatened to burn down a store if its employees called and harassed his family. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the evidence was sufficient to support the conviction. Under the first clause of § 9.61.160, only proof of a threat to injure property, and not proof of intent, was required, and the plain meaning of the word "threat" included future or conditional threats. Nor did the statute require the statement to be a "true" threat. Further, there was no error in the court's refusal to give defendant's proposed instructions that the state must prove a serious and present threat intended to alarm the listener as they were inaccurate, and the instructions given accurately reflected the statute. Finally, § 9.16.160 was not unconstitutionally overbroad and did not unduly limit protected speech. The social value of threats, although protected speech, was diminutive, and the statute was not so broad as to proscribe a substantial amount of protected speech.


OUTCOME: The trial court affirmed defendant's conviction for threatening to injure property.

 

1529 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Eikenberry v. Frodert


No. 18650-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


84 Wn. App. 20; 924 P.2d 933; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 553



October 18, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied April 2, 1997, Reported at: 131 Wn.2d 1017, 936 P.2d 417, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 194.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 91-2-02460-7. Date filed: 11/17/92. Judge signing: Hon. Paula K. Casey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed from a judgment by the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) that convicted the husband of leading organized crime and other related drug charges and awarded plaintiff state a $ 250,000 civil judgment against the husband based on his violation of the Criminal Profiteering Act.


OVERVIEW: The state obtained a $ 250,000 civil judgment against the husband based on the husband's violation of the Criminal Profiteering Act. The husband appealed from the judgment arguing that it violated the double jeopardy clause and the excessive fines clause of the Eighth Amendment. The husband also contended that the Criminal Profiteering Act was unconstitutional because it violated due process. Finally, the husband asserted that he was denied his constitutional right to legal counsel. The court held the civil judgment case did not violate the double jeopardy clause or the Eighth Amendment's excessive fines clause because it was remedial in nature and did not constitute punishment. The court upheld the constitutionality of the Criminal Profiteering Act because it provided sufficient process before seizure, forfeiture or the imposition of a penalty. Finally, the husband was not entitled to representation by legal counsel because the civil suit did not involve a risk of incarceration.


OUTCOME: The judgment that convicted the husband and awarded a civil judgment to the state was affirmed.

 

1530 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Frohs


No. 32498-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 803; 924 P.2d 384; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 540



October 14, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which upon a jury verdict of guilty convicted defendant of unlawful imprisonment and fourth degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful imprisonment and fourth degree assault from an incident wherein he pushed the victim, squeezed her mouth until it bled, and when she attempted to leave, he threatened to shoot her in the head and ordered her to sit in a chair while he watched her. Defendant maintained that the assault merged into the unlawful imprisonment because the assault was contemporaneous in time and place, was merely incidental thereto, and resulted in no greater injury than the unlawful imprisonment. Defendant contended that based on the merger of the two offenses his convictions for both violated the prohibition against double jeopardy. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions of both crimes. The court held that, while the merger doctrine was still in existence, it had no applicability to defendant's case. The court found that neither the unlawful imprisonment and fourth degree assault statutes expressly authorized cumulative punishment for acts committed in the commission of either crime, and that the "same evidence" test was satisfied because the elements of the two crimes were different and the statutes served to deter different types of injuries.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for unlawful imprisonment and fourth degree assault.

 

1531 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Pratt


No. 19925-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 531



October 11, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Docket No: 95-1-00296-2. Date filed: 09/25/95. Judge signing: Hon. Gordon L. Godfrey.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction for moving without registering with the local county sheriff, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.130, by the Superior Court of Grays Harbor, Washington. Section 9A.44.130 required any convicted sex offender to register with the sheriff of the county where the offender resided.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the term "residence" in § 9A.44.130 was void for vagueness. He also argued that the evidence was not sufficient to support the conviction and that a jury instruction defining the term "residence" was erroneous. The court held that: (1) based on the evidence, a rational trier of fact could find that defendant no longer resided in Seattle and had moved to Grays Harbor County where he was looking for work; (2) the term "residence" was easily understood by persons of common intelligence, and it was easily distinguishable from the term "domicile," which connoted residence plus the intent to make the place of residence a fixed and permanent home; (3) § 9A.44.130 was not unconstitutionally vague; and (4) there was little difference between the jury instruction given and that requested by defendant, and there was no error regarding the trial court's instruction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1532 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Friends of Forward Trust v. King County


No. 36596-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 451



September 30, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 93-2-07758-1. Date filed: 04/12/95. Judge signing: Hon. Kathleen J. Learned.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, nonprofit associations and residents, sought review of a decision by the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which granted summary judgment to respondents, King County (county) and King County Rural Library District (library district), on all but one of appellants' claims challenging the county's decision to surplus property to permit construction of a regional branch library building on a certain land.


OVERVIEW: Appellants contended that there were genuine issues of material fact about whether the county complied with its own requirements in declaring the property surplus and whether it adequately described the property. The court found that even if the manager changed her mind about property surplus only under pressure from the council, there was no basis for finding that the county acted in an arbitrary and capricious manner in declaring the property surplus. The trial court properly granted summary judgment to respondents on both issues appellants' raised. Although the current structure of Wash. Rev. Code § 39.33.020 made the statute something less than a model of clarity, given the history of § 39.33.020, the trial court did not err in concluding that the method provided for was alternative or permissive and that, therefore, the county was not required to comply with the provisions set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 39.33. Because the surplus declaration and leasing decision were not actions that a court could have taken, the decisions were not quasi-judicial in nature and the appearance of fairness doctrine did not apply. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to respondents.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment, which granted summary judgment to respondents on all but one of appellants' claims challenging the county's decision to surplus property to permit construction of the library building.

 

1533 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


In re Detention of Aqui


No. 37388-9-I.


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


84 Wn. App. 88; 929 P.2d 436; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 867



September 30, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Reconsideration denied November 14, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his civil commitment as a sexually violent predator. After the Indeterminate Sentence Review Board ordered defendant's release from prison, the state had alleged that defendant was a sexually violent predator and petitioned to commit him under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. The trial court (Washington) declared § 71.09 unconstitutional, the state supreme court upheld it, and remanded.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss because the state failed to provide a probable cause hearing within 72-hours of the state supreme court's mandate. The trial court denied the motion and determined that probable cause was established, except that the state had failed to allege the absence of less restrictive alternatives. The state amended its petition and the trial court again found cause to detain him. The court affirmed defendant's civil commitment. Although the trial court should have held a hearing on the issue of probable cause to detain within 72-hours, reversal for failure to hold a probable cause hearing was not required when a party could not show that such failure affected the ultimate outcome of the trial. Defendant was afforded a full hearing on the issue of commitment, and the absence of the 72-hour hearing did not affect the ultimate outcome of the proceeding. Additionally, the legislature's decision to create this civil commitment process for sexually violent predators did not violate the separation of power doctrine because the decision to release a prisoner from custody resulting from his criminal conduct was also one of legislative creation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's civil commitment as a sexually violent predator.

 

1534 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


In re Det. of Aqui


No. 37388-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 701; 923 P.2d 705; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 450



September 30, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PUBLISHED IN PART



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his civil commitment by a trial court, Washington, as a sexually violent predator under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09. Defendant claimed that because he was not provided a probable cause hearing within 72 hours, the proceeding should have been dismissed and that § 71.09 proceedings violated the separation of power doctrine by encroaching on the Indeterminate Sentence Review Board's (ISRB) power to determine sentences.


OVERVIEW: The ISRB ordered defendant's release from prison. The State petitioned to commit defendant under § 71.09 alleging that he was a sexually violent predator. The trial court declared § 71.09 unconstitutional. Section 71.09 was upheld on appeal. Defendant claimed that because a probable cause hearing was not provided within 72 hours of the remand of the case, the proceedings should have been dismissed. The court affirmed. A person detained under § 71.09 had to be given an opportunity to appear within 72 hours for a determination of whether probable cause existed to believe he was a sexually violent person. The trial court erred in denying the motion to dismiss based on the lack of a 72-hour hearing. However, the State would have been allowed to file a new petition, and reversal was not required when defendant could not show that the failure affected the ultimate outcome. Defendant was afforded an opportunity to appear before the trial court twice prior to trial and could not complain that he was deprived of due process. There was no violation of separation of powers because the decision to release a prisoner from custody and the civil commitment process were both legislatively created.


OUTCOME: The commitment was affirmed.

State v. Munds


No. 13998-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


83 Wn. App. 489; 922 P.2d 215; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 415



September 17, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a convicted child molester, sought review of the judgment from the Superior Court of Pend Oreille County (Washington), which denied his petition to be relived of the duty to register as a sex offender.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a petition to be relieved of the duty to register as a sex offender. The superior court denied his petition. On appeal, defendant contended that he could not lawfully be required to register because the registration requirement was never a part of his original judgment and sentence. The court affirmed the judgment denying defendant's petition. The court held that Plaintiff State's failure to include notification of the sex offender registration requirement in the judgment and sentence was cured by promptly notifying defendant when the oversight was discovered. Defendant's duty to register was triggered at that time. Failure to advise defendant of his duty to register at the time of his guilty plea was not reversible error because registration was only a collateral consequence of the plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court's judgment denying defendant's petition.

State v. Ross


No. 35448-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 390



September 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 94-1-03219-1. Date filed: 10/24/94. Judge signing: Hon. George T. Mattson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his convictions in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) for felony harassment and two counts of assault. He contended that the trial court abused its discretion in admitting certain hearsay statements, that its imposition of a no-contact order infringed upon his right to marry, and that it had no authority to condition the length of the no-contact order on his completion of a treatment program.


OVERVIEW: Police officers responded to a report of domestic violence at the victim's residence. They heard her calls for help. She suddenly ran outside and told the officers that defendant had been choking her and threatened to kill her. She told them the same story a few minutes later, after things had cooled down. At trial she changed her story. Between the trial and sentencing she married defendant. The trial court, as part of its sentence, ordered that defendant have no contact with the victim for ten years, but after learning of the marriage modified the provision to allow contact after defendant completed a treatment program for domestic violence batterers. The court held that the trial court properly admitted the police officers' testimony of what the victim told them as an excited utterance. The no-contact order did not impose an unconstitutional restriction on defendant's right to marry because the state had a compelling interest in preventing future crimes that was furthered by the order. The trial court had the authority under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(9)(c) to issue the order and also to make treatment a precondition for lifting the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court.

State v. Coverson


No. 33022-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 405



September 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 93-1-00527-6. Date filed: 07/02/93. Judge signing: Hon. Leroy McCullough.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, which convicted him of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. Defendant argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.130, authorizing strip searched of arrestees, violated the Fourth Amendment and Wash. Const. art. 1, § 7.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested as a result of a narcotics sting operation. After his arrest he was strip searched and narcotics were found. At a pre-trial hearing, defendant moved to suppress the physical evidence arguing that the police did not have probable cause to arrest him. On appeal, the court held that there was a reasonable basis or suspicion for strip searching defendant. Both the crime for which defendant was arrested, possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver, and his conduct prior to his arrest were sufficient to establish reasonable suspicion that he was carrying or concealing criminal evidence or contraband that would be discovered during a strip search. The police stripped searched defendant because he was seen with a baggie of suspected crack cocaine, but it was not visibly present at the time of his arrest, and the baggie was not found prior to the search. This, in conjunction with the other evidence of defendant's furtive movements in the car and his hand in the waistband of his pants, led police to believe that he had hidden the drugs in a common area that drug dealers use, the crotch or the buttocks.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Postema v. Snohomish County


No. 37389-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 574; 922 P.2d 176; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 356



September 9, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied April 4, 1997, Reported at: 131 Wn.2d 1019, 936 P.2d 417, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 176.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant resident challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), dismissing his action against appellees, county and various cities, that attacked the constitutionality of certain statutes of the Growth Management Act (Act), Wash. Rev. Code §§ 36.70A.210, .340, and actions taken by the county under the Act.


OVERVIEW: The Act required the legislative authority of certain counties to meet with its constituent city representative to establish a collaborative process to establish a countywide planning policy. The resident alleged that the Act created a regional government, violated the principle of one person, one vote, and unconstitutionally altered the police powers of the county and the cities. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of all but one of the resident's claims on standing and justiciability grounds, finding that the case was not ripe because no legal rights had been impacted. As to equal protection, the court reasoned that the Act only required the cities to collaborate with the county before adopting their comprehensive plans. The statute did not alter the county's powers because it did not require the adoption of any specific policy. The statute did not create a new governmental body nor authorize the exercise of governmental powers that would implicate the one vote principle. The court found the Act facially constitutional, the resident's arguments too speculative, and that the Act was not an unconstitutional delegation of the legislature's power to local government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the resident's constitutional attack on the Act.

State v. Baird


No. 35019-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 477; 922 P.2d 157; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 359



September 9, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, Review denied by State v. Baird, 131 Wn.2d 1012, 932 P.2d 1256, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 120 (1997)
Post-conviction relief denied at State v. Baird, 2009 Wash. App. LEXIS 2834 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 16, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction from the Superior Court, Whatcom County (Washington), for first-degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree assault after he beat his wife and surgically disfigured her face. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that exclusion of the illegally-recorded conversation, which was taped in violation of the Privacy Act, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.73.030, did not compromise the defense presented of voluntary intoxication and diminished capacity because defendant's state of mind after listening to the conversation was a collateral issue to those defenses. The court noted that none of defendant's experts testified that hearing the tape was a specific triggering event that would cause a psychological reaction such that defendant would not have the requisite intent for the crime. The court also held that the doctors' expert opinions that the cuts made on the victim's face were deliberate were properly admitted. The court finally held that defendant's sentence was not excessive based on the aggravating circumstance that the victim was particularly vulnerable because she was unconscious when defendant disfigured her face and based on the evidence that demonstrated that defendant acted with deliberate cruelty by his disfigurement of his wife's face.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree assault.

 

1540 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Tellevik v. 6717 100th Street S.W.


No. 18197-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


83 Wn. App. 366; 921 P.2d 1088; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 327



August 29, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 5, 1996. Petition for Review Denied January 7, 1998, Reported at: 133 Wn.2d 1029, 950 P.2d 476, 1998 Wash. LEXIS 47.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) that ordered the forfeiture of his home in respondent Washington State Patrol's forfeiture proceeding alleging that the property was used with the knowledge of the property owner for the manufacturing, compounding, processing, delivering, importing, or exporting of a controlled substance in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.505(a)(8).


OVERVIEW: The property owner argued that the forfeiture constituted double jeopardy within the meaning of the Fifth Amendment and Wash. Const. art. I, § 9, an excessive fine within the meaning of the Eighth Amendment, and a violation of his homestead rights under Wash. Const. art. XIX, § 1 and Wash. Rev. Code § 6.13.070(1). Because the lower court did not determine whether the forfeiture was unconstitutionally excessive, the court reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The court found no double jeopardy violations, explaining that civil forfeiture was remedial for purposes of double jeopardy, except where the clearest proof indicated that an in rem civil forfeiture was so punitive either in purpose or effect as to have been equivalent to a criminal proceeding. The court noted that forfeiture under the knowledge provision of § 6.13.070(1) did constitute punishment within the meaning of the Eighth Amendment and as such it was error for the lower court to have failed to conduct a proportionality analysis. The court concluded that the homestead exemption contained in § 6.13.070(1) was not subject to forfeiture conducted pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.505.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order forfeiting the property owner's home and remanded the case for further proceedings in the Washington State Patrol's civil forfeiture proceeding.

Guard v. Jackson


No. 34877-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 325; 921 P.2d 544; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 311



August 26, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted February 6, 1997, Reported at: 131 Wn.2d 1005, 932 P.2d 644, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 526.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a wrongful death action brought against respondent alleged tortfeasor, appellant deceased's father challenged a decision from the Superior Court of San Juan County (Washington) granting summary judgment for the alleged tortfeasor and respondent deceased's mother and dismissing him as a plaintiff under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.24.010.


OVERVIEW: A wrongful death action was brought against the alleged tortfeasor to recover damages for the deceased's death in a car accident. The deceased's father, who had only made occasional child support payments, was dismissed as a plaintiff under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.24.010, which allowed the father of an "illegitimate child" to recover in a wrongful death action on behalf of such child only if the father had regularly contributed to the child's support. On appeal, the deceased's father contended that he had regularly contributed to the deceased's support, and that § 4.24.010 was unconstitutional. The trial court correctly concluded that the deceased's father did not regularly contribute to the deceased's support within the meaning of § 4.24.010. However, the Equal Rights Amendment to the Washington Constitution absolutely prohibited discrimination on the basis of sex and was not subject to even the narrow exceptions permitted under traditional "strict scrutiny." The support proviso of § 4.24.010 denied equal rights on account of sex, in violation of Washington's Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the alleged tortfeasor and the deceased's mother which resulted in the dismissal of the deceased's father as a plaintiff in this wrongful death action.

Foster v. King County

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 339; 921 P.2d 552; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 320



August 26, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicants sought review of the decision from a Superior Court County: King (Washington), which granted respondent county and county hearing officer's motions for summary judgment and dismissed the applicants' complaint for writ of review of a State Environmental Policy Act (SEPA) threshold determination requiring an environmental impact study in connection with their application for a conditional use permit to create a water-ski pond.


OVERVIEW: The applicants applied for a conditional use permit to create a water-ski pond on their farm. The county issued a determination of significance (DS) under the SEPA and required an environmental impact study pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 41.21C.031. The applicants withdrew their application but began work on the pond. The county issued a stop work order and the applicants submitted a new proposal. The county issued another DS and applicants sought a writ of review. The trial court granted summary judgment to the county. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that a statutory writ of review under Wash. Rev. Code § 7.16 was not available to the applicants because an adequate remedy existed under the SEPA. The court found that the applicants failed to demonstrate that the county acted in an arbitrary or capricious manner and that the statute of limitations on the Wash. Rev. Code § 64.40 claim did not run while the applicants' permit application was pending. The court ruled that because the applicants' proposed use for the pond was not categorically exempt under the Wash. Admin. Code § 197-11-305(1), the county's actions were not contrary to law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court, which granted summary judgment to the county and dismissed the applicants' action.

Schroeder v. Bellevue


No. 36713-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


83 Wn. App. 188; 920 P.2d 1216; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 303



August 19, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), reversing the hearing officer's conclusion that respondent architect's plans did not comply with the city's land use code.


OVERVIEW: The architect prepared plans for a sun room addition to a residence. Under the city land use code, the property required a 25-foot rear-yard setback, but "minor structural elements" including bay windows were permitted to extend into the setback area.. The proposed sunroom was to extend five feet into the setback, but the entire rear wall was windows. A hearing officer for the city affirmed a determination that the proposed addition did not qualify as a "minor structural element." The court affirmed the trial court's reversal, finding that the intruding portion of the sun room met the dictionary definition of "bay window" because it was made of a series of windows, formed a recess in the sunroom, and projected outward from the rear wall of the residence. The city was required to enforce the code as written and could not interpret the provisions on a case-by-case basis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment finding that the architect's plans complied with the city's code requirements.

Kiewit Constr. Group v. Clark County


No. 18667-5-II CONSOLIDATED WITH: No. 18781-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


83 Wn. App. 133; 920 P.2d 1207; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 298



August 16, 1996, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction company sought review of the decision from the Superior Court, Clark County (Washington), which affirmed the decision of respondent Clark County Board of Commissioners (board) that required a supplemental environmental impact statement (EIS) for a conditional use permit (CUP) or alternatively, a conditional use permit subject to a condition that required construction of freeway ramps.


OVERVIEW: The construction company applied to the county for a CUP. The county required an EIS and the county hearings examiner approved the CUP with a number of conditions. Citizens appealed to the board, which ordered a supplemental EIS. Alternatively, the board granted the CUP on the condition that on-and-off ramps were constructed. The trial court affirmed the board's decision and the construction company appealed. The court affirmed and found that the adequacy of an EIS was a legal question and thus could be reviewed de novo by the board. As the county hearing examiner did not review the adequacy of the EIS, the board was not limited to an appellate role in reviewing it. The EIS did not address the specific impact of truck traffic on the bicycle trail. It also did not discuss the feasibility of building direct access ramps. The court found that the directive encompassed the effect of additional truck traffic on bicyclists, pedestrians, and vehicle traffic and the supplemental EIS was justified. The court found that the board did not unilaterally require the construction company to build ramps as a condition of receiving a CUP. This was simply an alternative.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court required a supplemental EIS. Alternatively, the CUP would be granted on the condition that on-and-off ramps were constructed.

Providence Ministries v. City of Gig Harbor


No. 19082-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 619



August 16, 1996, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended on Grant of Reconsideration November 1, 1996, Reported at:
Reported at Providence Ministries v. City of Gig Harbor, 82 Wn. App. 1063, 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 1152 (1996)
Reconsideration granted by, Amended by Providence Ministries v. City of Gig Harbor, 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 623 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 1, 1996)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 94-2-08561-7. Date filed: 01/09/95. Judge signing: Hon. Thomas J. Felnagle.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ministries sought review of the decision from the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which denied its statutory and constitutional writs of review and dismissed its constitutional claims against appellee city with prejudice. The ministries contended that the city's rezoning of its property from commercial to residential constituted a taking without just compensation and a substantive due process violation.


OVERVIEW: The city rezoned the ministries' property from commercial to residential. The ministries filed an action claiming a taking without just compensation and a substantive due process violation. The trial court denied the ministries' petition for writs of review and dismissed its claims with prejudice. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision in part and reversed it in part. The court held that: (1) where the ministries served process upon an administrative assistant rather than upon an appropriate city official, it failed to effect service upon the city and the trial court properly dismissed the action; (2) because the ministries raised a substantive due process claim in conjunction with a civil rights action, its claim was subject to a three-year statute of limitations; (3) where the ministries filed its action well within the three-year statutory period, the trial court erred in dismissing the action with prejudice; and (4) where the ministries' taking claim was filed well within prescriptive period, the trial court erred in ruling the claim was time-barred but properly dismissed the claim for want of ripeness where inverse condemnation proceedings had not occurred.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision insofar as it dismissed all of the ministries' claims, but reversed the trial court's decision insofar as it dismissed the claims with prejudice. The court vacated the judgment and remanded the case for entry of a judgment dismissing all claims without prejudice. The court held the federal takings claim was not ripe and consideration of the claim would have to await state inverse condemnation action.

In re Marriage of Schneider


No. 18842-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


82 Wn. App. 471; 918 P.2d 543; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 248



July 5, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted October 2, 1996, Reported at: 130 Wn.2d 1001, 925 P.2d 988, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 589.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of an order from the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which issued a restraining order upon her divorce from respondent father prohibiting her from moving from the state with the couple's minor child.


OVERVIEW: During a dissolution proceeding, the trial court approved a parenting plan under which the minor child would live a majority of time with her mother. The dissolution decree provided that neither party could remove the residency of the child from a certain area in the state without further court order and a continuing restraining order was issued against both the mother and the father. On appeal of the restraining order by the mother, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court had the discretion to include a residency restriction in the parenting plan upon a finding that it was in the best interests of the child unless the mother showed that the restriction placed an unreasonable burden on her right to travel. The mother failed to demonstrate how the limitation unreasonably burdened her travel rights or why a move would be in the best interests of her child. The trial court's findings in support of the residency restriction were supported by substantial evidence and demonstrated a careful balancing of competing interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the restraining order that prohibited the mother moving from the state with the couple's minor child.

State v. Myers


No. 18797-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


82 Wn. App. 435; 918 P.2d 183; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 238



June 28, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted December 4, 1996, Reported at: 130 Wn.2d 1016, 928 P.2d 413, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 778.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court for Thurston County, Washington, entered on a jury verdict, which convicted defendant of sexual exploitation of a minor, a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.040(1)(b).


OVERVIEW: At a family picnic, defendant videotaped the clothed buttocks and genital regions of adults and children. When he returned home from the picnic, he told his seven-year-old daughter to take a bath and, over her request not to, videotaped her in the bathtub. He used the camera's zoom feature to zoom in on her vagina, and held the camera's focus on that part of her body for extended periods of time. Defendant later edited the video. Defendant contended that he did not take the video for his own sexual stimulation but to anger his girlfriend. Affirming defendant's conviction, the court held that the videotaped picnic scenes related to defendant's motivation. The court found that the trial court did not abuse its discretion by holding the picnic scenes to be more probative than prejudicial because they showed that defendant's intent was to alter his daughter's behavior so that she would exhibit herself for his sexual stimulation, and that the scenes of her vaginal area were a continuation of that prurient purpose. The court held that a reasonable juror could conclude that defendant's purpose in making and editing the videotape was for his own sexual stimulation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Double D. Hop Ranch v. Sanchez


No. 13922-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


82 Wn. App. 390; 918 P.2d 174; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 236



June 27, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected June 27, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant worker, who filed a workers' compensation claim with respondent, the Department of Labor and Industries, sought review of a decision of the Superior Court, Yakima County (Washington), which concluded that, based on his work history, the worker was a seasonal worker within the meaning of Was. Rev. Code § 51.08.178(2) for purposes of computing his monthly wages.


OVERVIEW: Respondent employer hired the worker as a general farm laborer. Although the worker's pattern was to work from March to November, his job could be performed throughout the year. After the worker was injured, the Department awarded him monthly time loss compensation based on the conclusion that he was a seasonal worker. An industrial appeals judge (IAJ) reversed the Department's decision, and the Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals affirmed. However, the trial court reversed the Board's decision. On appeal, the court held that: (1) the worker's employment was exclusively seasonal in nature because he never worked during the months of December, January, and February; (2) substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding that the worker's employment would not have existed during the cold-weather months; (3) the IAJ's denial of the worker's rebuttal testimony did not violate his due process rights because the rebuttal testimony was merely a repeat of his earlier testimony; and (4) the worker's equal protection rights were not violated because it was reasonable for the Department to distinguish between workers with seasonable employment and those who were employed full time.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Lee


No 35012-9-I (Consolidated 1), No. 36767-6-I (Consolidated 2)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


82 Wn. App. 298; 917 P.2d 159; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 213



June 3, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted December 4, 1996, Reported at: 130 Wn.2d 1016, 928 P.2d 415, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 774.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, defendants appealed judgments from Superior Court, King County (Washington), which convicted defendants of stalking in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.110.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with stalking after they repeatedly followed women for whom they had romantic feelings. They contended that the stalking statute was overbroad and vague. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that although the word "follow" was not defined, its plain and ordinary meaning meant to deliberately and repeatedly correlate one's movements or appearances with another person's in order to have contact with the person. The court also determined that the statute was not vague because a reasonable person could look to identifiable sources of law defining when "lawful authority" existed to follow others. The court found no substantial impact on protected First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I, activities because the stalking statute only applied to acts causing fear in the victim; hence, the statute was not overbroad. Although the statute contained an exception for licensed private detectives, the court found no equal protection violation because that distinction was not irrational.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for stalking.

Grabicki v. Dep't of Retirement Sys.


No. 35691-7-I, No. 37822-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


81 Wn. App. 745; 916 P.2d 452; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 186



May 20, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied November 13, 1996, Reported at: 130 Wn.2d 1010, 928 P.2d 412, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 635.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent retiree appealed a judgment from the Thurston County Superior Court (Washington), which affirmed a decision from the Director of the Department of Retirement Systems that education pay was not "basic salary" so it could not be included in his retirement benefits calculation. The Director appealed a judgment from the Snohomish County Superior Court, which reversed the Department's decision in favor of a second retiree.


OVERVIEW: The retirees were police officers entitled to education pay in recognition of their bachelor's degrees. The Department advised the retirees that they were not entitled to benefits for the additional amount that they received as education pay. The Director concluded that education pay was not attached to their positions; therefore, it was not included in the calculation of their final average salary used to compute their retirement benefits. The retirees appealed to two different superior courts. One superior court affirmed and one reversed, and the cases were combined for appeal. On appeal, the court held that education pay was not included in "basic salary." The retirees were entitled to retirement benefits under Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.100, based upon the amounts of their final average salaries. Since Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.030(12)(a) did not explicitly address education pay, it was ambiguous as to whether such pay was "basic" or "special" salary or wages. The court concluded that the Department's interpretation of the statute was correct and education pay was excluded from basic salary for purposes of the retirement calculations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that determined that the Department correctly calculated the retiree's retirement benefits. The court reversed the judgment that ordered the Department to recalculate the second retiree's benefits.

 

1551 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Foss v. Dep't of Corr.


No. 18747-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


82 Wn. App. 355; 918 P.2d 521; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 240



May 17, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 28, 1996. Petition for Review Denied January 7, 1997, Reported at: 130 Wn.2d 1023, 930 P.2d 1230, 1997 Wash. LEXIS 20.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Both parties sought review of a summary judgment from the Superior Court of Clallam County (Washington), which granted plaintiff teachers' complaint against defendant department to gain access to the prison in order to fulfill their teaching contracts with the college. The teachers' positions with the college were dependent on the department's acceptance, and the department denied access because the teachers contested their contract terms.


OVERVIEW: The teachers' contracts with the college to teach in the prison provided that their positions depended upon their acceptance by the department. The teachers contested that provision of their contracts, and as a result the department denied them access to the prison. The teachers brought an action against the department to gain access to the prison so they could fulfill their contracts, and the trial court granted the teachers summary judgment. Both parties sought review. The court reversed the judgment and held that: (1) under the Washington Administrative Procedure Act (APA), Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.030(1)(c), the department's decision was exempt from review because the APA did not apply to persons under the department's jurisdiction; and (2) under the APA, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 34.05.010(3), 530, the teachers lacked standing to contest the department's decision because the APA did not apply to persons under the department's jurisdiction and because the department's decision with regard to "contracting or procurement of services" was not an "agency action."


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment for the teachers in their action against the department to gain access to the prison for teaching purposes and remanded the cause with instructions to the trial court to vacate its judgment and dismiss with prejudice the teachers' petition for review.

State v. Argo


No. 33461-I-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


81 Wn. App. 552; 915 P.2d 1103; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 164



May 6, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court, King County (Washington), which convicted defendant of first-degree theft and securities fraud under the Securities Act of Washington, Wash. Rev. Code § 21.20.005 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was operating a Ponzi scheme. Defendant was convicted of securities fraud under the Securities Act of Washington, Wash. Rev. Code § 21.20.005 et seq. Defendant contended that the trial court erred in concluding that the transaction in which defendant and his victims were engaged involved securities within the meaning of Wash. Rev. Code § 21.20.005(12). Defendant also argued that the transaction occurred more than five years before the filing and prosecution was barred by the statute of limitations. Also, defendant asserted the trial court erred in calculating his offender score and imposed an exceptional sentence of 10 years. The court affirmed the conviction. It held that "securities" was given a broad definition under the statute, and thus, defendant's activities fell within the statutory definition. Additionally, the court determined the statute of limitations was tolled through the application of the lulling doctrine. Finally, the calculation of the error score was a harmless error, and there was also sufficient substantial and compelling reasons to justify the exceptional sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's securities fraud conviction.

 

1553 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Foster


NO. 33808-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


81 Wn. App. 444; 915 P.2d 520; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 142



April 29, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted October 2, 1996, Reported at: 130 Wn.2d 1001, 925 P.2d 989, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 571.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of first degree child molestation. Defendant appealed, arguing that the Superior Court, King County (Washington) violated his right to confront the child witness who testified via one-way, closed-circuit television pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.150.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly molested a six-year-old girl. The trial court allowed the complaining witness to testify via one-way, closed-circuit television pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.150. The court found that the girl was unable to testify in defendant's presence, but was able to tell the truth outside of his presence even if he could hear her, as long as she could not see him. The court held that the trial court correctly applied § 9A.44.150 because the two competency hearings showed that the child could not reasonably communicate at trial and was thus "unavailable" except through one-way, closed-circuit television. The court found that the statute was constitutional on its face and did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VI or Wash. Const. art. I, § 22. The court held that, although the state constitution used the term "face to face," it was not to be taken in its literal sense as long as defendant had fair opportunity to cross-examine the child witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that convicted defendant of first degree child molestation.

 

1554 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nelson


No. 17934-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


81 Wn. App. 249; 914 P.2d 97; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 110



April 12, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review denied September 3, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington), which convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper stopped defendant for driving 81 miles per hour in a 65 mile per hour zone. When defendant was released from receiving her citation, she accelerated, spraying the trooper and his vehicle with gravel. The trooper followed defendant and soon observed that she was again driving 80 miles per hour in a 65 mile per hour zone. The state trooper custodially arrested defendant for negligent driving. Thereafter, he searched defendant's car and found drugs. Defendant moved to suppress, arguing that a custodial arrest for negligent driving was constitutionally unreasonable. The issue on appeal was whether defendant was lawfully arrested. The court affirmed, holding that: (1) pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.31.100, the trooper possessed authority to make a custodial arrest; (2) where the trooper in this case had probable cause to believe defendant had committed negligent driving, he had statutory authority to make a custodial arrest; (3) when defendant resumed her 80 mile per hour speed, she presented a danger to other persons using the public highway; and (4) the State's interest in maintaining the safety of others counterbalanced defendant's liberty interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction of unlawful possession of a controlled substance.

 

1555 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Massey


NO. 36291-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


81 Wn. App. 198; 913 P.2d 424; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 104



April 8, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with delivering cocaine in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(a)(1)(i). He pleaded guilty. Defendant appealed an order of the Superior Court, King County (Washington), which imposed sentence and required defendant to submit to searches by a community correction officer as a condition to community placement. The community placement order did not state that searches must be based on reasonable suspicion.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced defendant to seven months, with credit given for 115 days served, and ordered 12 months of community supervision. Defendant was ordered to refrain from using drugs and to submit to testing and searches of his person, residence, and vehicle to monitor compliance. Defendant challenged the community placement order, arguing that any search had to be based on reasonable cause. On appeal, the court affirmed the sentence, ruling that defendant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the order until he was subjected to a search that he deemed unreasonable. On the merits, the court indicated that the order did not violate Washington law, which recognized an exception to the search warrant requirement to search parolees or probationers. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.195, officers had to have a well-founded suspicion, not probable cause, to conduct such searches. Thus, as a matter of law, the legal standard for adjudicating a challenge to any search under the community placement order was reasonable suspicion. The failure to include language that any search must be based on reasonable suspicion did not affect the order's constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the sentencing order but strongly urged that sentencing courts include the reasonableness standard in community placement orders.

State v. Huddleston


No. 15494-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals May 9, 1996.]

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which found defendant guilty of five counts of first degree assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in a group brawl where five individuals were stabbed. Defendant, who had wielded the knife, was charged with five counts of assault. Defendant argued mistaken identity but did not argue self defense or defense of others. On appeal of the conviction, the court affirmed that the evidence was sufficient to support the findings that defendant used force likely to produce great bodily harm and that he acted with intent to inflict great bodily harm. The court further held that the issue of ineffective assistance of trial counsel could not be decided on the record before the court and that resolution of that issue required the development of a full and complete record.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first degree assault and remanded for retrial or a new trial using the correct definition of the term "great bodily harm."

Ventures Northwest v. State


No. 17893-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


81 Wn. App. 353; 914 P.2d 1180; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 134



March 8, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 19, 1996.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant owners of two separate tracts of land, challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington), which granted summary judgment to respondents, state and county, and dismissed the property owners' claims asserting that governmental regulations resulted in an unconstitutional taking of their property and a violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and that the county taxed their property arbitrarily.


OVERVIEW: A developer entered into an agreement to purchase the property owners' properties for development of a shopping center, contingent upon the issuance of approvals for development. The developer encountered difficulty in obtaining a permit under § 404 of the Federal Water Pollution Control Act, 33 U.S.C.S. § 1344, and abandoned the project before a final decision was made. The owners were unable to overcome the presumption that their fill proposal was the least environmentally damaging alternative. One was compelled to file bankruptcy. On appeal, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to the state and county in the owners' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights action. The burden upon a claimant who asserted that the government had taken his or her property required proof that the enforcement of a regulation proximately caused the loss of all economic viability of the claimant's property. In addition, there must have been a showing that the claimant had exhausted all available remedies or that resort to such remedies would be futile. Both owners failed to make a prima facie showing of causation, loss of economic viability, exhaustion, and futility.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed summary judgment in favor of the state and county.

State v. Blank


No. 17470-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


80 Wn. App. 638; 910 P.2d 545; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 43



February 16, 1996, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied June 4, 1996, Reported at: 129 Wn.2d 1017, 917 P.2d 576, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 342.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court of Pierce County. Superior Court Docket No. 92-1-04836-3. Date Filed in Superior Court: July 29, 1993. Superior Court Judge Signing: J. Arnold.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Acting pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.160 (1995) and Wash. R. App. P. 14, the State filed a bill of costs as the prevailing party in defendant's unsuccessful criminal appeal. Defendant, an indigent, opposed the bill, arguing that Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.160 (1995) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's manslaughter conviction was affirmed on appeal and the State submitted a bill of costs, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.160 (1995) and Wash. R. App. P. 14.2, 14.3. Defendant opposed the bill, challenging the constitutionality of § 10.73.160. The court awarded the State the amount requested. The court rejected defendant's contention that § 10.73.160 violated the constitutional prohibition against ex post facto laws, holding that § 10.73.160 was a valid procedural statute that was entitled to retroactive application. The court noted that the statute neither created any new rights nor divested defendant of any existing rights. The court rejected defendant's argument that § 10.73.160 "chilled" a defendant's right to appeal, noting that recoupment statutes were constitutional even if applied against indigent defendants. The court rejected defendant's contention that the State was precluded from recovering costs because it failed to request them in its brief, as was required by Wash. R. App. P. 18, noting that § 10.73.160(3) directed a party seeking costs to proceed under Wash. R. App. P. tit. 14, which did not require that costs be requested in a party's brief.


OUTCOME: The court awarded the State the amount requested in its bill of costs.

 

1559 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Klump


No. 14258-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


80 Wn. App. 391; 909 P.2d 317; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 24



January 30, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, denying his motion for relief from a consecutive sentence imposed upon a conviction entered on his plea of guilty to conspiracy to commit second-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was subject to a federal prison sentence, the trial court sentenced him to the statutory maximum, to run consecutively to the prior federal sentence. The federal sentence was reversed. On remand, the federal district court, considering the subsequent state conviction, ordered a sentence of the same length as it initially imposed. Defendant moved for relief from the state sentence, more than a year after it was entered. The trial court denied the motion as untimely. On appeal, the court held that the one-year limit provided by Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090 did not apply because it expressly applied only if the judgment and sentence was valid on its face. The sentence was valid when entered; it referred to a federal sentence previously imposed, a necessary predicate under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.400(3). However, when the federal sentence was reversed, there was no previously imposed sentence on which the state sentence could have operated. Thus, the one-year time limit did not apply. The court also held that under Wash. Crim. R. 7.8(b)(5), relief was justified for an extraordinary circumstance. Also, defendant's motion was filed within a reasonable time.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the case for reconsideration of the consecutive sentence, with instruction for the trial court to consider whether a new federal sentence was a previously imposed sentence, subject to consecutive sentencing, and whether the federal court's reliance, in resentencing defendant, on his conviction in the trial court affected the trial court's decision to impose a consecutive sentence.

State v. Becker


No. 35342-0-I, No. 35574-1-I Consolidated Cases


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


80 Wn. App. 364; 908 P.2d 903; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 19



January 16, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Granted June 4, 1996, Reported at: 129 Wn.2d 1013, 917 P.2d 576, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 350.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, convicted by a jury of the Superior Court for King County, Washington, of delivery of cocaine, appealed sentence enhancements under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(f)(1) because the jury found by special verdict that the delivery took place within 1000 feet of a school.


OVERVIEW: The school was a General Equivalency Degree (GED) program located on the third floor of an office building. It did not have a sign, but was listed on the building directory. Defendants challenged the jury instructions. Defendants contended that a school for enhancement purposes had to be a "common school" under Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.230.020 and that common schools were defined by statutes and administrative rules setting out various requirements such as reciting the pledge of allegiance, celebrating Temperance Day, and offering specific courses. The court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.150.010 recognized that public schools included common schools and schools and institutions of learning maintained at public expense with a curriculum below the college or university level. A school did not need to be a common school for purposes of sentence enhancement under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.435(f)(1) and due process did not require drug dealers be informed they were operating in a school zone.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed.

In re Personal Restraint of Paschke


No. 14355-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


80 Wn. App. 439; 909 P.2d 1328; 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 29



January 9, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 8, 1996. As Amended February 8, 1996.
Related proceeding at Paschke v. State (In re Det. of Paschke), 121 Wn. App. 614, 90 P.3d 74, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 982 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner detainee sought relief from personal restraint imposed upon him following the determination by the Superior Court (Washington) that he was a sexually violent predator under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09, Washington's Sexually Violent Predators Act (Act).


OVERVIEW: The detainee, over a period of years, accumulated convictions consisting of abduction, carnal knowledge, rape, and making obscene phone calls. When his sentences expired, and instead of releasing him, the state filed a petition under § 71.09. The trial court found the detainee a sexually violent predator. He was confined to an institution. He challenged the trial court's use of his prior convictions to support its determination. He contended they were invalid for use because he pleaded guilty without knowing the state would later use them to support confinement. He also contended that the conditions of his confinement under § 71.09 violated his constitutional rights. The court denied his petition and held that the state properly relied upon his prior guilty pleas to support his status as a sexual predator. He need not be advised at the time of his plea of the possibility of a habitual criminal proceeding as the possible confinement was a collateral consequence of his plea, not a definite, immediate, or automatic result. Finally, his due process rights were not violated because, in relation to the facilities' procedures, the act was narrowly drawn to further a compelling interest.


OUTCOME: The court denied the detainee's personal restraint petition. The state properly relied upon his prior guilty pleas to support the determination of his status as a sexual predator.
