State v. Pollard


No. 34039-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


80 Wn. App. 60; 906 P.2d 976; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 493



December 11, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied May 8, 1996, Reported at: 129 Wn.2d 1011, 917 P.2d 130, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 274.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Snohomish County (Washington), entered a judgment convicting defendant of malicious harassment in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.080(1)(b). Defendant claimed that there was insufficient evidence to uphold his conviction, or alternatively, that the statute was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made repeated virulent racial remarks to the victim, and threatened and pushed the victim. The State charged defendant with malicious harassment, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.080, fourth degree assault, and second degree criminal trespass. The trial court found defendant guilty of all three offenses. Defendant appealed his conviction for malicious harassment. On appeal, the court held that the evidence of defendant's racial remarks was sufficient to establish that the harassment was based on the victim's race and that the § 9A.36.080 provided adequate notice of what behavior was prohibited to withstand a vagueness challenge. In reaching its decision, the court found that victim pre-selection was not a necessary element of malicious harassment, that there was no need to read a substantial factor requirement into Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.080, and that the State did not have to produce evidence of preplanning in order to prove the crime of malicious harassment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for malicious harassment.

 

1563 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Fondren v. Klickitat County


No. 13660-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


79 Wn. App. 850; 905 P.2d 928; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 469



November 21, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff was first convicted of a fatal shooting, then acquitted after a retrial. He sued the defendant officials for malicious prosecution, false arrest, false imprisonment, civil rights violation, outrage, and defamation. The Superior Court of Klickitat County (Washington) dismissed all of the claims except negligence, which it treated as a claim for negligent investigation. The plaintiff appealed. The defendants cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: A conviction, although later reversed, was conclusive evidence of probable cause, unless that conviction was obtained by fraud, perjury or other corrupt means, or, unless the ground for reversal was absence of probable cause. Because probable cause was a complete defense to claims for malicious prosecution, as well as false arrest and imprisonment, those claims were barred unless the plaintiff could establish the conviction was obtained by fraud, perjury, or other corrupt means. While the complaint did not specifically allege fraud, perjury or other corrupt means, the court found the complaint identified factual scenarios that could establish those facts. The court held that the defendants had not established an insuperable bar to relief, and that the malicious prosecution, false arrest, false imprisonment, civil rights, outrage, and defamation claims should not have been dismissed. The plaintiff's negligent investigation claim should have been dismissed because the claim was not cognizable in Washington.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the malicious prosecution, false arrest, false imprisonment, civil rights, outrage, and defamation claims, and remanded for further proceedings. The court reversed the superior court's refusal to dismiss the negligent investigation claim, holding there was no such cause of action in Washington.

 

1564 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lopez


No. 13307-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL THREE


79 Wn. App. 755; 904 P.2d 1179; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 463



November 14, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision from the Superior Court, Chelan County (Washington), which convicted him of two counts of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver. He alleged that the dual conviction subjected him to double jeopardy, that the trial court erred in refusing to appoint new counsel before trial, and that there was insufficient evidence of intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: On appeal of defendant's convictions, the court held that, to constitute the "same offense" under the double jeopardy clause of the Fifth Amendment, the multiple acts were required to be the same both in law and in fact. The court found that defendant's convictions were for the same offense at law, as they were based on the same statute. The court found that, factually, defendant's possession was a single offense as he possessed cocaine in a continuous, uninterrupted series of events that was the focus of the prosecution against him. In effect, his possession of the cocaine from the undercover agent merged with his possession of the 14 bindles he brought with him. The court held that the trial court erred in failing to make a detailed investigation of defendant's request for new counsel and of his reasons for his disatisfaction. Nonetheless, this error was harmless, as defendant's counsel's performance did not actually violate his Sixth Amendment right to effective assistance of counsel. The large amount of cash after the transaction, coupled with the large amount of cocaine, was sufficient to prove defendant's intent to deliver.


OUTCOME: Having found that the dual convictions violated defendant's right against double jeopardy, the court reversed one of the convictions. The court affirmed the remaining, merged conviction and remanded the conviction for resentencing.

Daniel B. v. Department of Social & Health Servs. (In re C.B.)


No. 13670-1-III, No. 13671-0-III, No. 13672-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


79 Wn. App. 686; 904 P.2d 1171; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 460

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State of Washington Department of Social and Health Services initiated dependency proceedings for appellant father's three children after the father was convicted of killing his wife. The father sought review of the order of the Washington trial court, which terminated the father's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The father strangled his wife during a domestic violence incident and was convicted of first-degree manslaughter. The father's parental rights to his three children were terminated. The father claimed that the expedited termination proceedings under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.190(2), (3) violated his due process rights. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the father received notice of the State's termination proceedings, that the State chose the expedited process under § 13.34.190(2), (3) because the father's murder of the children's mother was an aggravating circumstance, that the father stipulated to the expedited process of § 13.34.190(2), (3), and that the process did not prevent the father from receiving necessary parenting services under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.180(4). The court also held that the father refused to acknowledge responsibility for his actions, that the father had a criminal history of violence, that the expedited proceedings did not deprive the father of his due process rights, and that the trial court's finding that the father's parental deficiencies would not be remedied in the near future was supported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's termination of the father's parental rights.

Danzig v. Danzig


No. 14057-1-III, No. 14118-7-III (consolidated)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


79 Wn. App. 612; 904 P.2d 312; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 450



October 31, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Granting Motion for Reconsideration by a Majority Denied December 4, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 499. Petition for Review Denied May 8, 1996, Reported at: 129 Wn.2d 1011, 917 P.2d 130, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 275.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT SPOKANE COUNTY. Superior Court No: 93-2-05959-5. Date filed in Superior Court: 5/10/94 for NO. 14057-1-III; 6/29/94 for NO. 14118-7-III. Superior Court Judge signing: HAROLD CLARKE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant non-lawyer sought review of an order of the Superior Court Spokane County (Washington), which dismissed his contract claim against respondents, a lawyer, the lawyer's wife, and the lawyer's law firm (collectively respondent), on a Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 12(b)(6) motion. Respondents cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant alleged that respondent approached him with a business proposition: for every client appellant steered into respondent's office, appellant would receive one-third of any fee received. Appellant accepted the offer and directed clients to respondent. However, appellant claimed that respondent breached the agreement and failed to pay him for a referral. The trial court dismissed appellant's complaint but ordered respondent to pay the disputed fee into the court pending an investigation. On appeal, the court reversed the portion of the trial court's order dismissing appellant's claim and remanded. The court also reversed for lack of jurisdiction that portion of the trial court's order compelling respondent to pay the fee into the registry of the trial court. The court held that: 1) the allegations in appellant's complaint stated a claim upon which relief could be granted as the prohibition on referral fees applied only to lawyers; and 2) the trial court did not have jurisdiction over respondent for conduct relating to the case in which the fee was earned because the issue of attorney discipline was not within the issues raised by appellant's complaint.


OUTCOME: The portion of the trial court's order dismissing appellant's claim was reversed and remanded for further proceedings. The portion of the trial court's order compelling respondent to pay the disputed fee into the registry of the trial court was also reversed.

Montesano v. Wells


No. 17853-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


79 Wn. App. 529; 902 P.2d 1266; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 437



October 16, 1995, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court for Grays Harbor County, Washington, for operating a vehicle (a bicycle) while intoxicated, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502, 1987 Wash. Laws 373, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was seen swerving on a bicycle and failed field sobriety and breath tests. A review of the statutory scheme as a whole lead the court to conclude that the legislature did not intend to apply the driving under the influence law, former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502, to bicyclists. Including bicyclists in the crime of driving under the influence, but not in the lesser-included offense of physical control, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.504, would lead to an absurd result. Subsequent amendments of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502 made no mention of applying it to bicycles.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed.

 

1569 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Malyon v. Pierce County


No. 17367-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


79 Wn. App. 452; 903 P.2d 475; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 435



October 10, 1995, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer sought a declaration that the sheriff department's chaplaincy program of defendant county violated the establishment of religion clauses of Wash. Const. art. I, § 11 and U.S. Const. amend. I. The taxpayer also sought an injunction prohibiting the application of public funds or property to the program. The Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) granted the county's motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Under the chaplaincy program, the county sheriff's department contracted with an organization to provide crisis intervention, death notifications, and counseling to employees and citizens. The organization was described as a Christian ministry, and all the volunteer chaplains were pastors of local congregations. Nothing in the contract or any other documents referred to religion or religious services. On appeal, the court held that the chaplaincy program was constitutional under Wash. Const. art. I, § 11 if it served a secular purpose and was religiously neutral; however, disputed factual issues precluded summary judgment. The record was unclear whether the volunteer chaplains limited themselves to determining the spiritual needs of people in crisis and to offering religious guidance only when the person expressed a need. The court also found that it could not tell whether public funds were applied to the support of a religious establishment because the organization was described as a Christian ministry.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings to determine whether the chaplaincy program was being operated consistently with the county's contract.

 

1570 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. McJimpson


No. 31653-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


79 Wn. App. 164; 901 P.2d 354; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 388



September 5, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied June 4, 1996, Reported at: 129 Wn.2d 1013, 917 P.2d 576, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 335.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted defendant of felony murder and felony assault. Defendant argued in part that double jeopardy precluded prosecution on both charges, that one offense was the lesser included of the other, and that he was given multiple punishments for a single offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant brandished a gun at one person, but when the gun discharged it killed another person. Defendant was convicted of felony or aggravated assault as to the first person, and felony murder as to the second person; the aggravated assault being the required underlying felony to support the felony murder charge. On review, the court held that charging multiple offenses or imposing multiple sentences arising from the same actions did not violate double jeopardy because double jeopardy did not preclude prosecution for different crimes. The court held that aggravated assault was not a lesser included offense of felony murder because each required proof of different elements. In addition, separate victims meant separate crimes. For the same reason the trial court was correct to deny giving a lesser included jury instruction. That was especially true as defendant claimed he acted in self-defense, which completely barred any claim of being guilty of a lesser included offense. The court held that because there were different crimes against different victims, the two crimes did not "merge," separate penalties could be imposed, and no jury instruction on merger was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

1571 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Acevedo


No. 17211-9-II, No. 18775-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


78 Wn. App. 886; 899 P.2d 31; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 340



August 2, 1995, Filed


NOTICE:   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied at 128 Wn.2d 1014 (1996).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This was a consolidated appeal and personal restraint petition by defendant following his conviction in the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) of two counts of delivery of cocaine within 1,000 feet of school grounds and one count of delivery of material in lieu of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Omnibus Alcohol and Controlled Substances Act (Act), which provided for 24-month sentence enhancements for drug offenses within 1,000 feet of school grounds, violated the state constitution's single subject rule because the legislature included appropriations within the Act. The court held that the appropriations effectuated the legislative purpose of the Act. Thus, there was rational unity between the appropriations and the Act and no violation of the single subject rule. The court stated that the single subject rule in Wash. Const. art. 2, § 19 provided that no bill shall embrace more than one subject and that shall have been expressed in the title. The court concluded that each provision of the Act, including enhanced penalties for drug offenses committed within 1000 feet of a school, furthered the legislative purpose of counteracting substance abuse problems. While the Act defined rights and appropriated money, it did not run afoul of the "logrolling" prohibition because the Act was not an appropriations bill. The court held that defendant had not sustained his burden and the Act did not violate the state constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence and dismissed the personal restraint petition.

Bass Partnership v. King County


No. 35038-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


79 Wn. App. 276; 902 P.2d 668; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 417



July 31, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish Opinion September 25, 1995, Reported at: 78 Wn. App. 1065, 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 416.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant partnership sought review of an order of the Superior Court King County (Washington), which required the partnership to obtain building permits before placing and occupying portable mini-warehouses on its commercial property in favor of appellee county.


OVERVIEW: The county cited the partnership for construction of mini-warehouses without permits and inspections. The partnership later submitted a building permit application. The county cancelled the application on the ground that the partnership had failed to submit the required documentation. The partnership submitted a second application. The county then informed the partnership that it would not approve the application, unless the partnership agreed to dedicate a 12-foot right of way. The partnership then withdrew its application. The partnership was then sent a notice of a code violation and ordered submit another application or to remove the mini-warehouses. The partnership appealed the notice, which was denied. By writ of certiorari, the partnership appealed to the trial court, which dismissed the writ. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court found that the county did not seek to regulate the manufacture and construction of the mini-warehouses, but rather required a permit for the placement of the warehouses. Thus, the court ruled that Wash. Rev. Code § 43.22.455 did not prohibit the county from issuing the notice and order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring the partnership to obtain building permits prior to placing mini-warehouses on its commercial property.

 

1573 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


In re Treatment of L.G.


No. 16440-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


78 Wn. App. 420; 897 P.2d 1275; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 285



July 5, 1995, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington), upholding the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code § 70.76A.140(1) (amend. 1993), which authorized non-attorneys to file petitions to commit individuals for involuntary treatment of alcoholism. Appellant claimed § 70.76A.140(1) violated Wash. Const. art. 4, § 1 by invading the judicial branch's exclusive purview to regulate the practice of law.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 70.76A.140(1) (amend. 1993), a county-designated chemical dependency specialist (CDCDS) prepared, signed, and filed a petition with the superior court for an order involuntary committing appellant for alcoholism treatment. After the petition was granted, appellant sought review, claiming § 70.76A.140(1) violated Wash. Const. art. 4, § 1 by invading the judicial branch's exclusive purview to regulate the practice of law. In affirming, the court rejected appellant's contention that the legislature had violated the separation of powers doctrine by statutorily authorizing non-attorneys to practice law. In rejecting this contention, the court noted that the judiciary's inherent powers included both the power to enjoin the practice of law, notwithstanding purported legislative authorization, as well as the power to allow it, irrespective of what the statutory language suggested. The court concluded that the judiciary's constitutional role in regulating the practice of law had not been violated by the legislature's limited authorization of a CDCDS to sign a petition for an order of commitment, as provided by Wash. Rev. Code § 70.76A.140(1) (amend. 1993).


OUTCOME: In affirming a judgment upholding the constitutionality of a statute which authorized non-attorneys to file petitions to commit individuals for involuntary treatment of alcoholism, the court held the statute had not invaded the judicial branch's exclusive purview to regulate the practice of law.

 

1574 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Brutsche v. Kent


No. 34390-4-I (Consolidated with 34490-1-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


78 Wn. App. 370; 898 P.2d 319; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 273



June 26, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied at 128 Wn.2d 1003, 907 P.2d 296 (1995).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners challenged a decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found that the landowners declaratory judgment action was time barred and granted summary judgment to respondent city. The landowner's claimed that the amendments to the city's zoning code that created three zones were facially unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city rezoned land in the downtown area to provide three zoning districts. The landowners' land was primarily used for manufacturing, but was located in the commercial enterprise zone. Although the landowners' businesses could continue to operate as legal nonconforming uses, they claimed that the rezoning had a detrimental impact on their business and that of their tenants. The trial court found their action was time barred and the court affirmed, holding that a 30-day limitation period applied and the landowners did not commence the action until 73 days after the ordinances were enacted. It found that the three-year period for claims under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 did not apply, as the pleadings below did not reflect that they sought such relief. Instead, the landowners only relied on the § 1983 limitation period in their opposition to the city's motion to dismiss. The court then used the reasonable-time-by analogy analysis to determine that a 30-day limitation period applied. It found that no other appeal period prescribed by state statute or local ordinance governed the type of land use action involved and that the limitation period for analogous land use decisions was 30 days.


OUTCOME: The court found that a 30-day statute of limitations governed the landowner's land use challenge. Accordingly, it affirmed the trial court's decision, which found that the landowner's suit was time-barred and granted summary judgment to the city.

State v. Bryant


No. 16244-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


78 Wn. App. 805; 901 P.2d 1046; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 397



June 21, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Publishing Opinion September 7, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 395.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Superior Court for Thurston County, Washington, which granted defendant's motion to arrest judgment and for a new trial after defendant was convicted of making a building available for the manufacture of a controlled substance, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.53.010(1).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation of the "building available" statute and with manufacturing marijuana, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(a)(1)(ii). A jury acquitted defendant on the manufacturing charge and could not reach a verdict on the "building available" charge. Accordingly, the trial court ordered a new trial on the latter charge. A jury found defendant guilty on retrial, but the trial court granted a new trial on the ground that the double jeopardy provisions of the Fifth Amendment were violated by the admission of evidence that was introduced at the first trial that tended to show that defendant was involved in or had knowledge of the marijuana growing operation. On appeal, the court held that defendant's double jeopardy rights were not violated because the two charges were not the same offense because they did not satisfy Washington's version of the Blockburger "same elements" test. The court rejected defendant's contention on appeal that the trial court's ruling was actually based on collateral estoppel principles because the court refused to consider an oral ruling by the trial court that was not formally incorporated into the order.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order, reinstated the guilty verdict, and remanded the case for sentencing.

State v. Olsson

The officer also observed the car's exhaust system appeared to have less clearing from the road than was required by Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.680. He stopped defendant for excessive noise and for the equipment violation. Upon being stopped, defendant told the officer he was carrying a knife. He arrested defendant for driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of drugs and for possession of cocaine. The trial court denied defendant's suppression motion, alleging the stop and search were without probable cause. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the record supported a finding the officer had specific facts leading him to stop defendant for noise and equipment violations and to believe defendant was under the influence of drugs. The court stated that he had legitimate safety concerns that prompted his pat-down search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the suppression motion and defendant's conviction.

State v. Whitney


No. 13380-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FOUR


78 Wn. App. 506; 897 P.2d 374; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 310

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington), which convicted defendant for driving while his license was suspended and for failure to remain at the scene of an accident.


OVERVIEW: The court rejected defendant's contention that because the revocation order was mailed to the address shown on his driver's license, not the address on his ticket, he was denied procedural due process. The court held that the Department of Licensing mailed the revocation notice, certified mail, to the address on defendant's driver's license. The court concluded that because defendant had not sent any change of address as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.205, his driver's license address was the address of record. Defendant further contended that evidence of his criminal history was improperly admitted and the trial court erred in denying his motion for a mistrial. The court rejected this contention, holding that the court could not see how the objected-to testimony could have affected the verdict. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that a review of the entire record showed that defendant was afforded a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of defendant for driving while his license was suspended and for failure to remain at the scene of an accident.

Walmer v. Department of Labor


No. 16150-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


78 Wn. App. 162; 896 P.2d 95; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 248



June 13, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied December 6, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, State Department of Labor and Industries, in the employee's claim for benefits under the Industrial Insurance Act. The employee argued that he was not barred from receiving benefits by Wash. Rev. Code § 51.32.160 and that the Act violated his equal protection rights under Wash. Const. art. 1, § 12.


OVERVIEW: The employee injured his back in a work accident, and the Department allowed medical treatment only. The employee's application to reopen the claim for an aggravation of his injury was denied, and reconsideration was denied. The denial was reversed on administrative appeal, but on remand for investigation, reconsideration was denied, and the employee did not appeal. After seven years, the employee filed a petition to waive the limitation in Wash. Rev. Code § 51.32.160 and to reopen the claim, and he was provided with medical and surgical benefits, but further benefits were denied. The petition for review was administratively denied, and the employee's appeal to the superior court was dismissed on the Department's motion for summary judgment. The employee appealed, and the court affirmed. Although § 51.32.160 allowed the employee to claim additional benefits, all other claims for benefits were time-barred. The employee's constitutional challenge failed because § 51.32.160 was fair on its face, and he did not show either unequal treatment or intentional discrimination. The discretion given to the Department's director was proper, and the employee was not treated arbitrarily.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the Department in the employee's challenge of the Department's denial of the employee's claim for additional benefits.

State v. Heiskell


No. 17046-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


77 Wn. App. 943; 895 P.2d 848; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 218



May 23, 1995, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The juvenile challenged a order from the Superior Court of Pierce County, Juvenile Division (Washington), which imposed a sentence that required the juvenile to register as a sex offender under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.130 after the juvenile pleaded guilty to one count of first degree child molestation.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile, who was under 15 years of age when he committed the offense, had pleaded guilty to one count of first degree child molestation. The juvenile court denied the juvenile's motion to waive sex offender registration on the basis of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.140. The juvenile argued that the registration was punitive and inconsistent with the intent of the sex offender statutes, that the State had failed to comply with the notice requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.01.200, and that the registration violated his constitutional right to liberty, travel, and privacy, and inflicted punishment greatly disproportionate to the offense. The court found that the sex offender statute was ambiguous, and adopted a construction that sustained the statute's constitutionality. The court held that a juvenile who committed a sex offense while under age 15 had two remedies: The juvenile could petition for discharge from the registration requirement in the same manner and subject to the same burden of proof as a juvenile who committed a sex offense while age 15 or over, or the juvenile could utilize the less strict burden of proof after waiting 2 years.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order and remanded for the juvenile court to exercise its discretion in determining whether the juvenile was required to register as a sex offender.

State v. Audley


No. 33273-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


77 Wn. App. 897; 894 P.2d 1359; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 221



May 22, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the King County Superior Court (Washington), which found the defendant guilty of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested and charged with possession of cocaine with intent to deliver after officers observed a drug transaction. After his arrest, defendant was placed in a holding cell at the police station and strip searched after giving written consent. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that Wash. Rev. Code § 10.79.130 was not unconstitutional and did not unreasonably intrude into defendant's private affairs. The court found that strip searches were not searches permitted under the exigent circumstances or search incident to arrest exceptions. The court ruled that based on the fact that defendant was arrested for possession of cocaine and was observed removing objects from inside his pants, the officers had reasonable suspicion to perform a strip search and furthermore, the need to prevent the introduction of contraband into the jail outweighed defendant's privacy interests. The court also refused to limit the searches under § 10-79-130(1)(a) only to the time before a person was placed in a holding cell.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine with the intent to deliver.

Keene v. Board of Accountancy


No. 17397-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


77 Wn. App. 849; 894 P.2d 582; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 209



May 18, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied October 4, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former certified public accountant (CPA) challenged the order of the Superior Court, Thurston County (Washington), that affirmed the decision of respondent Washington State Board of Accountancy (board) to revoke his certified public accountant license. The accountant also appealed from the decision of the trial court to uphold the conditions of reinstatement that the board imposed.


OVERVIEW: The accountant accepted a loan from an elderly client for a company that was on the verge of bankruptcy and loaned that money to a formerly bankrupt friend to help the friend's business of raising rabbits. The board found that the accountant was negligent and violated the rules of conduct governing CPAs. The board also ordered the accountant to reimburse his client for the loan, although the bankruptcy court had discharged that debt. The court held that the board exceeded its authority in imposing restitution as a condition of reinstatement because the bankruptcy code prohibited the state from exacting a discharged debt as the price of receiving or retaining a license. The court also held that the revocation of the accountant's license was not taken without due consideration. The court reasoned that the violated rules were not unconstitutionally vague simply because they did not list every possible prohibited behavior. The accountant also violated the fiduciary duty of loyalty conferred upon him by his client's power of attorney. Substantial evidence supported the board's decision, and the remaining sanctions it imposed were neither excessive nor arbitrary and capricious.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court to uphold the condition for reinstatement imposed by the board that required the accountant to reimburse his client for the discharged loan. The court also affirmed the decision of the trial court to uphold the board's revocation of the accountant's CPA license and affirmed the remaining conditions of reinstatement imposed by the board in all other respects.

Keene v. Edie


No. 33105-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


77 Wn. App. 1068; 909 P.2d 1311; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 525

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Order Amending Opinion and Granting Respondent Sharon Keene's Motion to Publish Opinion January 30, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 38. Petition for Review Denied May 8, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Wash. LEXIS 280.
Amended by Keene v. Edie, 1996 Wash. App. LEXIS 38 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 30, 1996)
Review denied by Keene v. Edie, 129 Wn.2d 1012, 917 P.2d 130, 1996 Wash. LEXIS 280 (1996)
Later proceeding at Keene v. Edie, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 610 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 29, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: King. Superior Court Cause No: 91-2-24043-4. Date filed in Superior Court: July 13, 1993. Superior Court Judge Signing: Hon. Charles W. Mertel.



DISPOSITION: The decision of the trial court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which awarded appellee daughter damages for child abuse that she suffered at the hands of her father.


OVERVIEW: The father sexually abused his daughter and she brought an action seeking damages. The trial court entered a judgment in favor of the daughter. The father challenged the judgment claiming multiple assignments of error surrounding the trial court's evidentiary rulings. The court found that the testimony of other alleged victims had been properly admitted. The court reasoned that the testimony was relevant and admissible under Wash. R. Evid. 404(b), to show the atmosphere in the parties' household. Further, the court found that the probative value of the testimony outweighed its prejudicial effect. The court also found that the deposition testimony of a certain witness was properly admitted. The court reasoned that the testimony was admissible under Wash. R. Evid. 804(b)(1) because the witnesses had died prior to trial. The court also found that the trial court had properly admitted the daughter's written recollection summary of the sexual abuse. The court reasoned that the written recollection was admissible under Wash. R. Evid. 801(d)(1)(ii). The evidence was introduced to rebut a claim by the father that the daughter's charge of sexual abuse was the result of hypnosis.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that awarded the daughter damages for child abuse that she suffered at the hands of her father.

Walden v. Seattle


NO. 34684-9-I, 34730-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


77 Wn. App. 784; 892 P.2d 745; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 142



April 3, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the City of Seattle and certain police department officials and officers (cumulatively the city), sought review of the denial by the Superior Court, King County (Washington), of that portion of their motion for summary judgment seeking dismissal of respondent alleged injured parties' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims. The city also filed a motion for discretionary review of the denial of the remainder of their motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The alleged injured parties filed a class action against the city and asserted federal civil rights violations, as well as state tort claims. All of the claims related to the city's use of police dogs against the alleged injured parties, who had been misdemeanor and nonviolent felony suspects. The alleged injured parties claimed that the dog handlers and the dogs used excessive or deadly force. The city contended that it was immune from the alleged injured parties' § 1983 claims under federal law. On appeal, the court granted the alleged injured parties' motion to dismiss the city's appeal from the denial of its motion for summary judgment as to the § 1983 claims. The court held that the city did not have a right to appeal under Wash. R. App. P. 2.2(a). The court further held that the supremacy clause was not violated because the state's discretionary review procedure under Wash. R. App. P. 2.3(b) provided an adequate and nondiscriminatory opportunity for immediate review of an adverse pretrial ruling. However, the court denied discretionary review because the trial court did not commit obvious or probable error in denying the city's motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the city's appeal and denied the city's motion for discretionary review.

State v. Rushing


No. 13587-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


77 Wn. App. 356; 890 P.2d 1077; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 128



March 28, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Superior Court of Douglas County (Washington), which convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated (DWI) in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the filing of DWI charges in Superior Court, instead of in the District Court, deprived him of equal protection because deferred prosecution was available in District Court, but was unavailable in Superior Court. When police stopped defendant, he tried to elude a police car. After he was stopped, blood-alcohol tests revealed he was drunk. In plea negotiations, the prosecutor offered not to file the DWI charge if defendant pleaded guilty to the felony of attempting to elude a police car. Negotiations failed and the State moved to amend its information to include the DWI charge. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in granting the motion. Defendant was found guilty of DWI, but not guilty of the felony charge. The court rejected defendant's contention that he was denied equal protection because he submitted no evidence that others charged with DWI and a related felony were prosecuted for the DWI in District Court. The court held that there was a rational basis for filing the DWI charges in Superior Court. The court also held that the offer to withhold filing the DWI charge in return for a guilty plea on the felony was permissible negotiation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

Marriage of Gillespie


No. 13282-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


77 Wn. App. 342; 890 P.2d 1083; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 131



March 28, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of a judgment of the Yakima Superior Court (Washington) in favor of respondent father in an action seeking a modification of a child support obligation.


OVERVIEW: The mother filed a petition seeking a modification of the father's child support obligation because the parties' son had turned 18 but was still in high school and dependent on the mother for financial support. The trial court denied the petition on the ground that it lacked jurisdiction to modify the obligation order because the child had turned 18 before the petition was filed. On appeal, the court held that the trial court's ruling was correct because the trial court's authority to modify the decree did not continue beyond the child's 18th birthday where there was language in the decree that terminated the support obligation at the child's 18th birthday. That position was supported by Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.170(3) which provided that child support obligations terminated when a child reached the age of majority.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the father in the mother's action seeking to modify the father's child support obligations and held that the trial court lost authority to modify the decree when the parties' child turned 18.

 

1587 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Detention of Aguilar


No. 11371-0-III, No. 11567-4-III, No. 12803-2-III, No. 12802-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


77 Wn. App. 596; 892 P.2d 1091; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 170



March 14, 1995, Decided  
March 14, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish Court's Opinion of March 14, 1995, Reported at: 77 Wn. App. 596, 892 P.2d 1091, 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 170. As Corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment entered by the Superior Court, Walla Walla (Washington), which found him to be a sexually violent predator and committed him to the Special Commitment Center (SCC) until it was safe for him to be at large in a matter brought by the state under Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.030. The offender also filed personal restraint petitions on three previous criminal convictions.


OVERVIEW: The state presented, for a determination of probable cause, an ex parte petition, which alleged that defendant was a sexually violent predator. The court granted the petition without a hearing and entered an order that committed defendant to the SCC. A jury subsequently found that defendant was a sexually violent predator. The trial court entered a judgment, which committed defendant to the SCC until it was safe for him to be at large. He appealed from that judgment. He also filed three personal restraint petitions. The court affirmed defendant's adjudication as a sexually violent predator. The matter was remanded for consideration of less restrictive alternatives to total confinement. Section 71.09.030 was not void for vagueness as long as less restrictive alternatives were considered. Moreover, the failure to provide a hearing on the ex parte petition did not require reversal because it did not affect the outcome of the trial. The court found that expert testimony was properly admitted and that no prejudice resulted from the alleged prosecutorial misconduct. The court dismissed the personal restraint petitions as untimely under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court's judgment that adjudicated defendant a sexually violent predator. The court remanded the matter solely for consideration of less restrictive alternatives to total confinement. Defendant's three personal restraint petitions were dismissed.

Guimont v. Seattle


No. 33624-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


77 Wn. App. 74; 896 P.2d 70; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 72



February 27, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. Order Denying Appellant's Motion for Reconsideration June 9, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 244. Petition for Review Denied November 1, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mobile home park and associated others, sought review of a judgment from the King County Superior Court (Washington), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and dismissed appellants' declaratory judgment action in which they contended a city ordinance regulating mobile home parks to be unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city passed an ordinance that reserved mobile home parks solely for mobile homes, excluding recreational vehicles (RV's), and provided that RV's could not be placed on mobile home lots that became vacant after the effective date of the ordinance and could accommodate mobile homes. The ordinance also required park owners to pay relocation assistance to tenants. Thereafter, the city notified the mobile home park that it was violating the ordinance. Appellants filed suit seeking a declaration that the ordinance effected an unconstitutional taking and violated their right to substantive due process. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment. Appellants sought review. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, holding that a per se violation of the taking clause occurred when the regulation constituted either a total taking or a physical invasion of the property or destroys a fundamental attribute of ownership. The court found that there was not a total taking because the ordinance did not prevent all economically viable use of the park. The court further found that the ordinance did not force park owners to submit to a physical invasion of their land.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that granted the city's summary judgment motion and dismissed appellants' declaratory judgment action that sought to have a city ordinance regulating mobile home parks declared unconstitutional.

 

1589 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Boneclub


No. 30416-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 872; 888 P.2d 759; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 55



February 13, 1995, FILED


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals March 28, 1995.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. Order Granting Motion for Reconsideration in Part, Denying Motion to Supplement Record on Review and Amending Opinion March 28, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 139. Petition for Review Granted on the public trial issue only July 12, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court for Whatcom County, Washington, which convicted him of possession and delivery of a controlled substance. The trial court denied his motion to dismiss the action for violation of the speedy trial rule, Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.3.


OVERVIEW: Police officers purchased cocaine from defendant, and the officers discovered a large amount of cash and a baggie of cocaine in defendant's possession. Defendant argued that the trial court violated his right to a public trial by closing the courtroom during the pre-trial testimony of an undercover officer, that the trial court erred in denying his motion to dismiss, and that the trial court erred in admitting his statements to the police. In affirming defendant's conviction, the court found that under a balancing test, the State's legitimate and compelling interest in protecting the undercover officer's identity outweighed defendant's interest in allowing spectators to be present. The court also found that the continuance, which delayed the trial, was granted for defendant's benefit because his original counsel was injured and defendant needed time to secure new counsel. Having executed one speedy trial waiver, defendant was clearly aware of his rights and failed to reassert his speedy trial right under Rule 3.3(f). Finally, evidence supported the trial court's finding that defendant's statements were freely given and not induced by a promise of leniency.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Buss


NO. 32268-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 780; 887 P.2d 920; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 44



February 6, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court, King County (Washington), which convicted defendant of one count of rape of a child in the first degree under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was the baby-sitter of a three-year old girl and her sister. After the three-year old told her mother that the babysitter "made me put my hand in her butt," the mother reported the babysitter to authorities. Thereafter, the trial court granted defendant's motion to exclude any reference to the sister. However, at defendant's trial, a testifying prosecutor referred to the sister. The court denied defendant's motion for a mistrial and gave a curative instruction. Defendant was convicted of one count of rape of a child in the first degree under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that defendant's statements to a "family minister" were not privileged communications because non-ordained church counselors were not "clergy" for the purposes of Wash. Rev. Code § 5.60.060(3). Further, although the trial court's refusal to allow cross-examination of the victim's father about a possible civil action was error, the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt because the excluded evidence did not affect the weight of the essential testimony. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion by denying defendant's motion for a mistrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision convicting defendant of one count of rape of a child in the first degree.

 

1591 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. White


No. 31245-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 801; 888 P.2d 169; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 45



February 6, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. Order Denying Motion for Reconsideration May 16, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 215. Petition for Review Granted October 4, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which entered a judgment of conviction for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(a)(1)(i). Defendant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence, and he further appealed a sentencing condition ordering him to stay out of identified drug trafficking areas.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed, using binoculars from the top floor of a parking garage, defendant conducting, what appeared to be, a drug transaction on the street below. Defendant contended that the officer had no probable cause to arrest him and that the evidence should have been suppressed because of an unlawful search when the officer looked over the top of the toilet stall. The court held that the motion to suppress was properly denied, finding that: (1) the observations of the first officer established probable cause that defendant committed a crime, and, under the fellow officer rule, the arresting officers had probable cause to arrest; (2) the search was justified under the Fourth Amendment requirement of reasonableness where the police had probable cause to believe defendant had committed a crime, that the suspect was in the stall, and that it was therefore reasonable to search the stall; (3) the evidence was also admissible under the inevitable discovery rule; and (4) the requirement of no contact with drug zones was proper under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120, as part of his post-release community placement, and it was immaterial that defendant had no prior felony drug offenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentence.

 

1592 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alexander


NOS. 31925-6-I, 31945-1-I (Consolidated Cases)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 830; 888 P.2d 175; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 48



February 6, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review on behalf of Pamela Potter and the Petition for Review on behalf of Richard Alexander Denied July 13, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendants sought review of the decisions of the King County Superior Court (Washington), which affirmed defendants' convictions for telephone harassment pursuant to Seattle, Wash., Municipal Code 12A.06.100 and Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230.


OVERVIEW: Defendant made 680 "hang up" phone calls to a crisis center over a four-day period and was convicted of telephone harassment under Seattle, Wash., Municipal Code 12A.06.100. Another defendant called his girlfriend up to 15 times a day over a period of months and was convicted of telephone harassment under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230. The superior court affirmed defendants' convictions. On consolidated appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that telephone harassment laws distinguished between harassing calls and other communication. Thus, the term "embarrass," as included in the harassment laws, was not unconstitutionally overbroad in light of the privacy concerns invoked by non-public telephone communications and the laws' emphasis on conduct instead of speech. Further, the terms "anonymously" and "repeatedly" as used in the telephone harassment laws provided adequate notice to persons of common intelligence as to what behavior was prohibited and as to the specific intent required. The laws also provided sufficient guidelines to prevent arbitrary enforcement. Thus, Seattle, Wash., Municipal Code 12A.06.100 and Wash. Rev. Code § 9.61.230 were not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions for telephone harassment.

 

1593 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Watkins


No. 33637-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 726; 887 P.2d 492; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 34



January 23, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of weapons possession pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040. Defendant argued that evidence obtained from a Terry stop should have been suppressed and that the law under which he was convicted was an ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW: Two police officers motioned a car with a mangled license plate to the side of the street, saw a man sitting in the passenger seat and leaning as if to place something under the seat, and asked the man to exit the car. One officer opened the car door and saw the butt of a revolver. The man was convicted of violating Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040, which prohibited possession of a firearm by a juvenile who had been convicted of a felony violation of the Uniform Controlled Substances Act. Defendant challenged the seizure and argued that his motion to suppress the fruits of the search should have been sustained. The court noted that brief detention during a Terry stop might constitute a seizure but did not amount to an arrest. The officers were entitled to ask defendant to exit the car. The search for weapons was justified by defendant's suspicious movements, which presented possible danger to the officers. Nor was defendant's ex post facto argument tenable: the statute created an entirely new offense, not an enhancement of an old one. The court affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court held that the superior court did not err when it denied defendant's motion to suppress the evidence obtained during his detention. The court also held that the statute under which defendant was convicted was not an ex post facto law. The court affirmed defendant's conviction for firearms possession.

 

1594 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Luxembourg Group v. Snohomish County


NO. 33263-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 502; 887 P.2d 446; 1995 Wash. App. LEXIS 2



January 9, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied July 13, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee county denied appellant applicant's subdivision application. The Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) granted summary judgment in favor of the county, upholding the denial of the subdivision application. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The applicant filed an application for a subdivision on certain property. The county required the applicant to dedicate a stub road access to a landlocked neighboring property as a condition for approval of the application. The applicant argued that the condition amounted to a taking of property without compensation. The court agreed with the applicant. The neighboring property had always been isolated from the county roads, thus its need for access was not a result of the proposed subdivision. Since the dedication requirement would not remedy any problem caused by the applicant's proposed subdivision, requiring the applicant to dedicate property for a stub road extension amounted to an unconstitutional taking. The court specifically held that the county could not condition approval of the subdivision on the dedication of property unless a need for the dedication arose from the development under review. Accordingly, the order denying the applicant's motion for summary judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The order denying the applicant's motion for summary judgment was reversed and the trial court was directed to enter an order granting the applicant's motion for summary judgment.

 

1595 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Torrey v. Tukwila


No. 33670-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


76 Wn. App. 32; 882 P.2d 799; 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 428



September 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Publication October 21, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 427. As Corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dancers sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which granted a motion for summary judgment in a conspiracy action brought under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985, 1986, 1988, for damages and attorney fees, in favor of appellees, city and sergeant.


OVERVIEW: The dancers were arrested during a raid for violating Tukwila, Wash., Municipal Code ch. 5.56.070. Prior to the raids, it was determined that full custodial arrests were to be effectuated. The dancers brought a conspiracy action under 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985, 1986, 1988, for damages and attorney fees against the city and the police sergeant. Before trial, the dancers stipulated that probable cause exited for their arrests. The trial court denied the dancers' summary judgment motion and granted the summary judgment motion of the city and the sergeant. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court because the dancers' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985(3) claim failed to identify the protected class of which they were members. Further, the dancers' Wash. Rev. Code § 10.31.100 claim did not survive because it was not based on a federal constitutional violation. Moreover, Wash. Ct. Ltd. Juris. Crim. R. 2.1(b)(2) exceeded federal protection and could not serve as the basis for a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim. Finally, because full custodial arrest was an option and no dancer was held more than 48 hours before a probable cause hearing, there was no violation of federal law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the lower court that granted a motion for summary judgment in an action brought under the civil rights statutes for damages and attorney fees, in favor of the city and the sergeant.

 

1596 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Arseneau


No. 30213-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


75 Wn. App. 747; 879 P.2d 1003; 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 399



September 12, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied March 14, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Wash. LEXIS 137.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court for Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted defendant of four counts of first degree incest.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted by information for incest with his stepdaughter, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.64.020. The information did not allege the age of the stepdaughter and also did not use the statutory term "descendent" to describe the stepdaughter. Defendant entered a plea of guilty and was convicted of four counts of incest. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the information was not deficient for failure to allege that the stepdaughter was under the age of 18 at the time of the offenses. The court determined that while the age of the stepdaughter was capable of providing a complete defense to a charge of incest as it related to a stepchild, the age was not a necessary statutory element required to have been set forth in the indictment. The court further held that the use of the word "stepdaughter" in place of "descendent" was a proper one because the definition of descendent under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.64.020(3) included stepchildren specifically. The court concluded that the information adequately informed defendant with reasonable certainty of the nature of the accusation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

1597 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


State v. Myles


No. 32229-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


75 Wn. App. 643; 879 P.2d 968; 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 389



September 6, 1994, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile challenged an order from the Superior Court for King County (Washington), which convicted the juvenile of carrying a dangerous weapon pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code Ann. § 9.41.250 and sentenced her to two months of community supervision and eight hours of community service. The juvenile challenged the constitutionality of § 9.41.250 as being vague as applied to her where she only had a three-inch paring knife in her jacket.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted a juvenile of carrying a dangerous weapon in violation of Wash. Rev. Code Ann. § 9.41.250 and sentenced her to two months of community supervision and eight hours of community service. The juvenile challenged the constitutionality of § 9.41.250 as being vague as applied to her where she only carried a three inch paring knife. The court reversed and dismissed the charges against her. The court held that § 9.41.250 could be construed as requiring evidence of identifiable conduct by the defendant that proved beyond a reasonable doubt that she intended to conceal a dangerous weapon. Merely carrying an item did not usually involve identifiable conduct. It was not an overt movement. The court reasoned that the drafters of § 9.41.250 must have had in mind a movement to conceal a weapon, done furtively, in a way meant to escape notice. Otherwise, the court concluded, there were all too many easily imagined instances of innocent conduct involving the carrying of pocket knives, kitchen knives, letter openers, pepper sprays, scissors, common tools, and other dangerous objects with intent to conceal them in, for example, a pocket, handbag, shopping bag, or boot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's conviction of the juvenile for carrying a dangerous weapon.

State v. Chapin


No. 31031-3-I (Consolidated with 31266-9-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


75 Wn. App. 460; 879 P.2d 300; 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 369



August 22, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended. Order Amending Opinion November 4, 1994, Repored at: 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 452. Petition for Review Denied February 9, 1995, Reported at: 125 Wn.2d 1024, 1995 Wash. LEXIS 78.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 89-1-00102-5 & 87-1-01214-4. Date filed in Superior Court: June 8, 1992 and July 22, 1992. Superior Court Judge Signing: John Wilson


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted defendant of one count each of possession of cocaine and possession of cocaine with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged that the traffic stop that resulted in his arrest on outstanding warrants and the discovery of the cocaine that was the basis of the possession charge was pretextual. The court found that the trial court did not err in refusing to suppress the evidence obtained from the traffic stop because the traffic stop for a license plate violation was not pretextual. Although the police officer was suspicious of the vehicle in which defendant was riding when he saw it emerge from behind an abandoned gas station, the license infraction gave him authority, independent of his suspicions, to stop the vehicle. Furthermore, upon observing that defendant was not wearing his seatbelt, the officer then had authority to request defendants identification. Finally, the stop was not pretextual because under the same circumstances a reasonable officer would have made the stop. The court also found, with respect to the intent to distribute charge, that the trial court did not err in instructing the jury that defendant had to prove entrapment by a preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of cocaine and possession of cocaine with intent to distribute.

Washington Indep. Tel. Assn. v. Telecommunications Ratepayers Assn. for Cost-Based & Equitable Rates


No. 16170-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


75 Wn. App. 356; 880 P.2d 50; 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 351



August 10, 1994, Filed


NOTICE:

[As amended by order of the Court of Appeals September 7, 1994.]


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Order Amending Opinion September 7, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 396.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Washington Independent Telephone Association (Commission), sought review of a judgment of the Thurston County Superior Court (Washington) in a declaratory judgment action filed by appellee, an association of telecommunications consumers, which invalidated Wash. Admin. Code § 480-120-425, a rule the Commission promulgated that created a fund that was to be funded by assessment of charges on certain telecommunication services.


OVERVIEW: The Commission adopted as part of rules that governed expanded local toll-free area telephone services a community calling fund that was to be funded by a charge levied on local exchange carriers (LEC) based on the number of exchange access lines each carrier controlled within the state. Under a formula in the rule, smaller LECs that experienced revenue shortfalls were eligible for support from the fund. The Commission filed a petition for declaratory judgment that sought a declaration that the rule was constitutional and within its authority. Appellee, an association of LECs, and the largest LEC were permitted by stipulation to intervene as parties. The association filed a cross-petition that sought a declaration that the rule was invalid because the fund exceeded the Commission's authority. The superior court found that the rule was invalid because the Commission had no statutory authority for its enactment. The court held that the state's public service laws did not authorize the imposition of a charge on all access lines as a funding mechanism for the fund.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the superior court.

 

1600 of 2268 DOCUMENTS


Campos v. Labor & Indus.


No. 16305-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


75 Wn. App. 379; 880 P.2d 543; 1994 Wash. App. LEXIS 352



August 10, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Review Denied March 10, 1995.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged the judgment of the Superior Court, Pierce County (Washington) entering summary judgment in favor of respondent, Department of Labor and Industries of the State of Washington (department), in the claimant's action challenging the department's denial of his request to reopen his claim for worker's compensation benefits under Wash. Rev. Code § 51.32.160.


OVERVIEW: The claimant injured his elbow in the course of his employment. The department accepted a claim for worker's compensation benefits. The department reopened the claim several times because the claimant alleged that his condition was aggravated. When the claimant applied to reopen his claim another time, the department denied his request because the application was not timely filed within the limitations period in § 51.32.160. The claimant appealed to an administrative board, but the board upheld the decision. The claimant filed an action against the department seeking judicial review. The trial court granted summary judgment for the department, finding that § 51.32.160 was constitutional. The claimant appealed. The court affirmed, holding that § 51.32.160 did not violate the claimant's equal protection rights. The court reasoned that there was a rational basis for determining whether claimants were subject to the limitations period in § 51.32.160 based on whether they had a medical evaluation for their injury. The classification was rationally related to the interest in finalizing claims. The court also held that § 51.32.160 did not violate due process guarantees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision entering summary judgment for the department in the claimant's action challenging the department's denial of his request to reopen his claim for worker's compensation benefits.
